Life of Imam al-Maturidi
beginner
5 min
Imam al-Maturidi: His Identity and Significance
Biographical account of Imam al-Maturidi with titles and historical role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identity, titles, and historical role of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi in defending Sunni theology, as well as the scholarly neglect he faced.

Core Idea
Imam al-Maturidi was a chief defender of Sunni creed, yet history often forgot him.

This passage introduces us to the author of the book we are studying — Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. We learn his full name, his place of origin, and the many honorific titles his followers gave him. The passage also places him alongside Imam al-Ash'ari as a twin defender of the Sunnah, and then notes a surprising historical neglect that contrasts with his immense influence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imam's name and origin
Read the first sentence and note the components of his name and the meaning of 'al-Maturidi' as a relative attribution to a locality in Samarqand.
2
Explore his honorific titles
List the five titles given (Imam of guidance, Banner of guidance, Imam of theologians, Corrector of creeds, Chief of Ahl al-Sunna) and consider what each says about his role.
These titles reflect his high status and the respect of his followers.
3
Compare his role with al-Ash'ari
Notice the geographical division: al-Maturidi in the East, al-Ash'ari in the central regions, both confronting extremist ideas.
This shows their complementary efforts in defending Sunnah.
4
Reflect on the historical neglect
Understand why the passage finds it surprising that historians barely mention al-Maturidi despite his stature and role.
The neglect contrasts with his importance and the school that emerged from him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مؤلف الكتاب هو الإمام أبو منصور محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي السمرقندي الأنصاري. فـ «الماتريدي» نسبة إلى «ماتريد» ، وهي محلة بسمرقند، في جمهورية أوزبكستان. وقد لقبه أصحابه بألقاب مختلفة ؛ فهو إمام الهدى ، و علم الهدى»، وهو «إمام المتكلمين»، وهو «مصحح عقائد المسلمين»، وهو رئيس أهل السنة . فهذه الأوصاف والألقاب تومئ إلى ما للرجل من مكانة في نفوس أصحابه، وإلى دور بارز تحقق له في نصرة السُّنة والدفاع عنها، حيث نهض الماتريدي في الأقاليم الشرقية من العالم الإسلامي، ونهض أبو الحسن الأشعري في الأقاليم المتوسطة لمجابهة ذوي الأفكار المتطرفة. وعلى الرغم من هذه المكانة التي نالها الإمام الماتريدي يلاحظ أنه قد أُهمل من كثير من المؤرخين، فلم يشيروا إليه من قريب ولا من بعيد ؛ وإن ذكره مؤرخ فهي كلمات مقتضبة لا تناسب مكانته، ولا مكانة المذهب المنبثق عنه، ولا الدور الذي قام به هو والأشعري في مواجهة المعتزلة والروافض وغيرهما من الفرق .
The author of the book is Imam Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi al-Samarqandi al-Ansari. 'Al-Maturidi' is a relative attribution to 'Maturid', which is a locality in Samarqand, in the Republic of Uzbekistan. His followers gave him various titles: he is the Imam of guidance, the Banner of guidance, the Imam of the theologians (mutakallimun), the Corrector of the creeds of the Muslims, and the Chief of the People of the Sunnah. These descriptions and titles indicate the man's status in the hearts of his followers, and a prominent role achieved for him in supporting and defending the Sunnah, as al-Maturidi rose in the eastern regions of the Islamic world, and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari rose in the central regions to confront those with extremist ideas. Despite this status that Imam al-Maturidi attained, it is observed that he was neglected by many historians, who did not mention him at all; if a historian mentions him, it is with brief words that do not befit his status, nor the status of the school that emerged from him, nor the role that he and al-Ash'ari played in confronting the Mu'tazila, the Rawafid, and other sects.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to al-Maturidi. It first gives his full name and lineage, explaining the nisba 'Maturidi' from a place in Samarqand. Then it lists several honorific titles his followers gave him, emphasizing his leadership in guidance, theology, and creedal correction. These titles indicate his high status. The passage then compares his regional role to that of al-Ash'ari: al-Maturidi operated in the East, al-Ash'ari in the central lands, both defending Sunnah against extremists. Finally, it notes a historical neglect: despite his importance, many historians barely mention him. This neglect is contrasted with the significant role he played alongside al-Ash'ari against the Mu'tazila, Rawafid, and other sects.

أبو الحسن الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Maturidi was a minor figure in Islamic theology.
Correction: The passage shows he was given lofty titles like 'Imam of guidance' and 'Chief of Ahl al-Sunna', and his role is compared to that of al-Ash'ari, indicating his major significance.

Checkpoint
What are the two regions where al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari respectively rose to defend the Sunnah?
A) Both in the East
B) Maturidi in the East, Ash'ari in the central regions
C) Maturidi in the West, Ash'ari in the East
D) Both in the central regions

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Maturidi, though a towering figure in Sunni theology, suffered from scholarly neglect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The scholars who preserve our faith often go unrecognized. Which silent defender of truth in your own life have you failed to appreciate or thank properly? Can you name one person today and take a step to honor them?
?
Imam al-Maturidi was neglected by historians despite his immense contribution. Are you neglecting the study of those who shaped your creed? Would you be able to identify even one book of al-Maturidi to study? If not, what is stopping you from beginning?
?
You have just read that al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari confronted extremist ideas in their time. Who is confronting the ideological distortions of today? Is it enough to just follow your inherited madhhab without knowing its foundations from scholars like al-Maturidi? Will you resolve read one page of a Maturidi text this week?

Imam Maturidi: Name, Origin, and Titles
Introduces Imam Maturidi's name, nisba, and honorific titles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biographical background of Imam Maturidi, including his full name, his geographical origin, and the honorific titles his companions gave him.

Core Idea
Imam Maturidi's titles reflect his central role in defending Sunni theology.

Before studying the theological content of Kitab al-Tawhid, it is important to know who its author is. Imam al-Maturidi is a towering figure in Sunni Islam, and his name and titles carry deep meaning. This passage introduces his lineage, his hometown, and the honorifics that his followers bestowed upon him.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the passage carefully, noting the full name and the explanation of 'al-Maturidi' as a nisba.
Pay attention to the place name Maturid.
2
Identify the titles
The passage lists five titles. List them and think about what each one signifies about Imam Maturidi's role.
These titles are given by his companions, indicating his stature.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why his companions gave him these titles. What do they tell us about his contribution to Sunni Islam?
The passage says they indicate his status and his role in defending the Sunna.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مؤلف الكتاب هو الإمام أبو منصور محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي السمرقندي الأنصاري. فـ «الماتريدي» نسبة إلى «ماتريد» ، وهي محلة بسمرقند، في جمهورية أوزبكستان. وقد لقبه أصحابه بألقاب مختلفة ؛ فهو إمام الهدى ، و علم الهدى»، وهو «إمام المتكلمين»، وهو «مصحح عقائد المسلمين»، وهو رئيس أهل السنة . فهذه الأوصاف والألقاب تومئ إلى ما للرجل من مكانة في نفوس أصحابه، وإلى دور بارز تحقق له في نصرة السُّنة والدفاع عنها.
The author of the book is the Imām Abū Manṣūr Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad ibn Maḥmūd al-Māturīdī al-Samarqandī al-Anṣārī. 'Al-Māturīdī' is a relative attribution to 'Māturīd', which is a district in Samarkand, in the Republic of Uzbekistan. His companions bestowed upon him various titles: he is 'Imām al-Hudā' (Imam of Guidance), 'ʿAlam al-Hudā' (Banner of Guidance), 'Imām al-Mutakallimīn' (Imam of the Theologians), 'Muṣaḥḥiḥ ʿAqāʾid al-Muslimīn' (Corrector of the Beliefs of Muslims), and 'Raʾīs Ahl al-Sunna' (Chief of the People of the Sunna). These descriptions and titles indicate the man's status in the hearts of his companions and the prominent role he achieved in supporting and defending the Sunna.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction. It begins by stating the author's full name: Abū Manṣūr Muḥammad ibn Muḥammad ibn Maḥmūd al-Māturīdī al-Samarqandī al-Anṣārī. It explains that the nisba 'al-Māturīdī' refers to Māturīd, a district in Samarkand (present-day Uzbekistan). Then it lists the honorific titles given to him by his followers: Imām al-Hudā (Imam of Guidance), ʿAlam al-Hudā (Banner of Guidance), Imām al-Mutakallimīn (Imam of the Theologians), Muṣaḥḥiḥ ʿAqāʾid al-Muslimīn (Corrector of the Beliefs of Muslims), and Raʾīs Ahl al-Sunna (Chief of the People of the Sunna). The passage concludes that these titles indicate his high status and his prominent role in supporting and defending the Sunna.

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi's full name, Central Asian origin, and honorific titles highlight his foundational role in Sunni theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The companions gave Imam Maturidi the title 'Corrector of the Beliefs of Muslims'. In what specific areas of your own belief do you feel most in need of correction? What one step will you take this week to seek clarity from the Quran and Sunnah on that issue?
?
Imam Maturidi was from a distant land in Central Asia, yet his legacy reached you centuries later. What are you doing right now—in your environment, however small—to actively defend the Sunna and leave a legacy of guidance for others?
?
Among his titles is 'Imam of Guidance'. Who is one person in your life that you are neglecting to guide or encourage toward good? What is the first thing you can say or do to fulfill that responsibility, starting today?

Maturidi's Role Alongside Ash'ari and Historical Neglect
Describes Maturidi's role with Ash'ari and the neglect he suffered from historians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's parallel role with Ash'ari in confronting extremists and the historical neglect that has obscured his contributions.

Core Idea
Maturidi and Ash'ari were two pillars of Sunni theology, yet history neglected one of them.

This passage introduces us to the geographical and theological context of Imām al-Māturīdī, comparing his role to that of Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī. It then turns to a puzzling fact: despite his immense influence, many historians have overlooked him, and even when mentioned, it is inadequately. The passage also highlights the balanced approach to reason and revelation that both scholars championed, and gives examples of modern scholars noting the neglect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get the full sense of the historical account.
Notice the contrast between the two regions and the common enemies mentioned.
2
Identify the parallel roles
Find where the text describes Maturidi and Ash'ari working in different regions to confront extremist ideas. Note the enemies they faced (Mu'tazila, Rawafid).
This sets the stage for understanding their importance.
3
Observe the neglect and its manifestation
Look for how the author says Maturidi was neglected by historians and the specific example of Carl Brockelmann's omission.
The neglect is not accidental; it's systematic.
4
Reflect on the balanced methodology
Notice the statement about elevating reason alongside revelation, representing Islamic moderation. This is the core theological contribution.
Maturidi's approach is a model for balancing rational and scriptural sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حيث نهض الماتريدي في الأقاليم الشرقية من العالم الإسلامي، ونهض أبو الحسن الأشعري في الأقاليم المتوسطة لمجابهة ذوي الأفكار المتطرفة. وعلى الرغم من هذه المكانة التي نالها الإمام الماتريدي يلاحظ أنه قد أُهمل من كثير من المؤرخين، فلم يشيروا إليه من قريب ولا من بعيد ؛ وإن ذكره مؤرخ فهي كلمات مقتضبة لا تناسب مكانته، ولا مكانة المذهب المنبثق عنه، ولا الدور الذي قام به هو والأشعري في مواجهة المعتزلة والروافض وغيرهما من الفرق . فقد كان للرجلين أثر بارز في إعلاء قيمة العقل مع النقل، حيث كانا نموذجا لوسطية الإسلام التي لا تهمل العقل ولا تعطيه وحده الثقة الكاملة . فلقد تنبه لهذا الإهمال بعض المستشرقين والباحثين المعاصرين، مثل ماكدونالد، وجولد تسيهر، وعبدالرحمن بدوي ؛ ولكن واحدا من هؤلاء لم يشر إلى ما يراه سبتا في هذا الإهمال . ولعل من مظاهر هذا الإغفال أو الغفلة ما كان من كارل بروکلمان (Carl Brockelmann)، حيث لم يذكر الماتريدي في ضمن من ذكر من المفسرين في الباب الثامن علوم (القرآن، واقتصر على ذكره في الباب التاسع (العقائد) ، على الرغم من أنه في هذا الباب ذكر ما وقف عليه من نسخ كتاب تأويلات القرآن. :انظر 1,346 ,.C. Brockelmann, GAL, 1, 209, 515-534; Suppl.
For al-Māturīdī rose in the eastern regions of the Islamic world, and Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī rose in the central regions to confront those with extremist ideas. And despite this status that Imām al-Māturīdī attained, it is observed that he was neglected by many historians, for they did not mention him at all; and if a historian did mention him, it was in brief words that do not suit his status, nor the status of the school that emerged from him, nor the role he and al-Ashʿarī played in facing the Muʿtazila, the Rawāfiḍ, and other sects. For the two men had a prominent impact in elevating the value of reason alongside revelation, as they were a model of Islamic moderation that neither neglects reason nor gives it full confidence alone. Some orientalists and contemporary researchers noticed this neglect, such as MacDonald, Goldziher, and ʿAbd al-Raḥmān Badawī; but not one of them indicated what he sees as a [cause?] for this neglect. Perhaps among the manifestations of this oversight or inattention was what Carl Brockelmann did, for he did not mention al-Māturīdī among those he mentioned of the exegetes in the eighth chapter on Quranic sciences, and restricted his mention to the ninth chapter (on doctrines), despite the fact that in this chapter he mentioned the copies of the book Taʾwīlāt al-Qurʾān that he came across. See: C. Brockelmann, GAL, 1, 209, 515-534; Suppl. 1, 346.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is a historical analysis. It first compares Maturidi and Ash'ari: Maturidi operated in the eastern regions of the Islamic world, while Ash'ari worked in the central regions, both confronting extremist ideas. Despite Maturidi's status, the passage notes that he was neglected by most historians—any mention is brief and disproportionate to his importance. The text then highlights the significant role both men played in balancing reason (ʿaql) and revelation (naql), exemplifying Islamic moderation. It also notes that some orientalists (MacDonald, Goldziher, Badawi) noticed this neglect but did not explain its cause. Finally, it gives an example: Carl Brockelmann omitted Maturidi from his list of Quranic exegetes (chapter 8), mentioning him only in the chapter on doctrines (chapter 9), despite having accessed Maturidi's tafsir work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Māturīdī was historically unimportant or that his work was not significant.
Correction: The passage shows that al-Māturīdī's neglect does not reflect his true status; he was systematically overlooked despite playing a key role alongside al-Ashʿarī and authoring major works like Taʾwīlāt al-Qurʾān.

Checkpoint
Which orientalist is cited as an example of neglecting al-Māturīdī by not listing him among Quranic exegetes?
A) MacDonald
B) Goldziher
C) Carl Brockelmann
D) ʿAbd al-Raḥmān Badawī

Key Takeaway
Maturidi played a pivotal role alongside Ash'ari in defending Islamic orthodoxy and balancing reason with revelation, yet he has been unjustly neglected by historians, as illustrated by Brockelmann's omission.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you study Islamic theology, do you find yourself gravitating toward the more well-known figures like al-Ash'ari while neglecting others like al-Māturīdī? What does that reveal about your own pursuit of knowledge? This week, will you seek out and read one source from a less celebrated scholar?
?
The author laments that al-Māturīdī was mentioned only in brief or not at all by many historians. Are there people in your life—family members, teachers, or historical figures—whose contributions you have overlooked or minimized? How can you honor them this week, even if only in your own heart?
?
The passage highlights the balance of reason and revelation as a model of Islamic moderation. Where in your life have you neglected reason—or revelation—in favor of the other? What is one concrete step you can take today to restore that balance?

Life of Imam al-Maturidi

Maturidi's Lineage and the Debate Over Its Authenticity
Discusses the claim of Maturidi's descent from Abu Ayyub al-Ansari and scholarly opinions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different scholarly views on Imam al-Maturidi's lineage and the distinction between genealogical and honorific attribution.

Core Idea
Maturidi's claimed Ansari lineage may be honorific, not literal.

This lesson explores a fascinating biographical question: Was Imam al-Maturidi of Arab descent from the Companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari? The sources are sparse, and scholars disagree. We will examine the key evidence and the nuanced interpretations of authorities like al-Zabidi and al-Biyadi.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the incomplete sentence at the end—this may affect interpretation.
2
Identify the two main positions
The passage presents two views: that Maturidi's lineage is literal (al-Sam'ani, al-Biyadi) and that it is honorific (al-Zabidi). Find where each is expressed.
3
Understand al-Zabidi's caution
Al-Zabidi's expression indicates that the attribution is one of appreciation and honor, for Maturidi's service to Islam, not a genealogical lineage. This is a key nuance.
Ask yourself: why would al-Zabidi make this distinction?
4
Reflect on the incomplete sentence
The passage ends with 'Perhaps the most correct on the subject is to say that the researcher is not...' Why might the author have left this sentence incomplete? What could be the intended conclusion?
This is a text-critical point; consider the implications for the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولدى الاطلاع إلى ما تيسر لنا من مراجع تناول أصحابها الحديث عنه، فلا نجد شيئا سوى اسمه واسم والده واسم جده اللهم إلا ما ذكره السمعاني والزبيدي، وما جاء على هامش الورقة الأولى من مخطوطة كتاب التوحيد، من أنه يرجع في نسبه إلى أبي أيوب خالد بن زید بن كليب الأنصاري .. ويدعم هذا الاتصال في النسب ما جاء على لسان البياضي من التصريح بتلك النسبة، عند الحديث عن الإمام الماتريدي . بيد أن عبارة الزبيدي تومئ إلى أن تلك النسبة إنما هي نسبة تقدير وتشريف، لقاء ما قدم في نصرة الدين، والدفاع عن وتجلية العقيدة والشريعة، وليست نسبة أصول و نسب . وربما يميل بعض من الباحثين إلى أنه إنما قصد بتلك النسبة بيان أصوله ونسبه في حقيقتها، على ما اتجه إليه أيوب علي مستندا إلى ما وجده على هامش كتاب التوحيد للماتريدي، من رجوع نسبه العربي إلى أبي أيوب الأنصاري ، فيظن هؤلاء أن مرجحات عربية الإمام الماتريدي أقوى من احتمالات عدم عربيته. ولعل الأصح في الموضوع أن يقال إن الباحث ليس. انظر: إشارات المرام للبياضي، ٢٣ . يقول تعليقاً على تلك النسبة : فإن صح ذلك ، فلا ريب فيه، فإنه ناشر السنة، وقامع البدعة، ومحيي الشريعة، كما إن كتبه تدل على ذلك أيضا . انظر : إتحاف السادة للزبيدي، انظر : عقيدة الإسلام والإمام الماتريدي لأيوب علي، ٢٥٠ .
And upon examining what was available to us of references whose authors discussed him, we find nothing except his name, his father's name, and his grandfather's name, except what al-Samʿānī and al-Zabīdī mentioned, and what appeared in the margin of the first folio of the manuscript of Kitāb al-Tawḥīd, that his lineage goes back to Abū Ayyūb Khālid ibn Zayd ibn Kulayb al-Anṣārī. This connection in lineage is supported by what came from al-Biyāḍī in explicitly stating that attribution when speaking about Imām al-Māturīdī. However, al-Zabīdī's expression indicates that this attribution is one of appreciation and honor, for what he contributed in supporting the religion and defending and elucidating creed and law, and not a genealogical lineage. And perhaps some researchers incline to the view that by that attribution he intended to state his actual origins and lineage, as Ayub ʿAlī inclined, relying on what he found in the margin of al-Māturīdī's Kitāb al-Tawḥīd, that his Arab lineage goes back to Abū Ayyūb al-Anṣārī. These people think that the indications of al-Māturīdī's Arabness are stronger than the probabilities of his non-Arabness. Perhaps the most correct on the subject is to say that the researcher is not... See: al-Biyāḍī, Ishārāt al-Marām, p. 23. He says, commenting on that attribution: 'If that is correct, then there is no doubt about it, for he is the spreader of the Sunna, the suppressor of innovation, and the reviver of the Sharīʿa, as his books also indicate that.' See: al-Zabīdī, Ithāf al-Sāda; see: Ayub ʿAlī, ʿAqīdat al-Islam wa al-Imām al-Māturīdī, p. 250.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly discussion of Imam Maturidi's lineage. It begins by noting that biographical sources rarely provide more than his name, father, and grandfather. Two scholars, al-Samʿānī and al-Zabīdī, and a marginal note in a manuscript of Kitāb al-Tawḥīd, claim his descent from Abū Ayyūb al-Anṣārī, a Companion of the Prophet. Al-Biyāḍī also affirms this connection. However, al-Zabīdī's wording suggests this attribution is honorific—a recognition of Maturidi's service to Islam—rather than an actual genealogical tie. Some researchers, like Ayub Ali, argue for a genuine Arab lineage based on the manuscript note, believing the evidence for Arab origin outweighs the likelihood of non-Arab origin. The author then states that perhaps the most correct view is that the researcher is not [certain] (the sentence is cut off). Finally, a quotation from al-Biyāḍī supports the lineage, saying that if it is correct, Maturidi's works confirm his role as a defender of the Sunna.

Key Terms
أبو أيوب الأنصاري

Maturidi's Lineage: Fact or Honor?
Critique of al-Maturidi's claimed Ansari lineage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly debate about Imam al-Maturidi's claimed lineage to Abu Ayyub al-Ansari and the distinction between genealogical and honorary attribution.

Core Idea
A lineage of honor, not necessarily blood.

Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi is a towering figure in Islamic theology, yet surprisingly little is known about his early life and family. This passage examines one specific claim: that he was a descendant of the famous companion Abu Ayyub al-Ansari. As we read, we will see how a later scholar casts doubt on the literal truth of this lineage, suggesting it may be an honorary title instead.

Guided Path
1
Understand the biographical gap
Notice how the passage begins by stating the scarcity of biographical information about al-Maturidi. Only his name, his father's name, and his grandfather's name are known from most sources.
This sets the context for why lineage claims are noteworthy.
2
Identify the sources of the claim
The passage mentions al-Sam'ani, al-Zabidi, and a manuscript margin as sources that trace his lineage to Abu Ayyub al-Ansari. Note that al-Bayadi explicitly states this connection.
3
Grasp al-Zabidi's qualification
Read carefully how al-Zabidi's expression is interpreted: he suggests the lineage is one of appreciation and honor, not literal descent. This is the key critical point of the passage.
Think about why scholars might give such an honorary lineage.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider the difference between a genealogical claim and an honorary one. What does this tell us about how scholars viewed al-Maturidi's contributions?
This connects to the broader theme of how religious figures are remembered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولدى الاطلاع إلى ما تيسر لنا من مراجع تناول أصحابها الحديث عنه، فلا نجد شيئا سوى اسمه واسم والده واسم جده اللهم إلا ما ذكره السمعاني والزبيدي، وما جاء على هامش الورقة الأولى من مخطوطة كتاب التوحيد، من أنه يرجع في نسبه إلى أبي أيوب خالد بن زيد بن كليب الأنصاري .. ويدعم هذا الاتصال في النسب ما جاء على لسان البياضي من التصريح بتلك النسبة، عند الحديث عن الإمام الماتريدي . بيد أن عبارة الزبيدي تومئ إلى أن تلك النسبة إنما هي نسبة تقدير وتشريف، لقاء ما قدم في نصرة الدين، والدفاع عن وتجلية العقيدة والشريعة، وليست نسبة أصول و نسب .
Upon examining what was available to us of references whose authors discussed him, we find nothing except his name, his father's name, and his grandfather's name, except what al-Sam'ani and al-Zabidi mentioned, and what came in the margin of the first folio of the manuscript of Kitab al-Tawhid, that his lineage goes back to Abu Ayyub Khalid ibn Zayd ibn Kulayb al-Ansari... and this genealogical connection is supported by what came on the tongue of al-Bayadi of explicit mention of that lineage when discussing Imam al-Maturidi. However, al-Zabidi's expression indicates that that lineage is only a lineage of appreciation and honor, for what he contributed in supporting the religion and defending and clarifying the creed and law, and it is not a lineage of roots and genealogy.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage presents and critiques the claim that Imam al-Maturidi was a descendent of Abu Ayyub al-Ansari. It begins by noting the scarcity of biographical information, with only his name and that of his father and grandfather known. The sources that do mention his lineage are al-Sam'ani, al-Zabidi, and a marginal note in the manuscript of Kitab al-Tawhid itself, which traces him to Abu Ayyub al-Ansari. This is supported by al-Bayadi's explicit statement. However, the author then cites al-Zabidi's interpretation that this lineage should be understood as one of honor and appreciation for Maturidi's service to the religion, not as a literal genealogical descent. The passage thus introduces a critical distinction between actual ancestry and honorary attribution.

Linguistic Evidence for Imam al-Maturidi's Turkish Origin
Argues from linguistic style in Kitab al-Tawhid that Maturidi was not Arab but Turkish.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how linguistic analysis of Kitab al-Tawhid suggests that Imam al-Maturidi was not of Arab origin but likely Turkish.

Core Idea
Linguistic style can reveal an author's native language.

This passage examines the linguistic evidence from Imam al-Maturidi's own work, Kitab al-Tawhid, to argue for his Turkish origin. The author points to obscure phrasing, grammatical errors, and sentence structures that resemble Turkish syntax, concluding that Maturidi was not an Arabic native speaker.

Guided Path
1
Context of the debate
Understand that there is a scholarly debate about Maturidi's ethnic origin, with some claiming Arab lineage based on an unsourced marginal note.
This passage challenges that claim using internal evidence from the text.
2
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the specific linguistic flaws the author identifies: obscure expressions, weak phrases, and grammatical errors.
3
Analyze the argument
The author argues that the sentence structure in Kitab al-Tawhid often mirrors Turkish syntax. This is the key evidence for Turkish origin.
Consider how a translator's perspective might reveal such patterns.
4
Reflect on implications
Think about how this evidence challenges assumptions that deep knowledge of Islamic sciences implies Arab origin.
The passage shows that linguistic analysis can provide important biographical clues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا كان المرجح لنسبه العربي قد اعتمد على ما جاء في هامش كتاب التوحيد دون ذكر مصدره فما ذا يقال حول كتاب التوحيد وأسلوبه اللغوي فيه ؟ إذ يجد الباحث فيه المؤلف يكتب عبارات غامضة في مسائل مهمة جداً، مع ما فيها من عبارات ضعيفة، وفيها أخطاء لغوية، تؤدي بالباحث بالتالي إلى أن يرجح كون أصل مؤلفه غير عربي . وعند تحقيقنا لـ كتاب التوحيد» وأثناء ترجمة بكر طوبال اوغلي الكتاب إلى اللغة التركية قد ظهرت القاطعة التي تشير بوضوح كامل إلى استحالة كون الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدي عربي الأصل ؛ فرغم علمه الزاخر وفكره العميق في سرد المسائل نرى أن عباراته اللغوية وأسلوبه في توضيح المسائل تدل على أن القائل يستحيل كونه شخصا من أسرة عربية. وفي مقابل ذلك نرى تركيب الجمل التي وردت غالبا في الكتاب شبيهة بالتركيب الوارد في اللغة التركية؛ لذلك لا نستطيع استبعاد الاحتمال الذي يؤدي بنا إلى القول بكون الماتريدي تركي الأصل.
If the proponent of his Arab lineage relied on what came in the margin of Kitab al-Tawhid without mentioning its source, then what can be said about Kitab al-Tawhid and its linguistic style? For the researcher finds that the author writes obscure expressions in very important matters, along with weak expressions and grammatical errors, leading the researcher consequently to prefer that the origin of its author is non-Arab. And during our verification of Kitab al-Tawhid and during Bakr Topaloğlu's translation of the book into Turkish, the decisive evidence appeared that clearly indicates the impossibility of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi being of Arab origin; for despite his abundant knowledge and deep thought in presenting issues, we see that his linguistic expressions and his style in clarifying issues indicate that the speaker cannot possibly be a person from an Arab family. In contrast, we see that the sentence structure that often appears in the book is similar to the structure found in the Turkish language; therefore we cannot exclude the possibility that leads us to say that al-Maturidi is of Turkish origin.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage presents a linguistic argument against the Arab origin of Imam al-Maturidi. It begins by questioning the basis of the Arab lineage claim, which relies on an unsourced marginal note. The author then points to the linguistic style of Kitab al-Tawhid itself: obscure phrasing, weak expressions, and grammatical errors in important matters. This suggests a non-Arab author. The decisive evidence came during the verification and Turkish translation by Bakr Topaloğlu, which revealed that the linguistic expressions and style are inconsistent with an Arab native speaker. Moreover, the sentence structure often mirrors Turkish syntax. Therefore, the author concludes that the probability of Turkish origin cannot be dismissed.

C) Statements by al-Sam'ani and al-Zabidi.

Linguistic analysis of Kitab al-Tawhid, particularly sentence structure resembling Turkish, suggests Imam al-Maturidi was of Turkish origin.

Examining the Claim of al-Maturidi's Brother
Examines the claim of a brother named Abu al-Qasim Ishaq al-Maturidi and its critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly critique of the claim that Imam al-Maturidi had a brother named Abu al-Qasim Ishaq.

Core Idea
Similar names do not prove brotherhood — historical evidence must be examined.

In this passage, we see how scholars assess biographical claims. A.S. Tritton proposed that a manuscript author might be al-Maturidi's brother. Fathallah Khalif responds, distinguishing between plausible discipleship and unsubstantiated sibling relation. This lesson examines the critical method used.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping, then read the English translation. Get a sense of the argument before analyzing.
Notice the names: Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad al-Maturidi vs. Imam al-Maturidi.
2
Identify Tritton's claim
What exactly does Tritton suggest? He notes a manuscript by Abu al-Qasim Ishaq and, because of the name similarity, proposes he might be al-Maturidi's brother and student.
3
Examine Khalif's critique
Khalif agrees the author could have been a student and identifies him as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi, but rejects that he was a brother. Why?
The names are clearly different, and historians mention no such brother.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider the principle: name similarity alone is not sufficient for establishing familial relationships. Historical evidence must be consistent.
This is a common pitfall in biographical research.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى طريق التعرف على أسرة الماتريدي تنبه الأستاذ تريتون (A. S. Tritton) إلى وجود كتاب مخطوط في المتحف البريطاني، تحت رقم (۷۸۱) بعنوان کتاب نقض المبتدعة الخارجة من السواد الأعظم على طريقة الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة، كتبه أبو القاسم إسحاق بن محمد الماتريدي. ولفت النظر ما بين هذا الاسم وبين اسم الإمام الماتريدي من تشابه، فقال: إنه ربما كان شقيق الإمام الماتريدي المشهور، مؤسس المدرسة الماتريدية. وذهب إلى أنه تتلمذ على الإمام الماتريدي في الفقه والكلام. وقد علق فتح الله خليف على ذلك بقوله : ونحن لا نستبعد أن يكون قد تتلمذ على الإمام الماتريدي ، وأن يكون هو القاضي أبا القاسم إسحاق بن محمد بن إسماعيل الشهير بالحكيم السمرقندي (ت ٣٤٠هـ / ٩٥١م)، ولكننا نستبعد أن يكون شقيق الإمام الماتريدي، لأن الاختلاف بين الاسمين بين، كما أن المؤرخين لا يذكرون شيئًا من ذلك .
And on the way to identifying al-Maturidi's family, Professor Tritton (A. S. Tritton) alerted to the existence of a manuscript in the British Museum, under number (781), titled 'Kitab Naqd al-Mubtadi'a al-Kharija min al-Sawad al-A'zam 'ala Tariqat al-Imam al-A'zam Abi Hanifa', written by Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad al-Maturidi. And he noted the similarity between this name and the name of Imam al-Maturidi, so he said: perhaps he was the brother of the famous Imam al-Maturidi, founder of the Maturidi school. And he opined that he studied under Imam al-Maturidi in jurisprudence and theology. Fathallah Khalif commented on that saying: 'We do not exclude that he may have studied under Imam al-Maturidi, and that he may be the judge Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il, known as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi (d. 340 AH / 951 CE), but we exclude that he was the brother of Imam al-Maturidi, because the difference between the two names is clear, and because the historians do not mention anything of that.'
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage discusses the possibility that Imam al-Maturidi had a brother named Abu al-Qasim Ishaq al-Maturidi. It begins by mentioning that A.S. Tritton found a manuscript by this name and suggested, due to the similarity of the names, that he might be al-Maturidi's brother and student. Then Fathallah Khalif responds: he agrees that this person could have been a student of al-Maturidi and identifies him as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi (d. 340 AH). However, he rejects the brotherhood claim because the names are not identical and historians do not mention such a brother. The passage thus presents a scholarly exchange, leaving open the possibility of a student relationship but dismissing the sibling hypothesis.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a similar name (al-Maturidi) automatically indicates a sibling relationship.
Correction: The passage shows that the names differ (Abu al-Qasim Ishaq vs. the Imam's name) and historians do not mention a brother, so the claim is rejected.

Inferring Maturidi's Birth Year from His Teachers
Inferring birth year from teachers' death dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars use indirect evidence, such as teachers' death dates, to estimate the birth year of historical figures like Imam al-Maturidi when direct records are absent.

Core Idea
No birth record? Use the teachers' death dates as clues.

When direct biographical details are missing, scholars must rely on circumstantial evidence. In the case of Imam al-Maturidi, no record of his birth year or generation survives. This lesson examines how the death dates of two of his teachers provide the only available clue to estimate when he was born. The passage from the matn presents this methodological approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice that the author states there is no direct indication of Maturidi's birth year.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the logic continues on the next page.
2
Identify the two teachers
Find the names and death years mentioned: Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi (248 AH) and Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi (268 AH).
3
Understand the inference
Consider why these dates are used: Maturidi must have been born before the earlier death (248 AH) to have studied under them. This establishes a latest possible birth year, placing his birth in the early 3rd century AH.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا ما حاولنا التعرف على السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام الماتريدي، فليس هناك إشارة إلى سنة ميلاده ولا إلى الجيل الذي ولد فيه . وكل ما نستطيعه هو ما وصلنا إليه في هذا الصدد من تاريخ وفاة اثنين من شيوخه، هما محمد بن مقاتل الرازي ونصير بن يحيى البلخي . أما الشيخ محمد بن مقاتل الرازي، فقد ذكر الكوثري أنه توفي سنة ثمان وأربعين ومائتين من الهجرة. وأما الشيخ نصير بن يحيى البلخي، فقد ذكر اللكنوي أنه توفي سنة ثمان وستين ومائتين من
If we try to identify the year in which Imam al-Maturidi was born, there is no indication of his birth year nor of the generation in which he was born. All we can do is what we have reached in this regard from the death dates of two of his teachers: Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi and Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi. As for Shaykh Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, al-Kawthari mentioned that he died in the year 248 AH. As for Shaykh Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, al-Laknawi mentioned that he died in the year 268 AH.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage addresses the challenge of determining Imam al-Maturidi's birth year. It states that there is no direct record of his birth date or generation. Instead, the only available clues are the death dates of two of his teachers: Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, who died in 248 AH according to al-Kawthari, and Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, who died in 268 AH according to al-Laknawi. The passage implies that since Maturidi must have studied under them before their deaths, his birth can be estimated to be sometime before the earlier death (248 AH) and possibly in the early 3rd century AH. The incomplete ending suggests that the argument continues with further inference.

شيوخ
محمد بن مقاتل الرازي
نصير بن يحيى البلخي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam al-Maturidi's birth year is recorded in historical sources.
Correction: The passage explicitly states there is no direct record, and scholars rely on indirect evidence from teachers' death dates.

Checkpoint

A) A direct statement in a biography.
B) The death dates of two of his teachers.
C) The date of his own death.
D) The founding date of the Maturidi school.

Key Takeaway
The death dates of a scholar's teachers can provide the only available clue to estimate his birth year when no direct record exists.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Does your practice of Islam depend on a living chain, or have you cut yourself off? Pray that Allah keeps you linked to the truth through those who transmit it.
?

What kind of 'record' are you leaving for those who come after you—not just dates, but true, unbroken reliance on the teaching of the Salaf? Make a pledge to learn the names and lessons of at least one scholar in your chain.

Imam Maturidi's Ethnic Origin: Linguistic Evidence
Biographer argues from linguistic style for Turkish origin of Maturidi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that Imam al-Maturidi's linguistic style in Kitab al-Tawhid suggests he was not of Arab origin, and how biographical conclusions can be drawn from textual evidence.

Core Idea
Language style can reveal a scholar's ethnic origin.

Biographical debates about early scholars often rely on indirect evidence. In this lesson, we explore how one biographer uses the internal linguistic features of Imam al-Maturidi's own book to argue that he was likely of Turkish origin, not Arab. This demonstrates how textual analysis can complement genealogical research.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how the author moves from questioning the Arab lineage claim to presenting linguistic evidence.
Pay attention to the contrast between the weak external evidence and the strong internal evidence.
2
Identify the two main arguments
The author presents two pieces of evidence: the unsourced marginal note for Arab lineage, and the linguistic style of Kitab al-Tawhid. Identify each and note how they are used.
3
Analyze the linguistic evidence
Focus on the specific linguistic features mentioned: obscure phrases, weak expressions, grammatical errors, and Turkish-like sentence structure. Ask why these would indicate non-Arab origin.
The author distinguishes between depth of knowledge and linguistic fluency.
4
Consider the common misunderstanding
The author emphasizes that Maturidi's abundant knowledge is not diminished by his non-native Arabic. Reflect on why this distinction is important.
This guards against equating linguistic skill with scholarly capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمامه إلا نسبة الأنصاري، ومَسند هذه النسبة غير معروف. فإذا كان المرجح لنسبه العربي قد اعتمد على ما جاء في هامش كتاب التوحيد دون ذكر مصدره فما ذا يقال حول كتاب التوحيد وأسلوبه اللغوي فيه؟ إذ يجد الباحث فيه المؤلف يكتب عبارات غامضة في مسائل مهمة جداً، مع ما فيها من عبارات ضعيفة، وفيها أخطاء لغوية، تؤدي بالباحث بالتالي إلى أن يرجح كون أصل مؤلفه غير عربي. وعند تحقيقنا لـ«كتاب التوحيد» وأثناء ترجمة بكر طوبال اوغلي الكتاب إلى اللغة التركية قد ظهرت القاطعة التي تشير بوضوح كامل إلى استحالة كون الإمام أبي منصور الماتريدي عربي الأصل؛ فرغم علمه الزاخر وفكره العميق في سرد المسائل نرى أن عباراته اللغوية وأسلوبه في توضيح المسائل تدل على أن القائل يستحيل كونه شخصا من أسرة عربية. وفي مقابل ذلك نرى تركيب الجمل التي وردت غالبا في الكتاب شبيهة بالتركيب الوارد في اللغة التركية؛ لذلك لا نستطيع استبعاد الاحتمال الذي يؤدي بنا إلى القول بكون الماتريدي تركي الأصل.
Except for the attribution to al-Ansari, and the source of this attribution is unknown. If the one who prefers his Arab lineage relied on what came in the margin of the Book of Tawhid without mentioning its source, what can be said about the Book of Tawhid and its linguistic style? For the researcher finds in it the author writing obscure phrases on very important matters, along with weak expressions and linguistic errors, leading the researcher to prefer that the origin of its author is non-Arab. And during our investigation of the Book of Tawhid and during the translation of Bakr Topaloglu of the book into Turkish, the decisive evidence appeared that clearly indicates the impossibility of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi being of Arab origin; for despite his abundant knowledge and deep thought in presenting issues, we see that his linguistic expressions and style in clarifying issues indicate that the speaker could not be a person from an Arab family. In contrast, we see that the sentence structure that often appears in the book resembles the structure in the Turkish language; therefore we cannot dismiss the possibility that leads us to say that al-Maturidi is of Turkish origin.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a biographical argument about Imam al-Maturidi's ethnic origin. The author begins by noting that the claim of an Arab lineage (specifically an Ansari lineage) is weak because it is based on an unsourced marginal note in a manuscript. He then shifts to an internal argument from the linguistic style of Kitab al-Tawhid itself. He observes that the book contains obscure phrases, weak expressions, and grammatical errors, which would be uncharacteristic of a native Arabic speaker. This is reinforced by the experience of a Turkish translator who noticed that the sentence structure often resembles Turkish. The author concludes that it is more likely that al-Maturidi was of Turkish origin. Importantly, the author does not disparage al-Maturidi's knowledge; rather, he distinguishes between linguistic fluency and depth of scholarship.

الأصل العربي
التركيب اللغوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Linguistic weakness in Arabic implies lack of knowledge or scholarship.
Correction: The author explicitly states that despite his linguistic style, Maturidi had 'abundant knowledge and deep thought,' distinguishing linguistic fluency from scholarly depth.

Did Imam al-Maturidi Have a Brother? A Manuscript Investigation
Tritton's speculation and Khalif's response on a possible brother of al-Maturidi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars evaluate historical claims about scholars' families, using manuscript evidence and historiographical criticism.

Core Idea
Not everyone who shares a name is a brother—historical claims need evidence.

This lesson examines a curious case: a manuscript named 'Naqd al-Mubtadi'a' was discovered, written by someone sharing the nisba 'al-Maturidi'. Could he be the brother of the famous Imam? We will see how scholars weigh manuscript evidence, name similarities, and historical silence to reach a conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the literal translation to understand the details.
Pay attention to the names and the chain of reasoning.
2
Identify the key claim and counter-claim
Notice Tritton's speculation that the manuscript author might be al-Maturidi's brother, and then Fathallah Khalif's response.
Khalif separates the possibility of being a student from the possibility of being a brother.
3
Reflect on the methodology
Ask yourself: why does Khalif reject brotherhood? What evidence does he use? This illustrates how historical researchers weigh manuscript clues and historical silence.
This connects to the learning objective about evaluating historical claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى طريق التعرف على أسرة الماتريدي تنبه الأستاذ تريتون (A. S. Tritton) إلى وجود كتاب مخطوط في المتحف البريطاني، تحت رقم (781) بعنوان كتاب نقض المبتدعة الخارجة من السواد الأعظم على طريقة الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة، كتبه أبو القاسم إسحاق بن محمد الماتريدي. ولفت النظر ما بين هذا الاسم وبين اسم الإمام الماتريدي من تشابه، فقال: إنه ربما كان شقيق الإمام الماتريدي المشهور، مؤسس المدرسة الماتريدية. وذهب إلى أنه تتلمذ على الإمام الماتريدي في الفقه والكلام. وقد علق فتح الله خليف على ذلك بقوله: ونحن لا نستبعد أن يكون قد تتلمذ على الإمام الماتريدي، وأن يكون هو القاضي أبا القاسم إسحاق بن محمد بن إسماعيل الشهير بالحكيم السمرقندي (ت 340هـ / 951م)، ولكننا نستبعد أن يكون شقيق الإمام الماتريدي، لأن الاختلاف بين الاسمين بين، كما أن المؤرخين لا يذكرون شيئًا من ذلك. ا انظر: الفوائد البهية للكنوي، 15؛ و 99-96 ,A.S. Tritton, “An Early Work from the School of al-Maturidi”؛ ومقدمة التحقيق في كتاب التوحيد للماتريدي، م2.
And on the way to learning about the family of al-Maturidi, Professor Tritton (A. S. Tritton) drew attention to the existence of a manuscript in the British Museum, under number (781), titled 'Kitab Naqd al-Mubtadi'a al-Kharija min al-Sawad al-A'zam 'ala Tariqat al-Imam al-A'zam Abi Hanifa', written by Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad al-Maturidi. He noted the similarity between this name and the name of Imam al-Maturidi, and said: He might be the brother of the famous Imam al-Maturidi, founder of the Maturidi school. And he went on to say that he studied under Imam al-Maturidi in fiqh and kalam. Fathallah Khalif commented on that, saying: We do not rule out that he may have studied under Imam al-Maturidi, and that he might be the judge Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il, known as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi (d. 340 AH / 951 CE), but we rule out that he was the brother of Imam al-Maturidi, because the difference between the two names is clear, and also the historians do not mention anything of that. See: al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya by al-Laknawi, p. 15; and A.S. Tritton, 'An Early Work from the School of al-Maturidi', pp. 96-99; and the introduction of the critical edition of Kitab al-Tawhid by al-Maturidi, vol. 2.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on the family of Imam al-Maturidi. The author reports that the orientalist Tritton discovered a manuscript in the British Museum written by one Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad al-Maturidi. Because of the similarity of the name 'al-Maturidi', Tritton speculated that this person might be the brother of the famous Imam al-Maturidi and also his student in fiqh and kalam. The author then presents the comment of the modern scholar Fathallah Khalif. Khalif agrees that it is possible this person was a student of Imam al-Maturidi, and he identifies him as the judge known as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi. However, Khalif rejects the idea that he was the Imam's brother, citing the obvious difference in the names (the manuscript author's name includes 'Ishaq' while the Imam's name is 'Muhammad') and the silence of the historians on such a relationship. The passage ends with a footnote listing sources.

الشقيق
المخطوط
تتلمذ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Shared nisba (al-Maturidi) means they were brothers.
Correction: The names differ (Muhammad vs Ishaq) and historians do not mention any brother relationship. Similar nisba only indicates a common geographic origin, not family relation.

Key Takeaway
Historical claims about scholars' families require evaluating manuscript evidence, name differences, and the silence of historical sources.

Determining Imam al-Maturidi's Birth Year from His Teachers
Author deduces Maturidi's birth year from his teachers' death dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars use circumstantial evidence—specifically the death dates of teachers—to approximate the birth year of a historical figure when no direct record exists.

Core Idea
Scholars deduce birth years from teachers' death dates, assuming a minimum age of study.

Biographers often lack direct birth records for early Islamic scholars. In such cases, they rely on indirect evidence. Here, the author uses the death dates of two of Maturidi's teachers to bracket his birth year. This lesson walks through that deduction and its implications for Maturidi's place in Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the author's logical steps from known death dates to a probable birth year.
2
Identify the two teachers and their death dates
The passage mentions two teachers: Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi (d. 248 AH) and Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi (d. 268 AH). Note which one died earlier.
Al-Razi's death (248 AH) is the key anchor because Maturidi must have studied under him before that year.
3
Understand the logical deduction
The author argues that Maturidi must have been at least ten years old when al-Razi died in order to have studied under him. Therefore, his birth cannot be later than 238 AH (248 - 10).
This is a minimum estimate; he could have been born earlier.
4
Compare with al-Ash'ari's timeline
The passage notes that al-Maturidi's birth predates al-Ash'ari's by over twenty years, and that Maturidi was a Sunni throughout his life, whereas al-Ash'ari converted from Mu'tazilism after the third century.
This highlights Maturidi's pioneering role in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا ما حاولنا التعرف على السنة التي ولد فيها الإمام الماتريدي، فليس هناك إشارة إلى سنة ميلاده ولا إلى الجيل الذي ولد فيه. وكل ما نستطيعه هو ما وصلنا إليه في هذا الصدد من تاريخ وفاة اثنين من شيوخه، هما محمد بن مقاتل الرازي ونصير بن يحيى البلخي. أما الشيخ محمد بن مقاتل الرازي، فقد ذكر الكوثري أنه توفي سنة ثمان وأربعين ومائتين من الهجرة. وأما الشيخ نصير بن يحيى البلخي، فقد ذكر اللكنوي أنه توفي سنة ثمان وستين ومائتين من الهجرة. من هذا لا نملك إلا أن نقرر بأن مولد الماتريدي بالضرورة كان قبل وفاة أستاذه محمد بن مقاتل الرازي؛ أعني أنه ولد قبل سنة 248هـ / 862م بالقدر الذي يتمكن معه من التوجه إلى طلب العلم والتتلمذ عليه، ليتلقى منه فقه أبي حنيفة وآراءه في العقيدة. ولا يتصور أن يكون ذلك وهو في سن تقل عن عشرة أعوام؛ أي إن الماتريدي على أقل تقدير يكون قد ولد سنة ثمان وثلاثين ومائتين، وقد يكون ميلاده قبل ذلك، ولكنه لا يتصور بعد ذلك. وهذا يعني أنه ولد في عهد المتوكل، الخليفة العباسي (232-247هـ / 847-861م)، كما يعني أنه يتقدم في مولده على أبي الحسن الأشعري بأكثر من عشرين سنة. فإذا ضممنا إلى هذا أن الأشعري بدأت حياته معتزليا، ودام على الاعتزال أربعين سنة - مما يعني أنه بدأ نشاطه في مواجهة الاعتزال، ومناصرة أهل السنة، بعد المائة الثالثة - تبيّن لنا أن الإمام الماتريدي كان من أهل السنة طوال حياته وكان على رأس الاتجاه السني قبل أبي الحسن الأشعري.
If we try to identify the year in which Imam al-Maturidi was born, there is no indication of his birth year nor of the generation in which he was born. All we can do is what we have reached in this regard from the death dates of two of his teachers: Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi and Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi. As for Shaykh Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, al-Kawthari mentioned that he died in the year two hundred and forty-eight of the Hijra. As for Shaykh Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, al-Laknawi mentioned that he died in the year two hundred and sixty-eight of the Hijra. From this we have no choice but to determine that the birth of al-Maturidi necessarily occurred before the death of his teacher Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi; I mean that he was born before the year 248 AH / 862 CE to such an extent that he was able to turn to seeking knowledge and studying under him, to receive from him the fiqh of Abu Hanifa and his views on creed. And it is inconceivable that this was at an age less than ten years; that is, al-Maturidi at the very least must have been born in the year two hundred and thirty-eight, and his birth may have been before that, but it cannot be conceived after that. This means that he was born in the era of al-Mutawakkil, the Abbasid caliph (232-247 AH / 847-861 CE), and it also means that his birth precedes that of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari by more than twenty years. If we add to this that al-Ash'ari began his life as a Mu'tazili and remained in Mu'tazilism for forty years - meaning that he began his activity in opposing Mu'tazilism and supporting Ahl al-Sunna after the third century - it becomes clear to us that Imam al-Maturidi was a Sunni throughout his life and was at the head of the Sunni trend before Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is a biographical determination of Imam al-Maturidi's birth year. Since no direct record exists, the author uses the death dates of two of his teachers: Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi (d. 248 AH) and Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi (d. 268 AH). Because al-Maturidi must have been old enough to study under the first teacher before his death, the author reasons that al-Maturidi was born at least ten years before 248 AH, i.e., no later than 238 AH. This places his birth in the reign of Caliph al-Mutawakkil. The author then compares his birth to that of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, who was born more than twenty years later. He notes that al-Ash'ari was a Mu'tazili for forty years, only becoming Sunni after the third century, whereas al-Maturidi was Sunni throughout his life. Thus, al-Maturidi was a pioneer of Sunni theology before al-Ash'ari.

أبو الحسن الأشعري

Correction: This passage shows al-Maturidi predates al-Ash'ari's Sunni phase by decades; al-Ash'ari was a Mu'tazili for forty years before converting, while al-Maturidi was Sunni throughout his life.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Maturidi was born before 238 AH, making him a senior Sunni theologian before Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Pick one topic in your faith where you have only superficial knowledge, and commit to studying it with depth this month.

Imam al-Maturidi's Death Date: Scholarly Views
Author presents the commonly accepted death year of Maturidi as 333 AH and mentions alternative views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that while most scholars agree Imam al-Maturidi died in 333 AH, there are recorded alternative opinions for his death year.

Core Idea
Scholars nearly agree on 333 AH, but a few dates vary.

In historical biography, even basic facts like a scholar's death date can have multiple reports. This passage from a traditional source presents the range of opinions on Imam al-Maturidi's death, showing that scholarly consensus is often nuanced. As you read, notice how the author weighs the evidence and cites various authorities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation together. Get a feel for the author's style and the flow of information.
The passage includes a long footnote; treat it as part of the main text.
2
Identify the main claim
Notice the phrase 'near-agreement' (ما يشبه الاتفاق). This is the author's central claim: the majority opinion is 333 AH, but it is not unanimous.
3
List the alternative opinions
The passage mentions three possible years: 332 AH (al-Kawthari and al-Nadawi), 333 AH (al-Qurashi and majority), and 336 AH (unnamed source). Count them and note who supports each.
These are not just random; each has a chain of narration.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why does this matter? The exact date helps place Maturidi in relation to other scholars like al-Ash'ari. It also shows the careful methodology of Islamic biography.
This connects to the broader lesson on how scholarly consensus is formed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المقابل نجد ما يشبه الاتفاق بين من تعرضوا لوفاة الشيخ على أنه مات بسمرقند سنة 333هـ / 944م. نقول: ما يشبه الاتفاق، لأن هناك من قال بأن وفاته كانت سنة 336هـ. وذكر الكوثري أن الماتريدي توفي سنة 332هـ على ما رواه قطب الدين الحلبي. وقطع بذلك الشيخ أبو الحسن الندوي. ولكن القرشي ذكر أنه توفي سنة 333هـ، بعد وفاة أبي الحسن الأشعري بقليل، وأن قبره بسمرقند. انظر: الفوائد البهية للكنوي، 221؛ ومقدمة الكوثري لـ كتاب العالم والمتعلم لأبي حنيفة. 2 مفتاح السعادة لطاش كوبري زاده 37/3. وفيات الأعيان لابن خلكان 446/2؛ وتاريخ المذاهب الإسلامية لأبي زهرة، 266. انظر: تاج التراجم لابن قطلوبغا، 59؛ والأنساب للسمعاني، ص 498؛ والفوائد البهية للكنوي، 195؛ وهدية العارفين للبغدادي، 1339. انظر الجواهر المضية لأبي الوفاء القرشي، 158؛ وكشف الظنون لحاجي خليفة، 406/2؛ ومقدمة الكوثري لـ كتاب العالم والمتعلم لأبي حنيفة، 4؛ ورجال الفكر والدعوة في الإسلام لأبي الحسن الندوي، 12. 128-127/1
And on the other hand, we find near-agreement among those who discussed the death of the Shaykh that he died in Samarkand in the year 333 AH / 944 CE. We say: near-agreement, because there are those who said that his death was in the year 336 AH. And al-Kawthari mentioned that al-Maturidi died in the year 332 AH according to what Qutb al-Din al-Halabi narrated. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Nadawi was certain of this. But al-Qurashi mentioned that he died in the year 333 AH, shortly after the death of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and that his grave is in Samarkand. See: al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya by al-Laknawi, p. 221; and the introduction of al-Kawthari to Kitab al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim by Abu Hanifa. 2 Miftah al-Sa'ada by Tashkopruzada 37/3. Wafayat al-A'yan by Ibn Khallikan 446/2; and Tarikh al-Madhahib al-Islamiyya by Abu Zahra, p. 266. See: Taj al-Tarajim by Ibn Qutlubugha, p. 59; and al-Ansab by al-Sam'ani, p. 498; and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya by al-Laknawi, p. 195; and Hadiyyat al-'Arifin by al-Baghdadi, p. 1339. See al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya by Abu al-Wafa' al-Qurashi, p. 158; and Kashf al-Zunun by Hajji Khalifa, 406/2; and the introduction of al-Kawthari to Kitab al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim by Abu Hanifa, p. 4; and Rijal al-Fikr wa al-Da'wa fi al-Islam by Abu al-Hasan al-Nadawi, p. 12. 128-127/1

Commentary
This passage is a summary of the scholarly discussion on Imam al-Maturidi's death date. The author states that most scholars agree he died in 333 AH in Samarkand, but notes that this is only near-agreement because some put the date at 336 AH. He then presents two specific opinions: al-Kawthari reports a narration from Qutb al-Din al-Halabi that it was 332 AH, a view affirmed by al-Nadawi; but al-Qurashi states it was 333 AH, shortly after al-Ash'ari's death. The author provides a lengthy footnote listing sources for these views. The passage does not resolve the discrepancy but simply presents the range of opinions, with the majority leaning toward 333 AH.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: This passage shows that while 333 AH is the most commonly accepted, there are recorded alternatives of 332 and 336 AH, demonstrating that historical consensus can have nuances.

Deducing Maturidi's Birth from His Teacher
Maturidi's birth is deduced from his teacher's death and minimum learning age.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars use the death date of a teacher and a minimum learning age to deduce the birth year of Imam al-Maturidi, and how this places him historically relative to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Historical evidence sets Maturidi's birth before 238 AH, making him over 20 years older than Ash'ari.

This lesson presents a careful historical argument to determine when Imam al-Maturidi was born. Using the death date of his teacher and a reasonable minimum age for study, the author narrows down Maturidi's birth year. This is not just trivia; it reveals that Maturidi was a Sunni from the start, preceding Ash'ari by over two decades.

Guided Path
1
Understand the evidence
Read the passage to identify the key pieces of evidence: the teacher's death in 248 AH and the assumption of a minimum age of ten for serious study.
Notice that the argument does not rely on any direct record of Maturidi's birth.
2
Calculate the latest birth year
Follow the author's reasoning: if the teacher died in 248 AH and Maturidi needed to be at least ten to study, the latest possible birth year is 238 AH.
The author says 'at the very least'—Maturidi could be older, but not younger.
3
Compare with al-Ash'ari
Observe how the author compares Maturidi to Ash'ari: Maturidi is older by over 20 years and was always Sunni, while Ash'ari converted later.
This shows Maturidi's precedence in Sunni theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من هذا لا نملك إلا أن نقرر بأن مولد الماتريدي بالضرورة كان قبل وفاة أستاذه محمد بن مقاتل الرازي؛ أعني أنه ولد قبل سنة ٢٤٨هـ / ٨٦٢م بالقدر الذي يتمكن معه من التوجه إلى طلب العلم والتتلمذ عليه، ليتلقى منه فقه أبي حنيفة وآراءه في العقيدة. ولا يتصور أن يكون ذلك وهو في سن تقل عن عشرة أعوام؛ أي إن الماتريدي على أقل تقدير يكون قد ولد سنة ثمان وثلاثين ومائتين، وقد يكون ميلاده قبل ذلك، ولكنه لا يتصور بعد ذلك. وهذا يعني أنه ولد في عهد المتوكل، الخليفة العباسي (٢٣٢- ٢٤٧ هـ / ٨٤٧-٨٦١م) ، كما يعني أنه يتقدم في مولده على أبي الحسن الأشعري بأكثر من عشرين سنة. فإذا ضممنا إلى هذا أن الأشعري بدأت حياته معتزليا، ودام على الاعتزال أربعين سنة - مما يعني أنه بدأ نشاطه في مواجهة الاعتزال، ومناصرة أهل السنة، بعد المائة الثالثة - تبيّن لنا أن الإمام الماتريدي كان من أهل السنة طوال حياته وكان على رأس الاتجاه السني قبل أبي الحسن الأشعري.
From this we have no choice but to conclude that Maturidi's birth necessarily occurred before the death of his teacher Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi; that is, he was born before the year 248 AH / 862 CE, to the extent that he was able to engage in seeking knowledge and studying under him, receiving from him the fiqh of Abu Hanifa and his views on creed. And it is inconceivable that that would be while he was less than ten years old; that is, Maturidi at the very least would have been born in the year 238 AH, and his birth may have been before that, but it is inconceivable after that. This means that he was born in the era of al-Mutawakkil, the Abbasid caliph (232-247 AH / 847-861 CE), and it also means that he precedes Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in birth by more than twenty years. If we add to this that al-Ash'ari began his life as a Mu'tazili and persisted in Mu'tazilism for forty years - meaning that he began his activity in opposing Mu'tazilism and supporting Ahl al-Sunna after the third century - it becomes clear to us that Imam al-Maturidi was of Ahl al-Sunna throughout his life and was at the head of the Sunni current before Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage uses biographical evidence to determine Maturidi's birth date. The author argues that Maturidi must have been born before 248 AH because his teacher Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi died in that year, and Maturidi needed to be old enough to study under him. Assuming a minimum age of ten for serious study, Maturidi's birth cannot be later than 238 AH. This places his birth in the reign of caliph al-Mutawakkil. The author then compares Maturidi with Ash'ari, noting that Maturidi is older by over twenty years. Since Ash'ari was a Mu'tazili for forty years and only turned to Sunnism after 300 AH, Maturidi was a Sunni throughout his life and led the Sunni trend earlier than Ash'ari.

Maturidi's Death Date Discrepancies
Various opinions on Maturidi's death year are presented and compared.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the varying scholarly opinions regarding Imam Maturidi's death year and the sources that support each.

Core Idea
Maturidi's death date is not unanimously agreed upon — it varies among scholars.

This passage from a biographical study presents several reports about when Imam Maturidi passed away. While many sources agree on 333 AH, other dates have been recorded by respected scholars. Let's explore the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully

2

Al-Kawthari reports 332 AH; al-Qurashi reports 333 AH; some say 336 AH.
3
Analyze the sources
Consider the reliability of the narrators: al-Kawthari, Qutb al-Din al-Halabi, al-Nadwi, and al-Qurashi. Why might there be discrepancies?
Historical records can vary due to transmission errors or different calendars.
4
Reflect on the significance

Precise dating aids historical context but does not affect theological contributions.

Samanid Independence and Cultural Patronage
Historical background: Samanid state and its patronage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Samanid dynasty's political independence from the Abbasid caliphate fostered an environment of intellectual and scientific flourishing that deeply influenced Imam al-Maturidi's context.

Core Idea
Political independence enabled the Samanids to become patrons of a golden age of Islamic learning.

Imam al-Maturidi emerged from a world shaped by politics. The Abbasid caliphate was fragmenting, and new dynasties like the Samanids arose. In this lesson, we'll see how the Samanids used their independence to build a state that sponsored scholarship, creating a rich environment for theological development. The following passage from the biography of al-Maturidi explains this crucial background.

Guided Path
1
Read about the Abbasid decline
Start by reading the passage, which begins by setting the scene of a weakening Abbasid state under al-Ma'mun and al-Mutawakkil. This context is key to understanding why the Samanids could break away.
Notice that the text mentions three breakaway states: Samanids, Saffarids, and Zaydis.
2
Identify the Samanid independence date
Locate the precise year the Samanids formally separated from the caliphate. The passage gives both Hijri and Gregorian dates.
261 AH / 875 CE
3
Analyze the Samanid response
After independence, the Samanids did not just rule; they actively built a great state that rivaled the caliphate and sponsored intellectual activities. Identify the fields they promoted.
They opened fields of intellectual, scientific, and literary activity.
4
Reflect on the impact on Maturidi
Consider how this environment of patronage and competition among scholars might have influenced Maturidi's own theological work. The passage suggests a connection.
Maturidi's hometown was within the Samanid state.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مما تقدم يتبين أن الإمام الماتريدي درج في المنطقة الشرقية من الدولة الإسلامية ونشأ فيها . ومعلوم أن الأجزاء الشرقية من الدولة الإسلامية ظلت خاضعة لسلطان الخلفاء العباسيين في رابطة محكمة، حتى إذا كان عصر الخليفة المأمون أخذت روابط الدولة تتهاوى، وبدأت أجزاء كثيرة تخرج من دائرة السلطة في بغداد. فلما تولى الخلافة المتوكل كان كثير من تلك البلاد قد استقل عن سلطان الخليفة العباسي خصوصا تلك البلاد الشرقية، فرأينا الدولة السامانية في بلاد ما وراء النهر، والدولة الصفارية تضم فارس و خراسان و سجستان، وكرمان، والدولة الزيدية العلوية في جرجان وطبرستان . أما الدولة السامانية - وهي التي تضم الماتريدي - فإنها لم تنفصل عن دولة الخلافة العباسية إلا في سنة ٢٦١هـ / ٨٧٥م . ولما استقل حكامها عن التبعية للخليفة العباسي حرص السامانيون على أن يقيموا فيها دولة عظيمة تتوازن مع دولة الخلافة، وتحقق لهم ما أرادوا، فكان لهم دولة تنافس دولة الخلافة واستمرت حتى سنة ٣٨٩هـ / ٩٩٩م، حيث انتهت على أيدي آل سبكتكين من جهة، وأيدي الترك الخاقانيين من جهة أخرى. وفي ظل هذا الحرص الساماني على عظمة دولتهم فتح ميدان الحركة الفكرية والعلمية والأدبية، فكان ميدانًا للتنافس في هذه الاتجاهات كلها وهكذا سعى السامانيون بكل السبل لتقديم أجل الخدمات التي تحقق ازدهار العلوم الإسلامية واللغة العربية وآدابها.
From what has preceded, it becomes clear that Imam al-Maturidi flourished in the eastern region of the Islamic state and grew up there. And it is known that the eastern parts of the Islamic state remained subject to the authority of the Abbasid caliphs in a firm bond, until when the era of Caliph al-Ma'mun came, the bonds of the state began to crumble, and many parts began to exit the sphere of authority in Baghdad. When al-Mutawakkil assumed the caliphate, many of those lands had already become independent from the rule of the Abbasid caliph, especially those eastern lands, so we saw the Samanid state in Transoxiana, the Saffarid state encompassing Fars, Khurasan, Sijistan, and Kirman, and the Zaydi Alid state in Jurjan and Tabaristan. As for the Samanid state - which includes al-Maturidi - it did not separate from the Abbasid caliphate until the year 261 AH / 875 CE. And when its rulers became independent from subordination to the Abbasid caliph, the Samanids were keen to establish a great state that balanced the caliphate and achieved what they wanted, so they had a state that rivaled the caliphate and continued until 389 AH / 999 CE, when it ended at the hands of the Sebuktigin family on one side and the Khaghanid Turks on the other. Under this Samanid concern for the greatness of their state, the field of intellectual, scientific, and literary activity opened up, and it became a field for competition in all these directions, and thus the Samanids sought by all means to provide the greatest services that achieved the flourishing of Islamic sciences and the Arabic language and its literature.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage provides historical background for Maturidi's environment. It first notes that Maturidi grew up in the eastern part of the Islamic world. It then describes the political decline of the Abbasid empire starting with al-Ma'mun, leading to the independence of various states like the Samanids, Saffarids, and Zaydis. The Samanid state, where Maturidi lived, became independent in 261 AH and lasted until 389 AH. The Samanids, after independence, strove to build a powerful state and sponsored intellectual, scientific, and literary activity, thereby fostering a flourishing of Islamic sciences and Arabic culture.

Samanid Scholars: Defenders of Sunni Orthodoxy
Samanid scholars combated heresy and Mu'tazilism, strengthening Sunni Hanafi doctrine.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Samanid scholars spearheaded a scholarly movement that combated heresy and Mu'tazilism, strengthening Sunni Hanafi doctrine.

Core Idea
The Samanids initiated a vast scholarly movement that defended Sunni Islam against heresy and rationalist deviations.

This passage highlights the remarkable scholarly environment of the Samanid era. Historians like al-Muqaddasi and Ibn Khallikan praised the region's learning. The Samanid rulers supported a wide range of sciences, producing scholars who actively countered heresy and Mu'tazilism, promoting the Sunni school, especially the Hanafi madhhab.

Guided Path

Read the passage and translation

The passage explicitly states these effects.
3
Reflect on the historical context
Consider how the Samanids fostered a broad scientific movement that served orthodox Islam, not just secular sciences.
The movement produced scholars in many fields, all contributing to Sunni defense.
4
Understand the lasting influence
The passage shows the region became deeply attached to the Hanafi school in both creed and fiqh.

فلم يستطع مؤرخ مثل المقدسي إلا أن يقول في ملوك السامانيين ووصف بلاد ما وراء النهر وخراسان: إنه أجل الأقاليم وأكثرها أجلة وعلماء. وهو معدن الخير ومستقر العلم وركن الإسلام المحكم وحصنه الأعظم. وملكه خير الملوك وجنده خير الجنود، فيه يبلغ الفقهاء درجة الملوك. وكذلك كانت رؤية ابن خلكان هذا العرض الموجز تبين أنه كان للسامانيين فضل بدء حركة علمية واسعة النطاق من في البلاد، مما ساعد على إنجاب عدد لا يحصى من العلماء المتخصصين في شتى مجالات العلم والمعرفة من تفسير وفقه وحديث وكلام وفلسفة، وتصوف، ولغة وأدب، وطب، وفلك، وطبعيات الخ. وكان لهؤلاء الأئمة الأجلاء دور بارز في توهين كثير من آراء الزندقة التي كانت تنتشر في البلاد متردية ثوب العقل. كما كان لهم أثر بالغ في تقليص مذهب المعتزلة، وتوجيه عامة البلاد إلى مذهب أهل السنة وتجليته والدفاع عنه، حتى أصبحوا أشد الناس به وحرصا عليه إلى جوار مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة في العقيدة والفقه.
A historian like al-Muqaddasi could not help but say about the Samanid kings and the description of Transoxiana and Khurasan: 'It is the greatest of regions, the most possessed of nobles and scholars. It is a mine of good, a repository of knowledge, the firm pillar of Islam and its greatest fortress. Its king is the best of kings, and its army is the best of armies; in it, jurists reach the rank of kings.' And similarly was the view of Ibn Khallikan. This brief presentation shows that the Samanids had the merit of initiating a vast scientific movement in the country, which helped produce countless specialized scholars in various fields of knowledge: tafsir, fiqh, hadith, kalam, philosophy, Sufism, language, literature, medicine, astronomy, natural sciences, etc. These noble imams had a prominent role in weakening many of the opinions of heresy (zandaqa) that were spreading in the country disguised as rational thought. They also had a great effect in reducing the Mu'tazilite school, directing the general populace to the school of Ahl al-Sunna, making it clear and defending it, until they became the most attached to it and careful about it alongside the school of Imam Abu Hanifa in creed and fiqh.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage highlights the scholarly achievements of the Samanid era. It quotes al-Muqaddasi praising the region's high level of scholarship and Ibn Khallikan's similar view. The Samanids initiated a broad scientific movement producing scholars in many disciplines. These scholars actively combated heresy (zandaqa) that was disguised as rationalism, weakened the Mu'tazilite school, and promoted the Sunni school, especially the Hanafi school in both creed and fiqh, until the populace became firmly attached to it.

?
