The Emergence of Maturidi and Ash'ari as Sunni Defenders
Narrates the historical circumstances leading to the formation of Maturidi and Ash'ari schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazilite overemphasis on reason triggered a Sunni synthesis of reason and revelation, leading to the formation of the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilite excess sparked a Sunni synthesis of reason and revelation.

This passage sets the historical stage for the two great Sunni theological schools. It describes how the Mu'tazila's glorification of reason and their attacks on tradition caused public backlash, preparing the ground for al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari to develop methodologies that balanced reason and transmitted knowledge. The passage highlights their distinct approaches: while both integrated reason, Ash'ari prioritized transmission, while Maturidi relied on reason guided by Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its flow, then read the English translation carefully. Note that this is a historical narrative, not a doctrinal definition.
Pay attention to the political calm and intellectual diversity mentioned at the beginning.
2
Identify the two imams and their contexts
Locate the sections about al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari. Note the environment in which each emerged: Maturidi in the eastern region, Ash'ari in Basra. What common factor triggered both?
The Mu'tazila's exaggeration is the catalyst.
3
Compare the approaches of the two schools
The passage explicitly contrasts the Ash'ari and Maturidi methodologies. Identify the difference: Ash'ari scholars are described as 'bound by transmission and supported it with reason', while Maturidi is said to 'rely on reason guided by the Shari'ah'. Reflect on how this difference affects their theological methods.
This comparison is a key point for understanding later developments in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كما يتضح من هذا أن البيئة التي نشأ فيها أبو منصور الماتريدي كانت هادئة سياسيا، خالية من الصراع العنيف والتقلبات المضطربة، وأنها كانت في الوقت ذاته مزدحمة بالمفكرين والمبدعين من شتى الاتجاهات ومختلف المذاهب. ولما بالغ المعتزلة في تمجيدهم دور العقل مستقلاً في بحث المعتقدات، واشتطوا في تهجمهم على المحدثين والفقهاء ومن حذا حذوهم في الاعتماد على الآثار المنقولة نالوا غضب عامة المسلمين واستنكارهم، مما هيأ المجال لاشتعال الصراع بين هؤلاء وأولئك. فكان تمهيدا لظهور الماتريدي الذي استطاع أن يجمع بين الوجهتين - النقل والعقل ـ في المنطقة الشرقية. ثم تلاه أو صاحبه خروج الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري في البصرة على المعتزلة الذين كان قد تتلمذ على شيخهم أبي على الجبائي، وتمكن بمقدرته العلمية وفصاحته من أن يتولى الجدل نائبًا عن شيخه، واستمر على الاعتزال أربعين سنة، تكشفت له في أثنائها جوانب الخلل في آرائهم. فكان هذان الإمامان أبو منصور الماتريدي وأبو الحسن الأشعري علامة بارزة على طريق أهل السنة، على الرغم مما كان بين الإمامين من فوارق - ليس هنا مجال الحديث عنها مفصلاً - حيث كان علماء الأشعرية يتقيدون بالنقل ويؤيدونه بالعقل، بينما كان الماتريدي يعتمد على العقل بإرشاد من الشرع خصوصا في المسائل العقلية المتعلقة بالعقيدة، حتى وسم المذهب بميسمه وأصبح منسوبًا إليه ، على الرغم من أنه لم يكن مبتدعه، بل كان فيه سائرًا على منهج شيخ شيوخه الإمام أبي حنيفة، غير أنه تحول به من ميدان الفقه إلى ميدان العقيدة والفكر .
As becomes clear from this, the environment in which Abu Mansur al-Maturidi grew up was politically calm, free from violent conflict and turbulent upheavals, and at the same time crowded with thinkers and innovators from all directions and various schools. When the Mu'tazila exaggerated in glorifying the role of reason independently in investigating beliefs, and transgressed in their attacks on the hadith scholars and jurists and those who followed them in relying on transmitted traditions, they incurred the anger and disapproval of the general Muslim populace, which prepared the arena for the ignition of conflict between these groups. Thus it was a prelude to the emergence of al-Maturidi, who was able to combine the two aspects—transmission and reason—in the eastern region. Then followed or accompanied him the emergence of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in Basra against the Mu'tazila, whose shaykh Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i he had studied under. With his scholarly ability and eloquence, he was able to take up debate as a deputy for his shaykh, and he continued on Mu'tazilism for forty years, during which the aspects of flaw in their views became clear to him. So these two imams, Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, were a prominent sign on the path of Ahl al-Sunnah, despite the differences between the two imams—this is not the place to discuss them in detail—whereas the Ash'ari scholars were bound by transmission and supported it with reason, while al-Maturidi relied on reason guided by the Shari'ah, especially in rational matters related to creed. Thus the school was stamped with his mark and became attributed to him, even though he was not its innovator, but rather in it he followed the methodology of the shaykh of his shaykhs, Imam Abu Hanifa, except that he transformed it from the field of fiqh to the field of creed and thought.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage explains the intellectual climate that led to the emergence of al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari. It first describes the environment as politically calm but intellectually vibrant. The Mu'tazila's overemphasis on independent reason and their attacks on tradition caused public backlash, setting the stage for al-Maturidi, who successfully synthesized reason and transmission. Then al-Ash'ari, originally a Mu'tazilite student of al-Jubba'i, broke away after forty years, realizing the flaws in their views. Both imams became pillars of Sunni theology. The passage notes a key difference: Ash'ari scholars prioritized transmission and supported it with reason, while al-Maturidi relied on reason guided by Shari'ah, especially in rational creedal matters. It emphasizes that al-Maturidi's school is essentially the application of Abu Hanifa's methodology to theology, not a new invention.

Key Terms
الماتريدي
الأشعري
المعتزلة
النقل والعقل
أهل السنة
أبو حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Maturidi and Ash'ari completely rejected reason and relied only on tradition.
Correction: Both schools integrated reason, but in different ways: Ash'ari used reason to support transmission, while Maturidi used reason guided by Shari'ah.

Checkpoint
What triggered the emergence of al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari according to the passage?
A) Political instability and violent conflict
B) The Mu'tazila's exaggeration of reason and attacks on tradition
C) The decline of hadith scholarship
D) The spread of Greek philosophy

Key Takeaway
Maturidi and Ash'ari emerged as Sunni defenders by integrating reason and revelation in distinct ways, countering Mu'tazilite rationalism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila attacked the traditionalists for relying on transmitted reports. When you encounter a teaching that seems to conflict with your rational understanding, do you instinctively dismiss it? How can you ensure you give both revelation and reason their proper place in your faith?
?
Al-Maturidi transformed the fiqh methodology of Abu Hanifa into a creedal framework. Is your belief system merely inherited, or have you internalized it with understanding and conviction? What is one area where you need to move from blind imitation to deep, guided reflection?
?
Though both imams faced the same Mu'tazilite challenge, they responded differently. Are you willing to learn from both approaches and integrate them in your own life, even if it means holding tensions (like reason vs. revelation) without minimizing either?

Maturidi's Education and His Teachers
Scarce biographical information and list of four teachers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the challenge of reconstructing al-Maturidi's education from scarce sources and know the four teachers mentioned in detail.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's education is known only through glimpses, but his teachers connect back to Abu Hanifa.

This passage gives us a rare window into al-Maturidi's intellectual formation. The sources do not provide a neat biography of his studies; instead, we must piece together hints. Here, we learn that he studied under leading scholars of his time and that they form a chain back to the great Imam Abu Hanifa. The text then names the few teachers we know in detail.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once without pausing. Then read the English translation to get the overall meaning. Notice how the author begins by noting the scarcity of direct information.
The passage includes footnote references embedded in the text; these are part of the original source.
2
Understand the biographical problem
The passage states that researchers find no direct sequential account of al-Maturidi's education, only scattered glimpses. Reflect on why this might be the case for early Islamic scholars.
This is typical for many pre-modern scholars; full biographies are rare.
3
Identify the chain to Abu Hanifa
The passage emphasizes that al-Maturidi's teachers form a continuous chain ending with Imam Abu Hanifa. Note the importance of this chain in the Hanafi tradition.
Abu Hanifa is the eponymous founder of the Hanafi school.
4
List the known teachers
The text says the number of teachers known in detail does not exceed four, and it names the first two: Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi and Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn... The rest are not specified in this passage.
The names are partially given; the second teacher's full name is cut off by a footnote.
5
Answer the checkpoint
Test your understanding by answering the question about how many teachers are mentioned in detail.

His Education: The researcher in the biographical works and historians does not find a direct description that shows al-Maturidi's scholarly progress. Rather, there are glimpses, excerpts, and indications that can shed light on this aspect of his life in a summary form if they are collected together. All the sources available to us state in general that al-Maturidi acquired fiqh knowledge from the leading scholars of his time in his homeland, and that these scholars represent a link in a continuous chain ending with Imam Abu Hanifa. The first of these scholars that we get to know in detail are no more than four: Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn al-'Abbas ibn al-Husayn al-'Iyadi, and Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn [1: See: The Dawn of Islam by Ahmad Amin, 1/261; 2 History of Islamic Sects by Abu Zahra, pp. 293-294; The Blissful Benefits by al-Kanawi, pp. 130-131].

Then it specifically names his known teachers: the first is Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, and the second is Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn ... (the text is interrupted by footnote references). The passage indicates that the number of known teachers does not exceed four, though only the first two names are partially given.

Maturidi's Environment: Political Calm and Intellectual Diversity
Describes the political peace and intellectual diversity that shaped Maturidi's thought

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the political and intellectual factors that set the stage for Imam Maturidi's synthesis of reason and revelation.

Core Idea
Maturidi's theology emerged from a calm yet diverse intellectual environment.

This passage introduces the unique environment of political stability and intellectual ferment that allowed Maturidi to develop his balanced approach. It highlights the conflict between Mu'tazila rationalists and traditionalists, and how Maturidi resolved this tension by combining transmission (naql) and reason ('aql).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal English translation. Notice the two key features of Maturidi's environment: political calm and intellectual diversity.
2
Identify the conflict trigger
The passage states that the Mu'tazila exaggerated the role of reason and attacked hadith scholars and jurists. This led to conflict. Ask yourself why this extremism provoked reaction.
3
Understand Maturidi's synthesis
The passage concludes that Maturidi was able to combine both transmission and reason. Reflect on how this balanced approach emerged from the preceding turmoil.
Maturidi did not simply compromise; he developed a deliberate methodology.

كما يتضح من هذا أن البيئة التي نشأ فيها أبو منصور الماتريدي كانت هادئة سياسيا، خالية من الصراع العنيف والتقلبات المضطربة، وأنها كانت في الوقت ذاته مزدحمة بالمفكرين والمبدعين من شتى الاتجاهات ومختلف المذاهب. ولما بالغ المعتزلة في تمجيدهم دور العقل مستقلاً في بحث المعتقدات، واشتطوا في تهجمهم على المحدثين والفقهاء ومن حذا حذوهم في الاعتماد على الآثار المنقولة نالوا غضب عامة المسلمين واستنكارهم، مما هيأ المجال لاشتعال الصراع بين هؤلاء وأولئك. فكان تمهيدا لظهور الماتريدي الذي استطاع أن يجمع بين الوجهتين - النقل والعقل ـ في المنطقة الشرقية.

Commentary
This passage provides background on the historical and intellectual context that led to the formation of Maturidi's theology. It begins by noting that Maturidi's environment was politically stable, free from violence and turmoil. At the same time, it was intellectually bustling, filled with thinkers and innovators from diverse directions and schools. The passage then explains that the Mu'tazila overemphasized the role of reason as independent in investigating beliefs and attacked the traditionalists (hadith scholars and jurists) who relied on transmitted reports. This extremism angered the general Muslim populace and sparked conflict between the two groups. This conflict set the stage for the emergence of al-Maturidi, who succeeded in combining transmission (naql) and reason ('aql) in an integrated approach, in the eastern Islamic lands.

Maturidi and Ash'ari: Two Approaches to Reason and Revelation
Compares Maturidi and Ash'ari on combining reason and transmitted tradition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical moments of Imam al-Ash'ari's emergence and the different methods of combining reason and revelation in the Maturidi and Ash'ari schools.

Core Idea
Maturidi prioritizes reason guided by revelation; Ash'ari prioritizes tradition supported by reason.

This passage introduces Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's journey from Mu'tazilism to Ahl al-Sunnah and contrasts his approach with that of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. Understanding these two figures is essential for grasping the intellectual diversity within Sunni theology. Let's explore how each school balances reason and transmitted tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ash'ari's emergence
Read the first part of the passage describing how al-Ash'ari studied under the Mu'tazila and later saw the flaws in their views. Notice the transition.
This sets the stage for understanding his later methodology.
2
Compare the two methodologies
Focus on the sentences that explicitly compare the approaches: Ash'ari scholars 'adhered to transmission and supported it with reason', while Maturidi 'relied on reason guided by revelation'. Reflect on the difference.
The passage notes that Maturidi's school is named after him though he followed Abu Hanifa.
3
Ask why this matters
Consider why these different approaches developed and how they influence Sunni theology today. The passage positions both as 'a prominent sign on the path of Ahl al-Sunnah'.

ثم تلاه أو صاحبه خروج الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري في البصرة على المعتزلة الذين كان قد تتلمذ على شيخهم أبي على الجبائي، وتمكن بمقدرته العلمية وفصاحته من أن يتولى الجدل نائبًا عن شيخه، واستمر على الاعتزال أربعين سنة، تكشفت له في أثنائها جوانب الخلل في آرائهم. فكان هذان الإمامان أبو منصور الماتريدي وأبو الحسن الأشعري علامة بارزة على طريق أهل السنة، على الرغم مما كان بين الإمامين من فوارق - ليس هنا مجال الحديث عنها مفصلاً - حيث كان علماء الأشعرية يتقيدون بالنقل ويؤيدونه بالعقل، بينما كان الماتريدي يعتمد على العقل بإرشاد من الشرع خصوصا في المسائل العقلية المتعلقة بالعقيدة، حتى وسم المذهب بميسمه وأصبح منسوبًا إليه، على الرغم من أنه لم يكن مبتدعه، بل كان فيه سائرًا على منهج شيخ شيوخه الإمام أبي حنيفة، غير أنه تحول به من ميدان الفقه إلى ميدان العقيدة والفكر.
Then followed him or accompanied him the emergence of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari in Basra against the Mu'tazila, with whose teacher Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i he had studied. Through his scholarly ability and eloquence, he was able to undertake debate as a deputy for his teacher, and he continued in Mu'tazilism for forty years, during which time the aspects of flaw in their views became clear to him. These two imams—Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari—were a prominent sign on the path of Ahl al-Sunnah, despite the differences between the two imams—not the place to discuss them in detail—in that the Ash'ari scholars adhered to transmission and supported it with reason, while al-Maturidi relied on reason guided by revelation, especially in rational matters related to creed, until the school was marked with his brand and became attributed to him, even though he was not its originator, but rather in it he followed the method of the teacher of his teachers, Imam Abu Hanifa, except that he transformed it from the field of jurisprudence to the field of creed and thought.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage continues the historical narrative by discussing the emergence of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari alongside al-Maturidi. It first recounts that al-Ash'ari studied under the Mu'tazili teacher Abu 'Ali al-Jubba'i and even debated on his behalf. He remained a Mu'tazili for forty years before the flaws in their views became apparent to him. Then the passage compares the two imams: both are major figures on the path of Ahl al-Sunnah, but they differ in their methodology. The Ash'ari scholars are described as adhering to transmitted tradition (naql) and supporting it with reason ('aql). In contrast, al-Maturidi is said to rely on reason guided by revelation (shar'), especially in rational matters concerning creed. The passage concludes that the Maturidi school was named after him, though he did not originate it; he followed the method of Abu Hanifa but shifted its application from jurisprudence to creed and thought.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
المعتزلة
النقل والعقل
أبو حنيفة
أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi and Ash'ari are essentially the same in their methodology.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Ash'ari scholars adhere to transmission and support it with reason, while Maturidi relies on reason guided by revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes Maturidi's approach from Ash'ari's?
A) Ash'ari relied on reason alone, Maturidi on tradition alone
B) Ash'ari adhered to tradition and supported it with reason, while Maturidi relied on reason guided by revelation
C) Both followed the same method
D) Maturidi was a Mu'tazili before converting

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi and Ash'ari schools, while both Sunni, differ in their primary emphasis: Ash'ari gives priority to transmitted tradition supported by reason, while Maturidi gives priority to reason guided by revelation.

?

?
Al-Maturidi took the method of Abu Hanifa from jurisprudence to theology. Are the intellectual tools you use for understanding faith consistent across different areas of your life, or do you compartmentalize? What would it mean for you to apply a unified, earnest search for truth in everything?

Maturidi's Teachers and Their Hanafi Lineage
Lists Maturidi's direct teachers and traces their chain back to Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identities of al-Maturidi's four direct teachers and how their scholarly chains connect back to Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's teachers link him directly to the Hanafi tradition through multiple chains.

This passage introduces the four main teachers of Imam al-Maturidi and traces their scholarly lineage back to Imam Abu Hanifa. Understanding this chain helps situate al-Maturidi within the broader Hanafi school and shows the depth of his traditional education. Let's explore each teacher and their connection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get a clear picture of the names and chains.
Pay attention to the names and the verbs of study (تفقه, تتلمذ).
2
Identify the four teachers
Look for the four names listed at the beginning. Note their full names and any titles like 'Qadi al-Qudat'.
3

For each teacher, follow the chain of teachers mentioned back to Abu Hanifa. Notice how some share intermediate teachers.
Use the guided breakdown below to map each chain step by step.
4
Appreciate the fields of expertise
The passage ends by noting that his teachers combined many disciplines. Reflect on how this shaped al-Maturidi's own scholarship.

وأول من نتعرف عليهم من هؤلاء الأئمة تفصيلاً لا يتجاوز أربعة هم: أبو نصر أحمد بن العباس بن الحسين العياضي، وأبو بكر أحمد بن إسحاق بن صالح الجوزجاني صاحب الفرق والتمييز، ونصير بن يحيى البلخي، ومحمد بن مقاتل الرازي قاضي القضاة. أما أبو نصر العياضي، فقد كان شيخا للماتريدي، وكان في الوقت ذاته رفيقا له حيث تتلمذا معا لأبي بكر أحمد الجوزجاني، الذي تفقه على أبي سليمان موسى بن سليمان الجوزجاني المتوفي بعد المائتين. وهذا الأخير قد تفقه على القاضي أبي يوسف (ت ١٨٢هـ / ٧٩٨م)، ومحمد بن الحسن الشيباني (ت ١٨٩هـ / (٨٠٥م ، اللذين تفقها على الإمام أبي حنيفة ت ١٥٠هـ / ٧٦٧م) . وأما الإمام نصير بن يحيى البلخي فقد تفقه هو أيضا على الإمام أبي سلیمان موسى بن سليمان الجوزجاني. وتفقه البلخي كذلك هو والإمام محمد بن مقاتل الرازي على الإمامين أبي مطيع الحكم بن عبدالله البلخي (ت۱۹۹ هـ / ٨١٥م)، وأبي مقاتل حفص بن مسلم السمر قندي (ت ٢٠٨هـ / ٨٢٣م . ثم إن الإمام محمد بن مقاتل الرازي أخذ عن محمد بن الحسن الشيباني . أما الميادين التي برز فيها شيوخه فقد كانت تجمع بين الأصول والفروع، والتوحيد والفرق، والتمييز والتحديث.
The first of these imams whom we recognize in detail are no more than four: Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn al-'Abbas ibn al-Husayn al-'Iyadi, and Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ishaq ibn Salih al-Juzjani (author of 'al-Furq wa al-Tamyiz'), and Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, and Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi (chief judge). As for Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, he was a teacher of al-Maturidi and at the same time a companion of his, for they studied together under Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, who studied fiqh under Abu Sulayman Musa ibn Sulayman al-Juzjani (who died after 200 AH). The latter studied fiqh under Judge Abu Yusuf (d. 182 AH / 798 CE) and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH / 805 CE), both of whom studied fiqh under Imam Abu Hanifa (d. 150 AH / 767 CE). As for Imam Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, he also studied fiqh under Imam Abu Sulayman Musa ibn Sulayman al-Juzjani. Al-Balkhi and Imam Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi also studied under the two imams Abu Muti' al-Hakam ibn 'Abdullah al-Balkhi (d. 199 AH / 815 CE) and Abu Muqatil Hafs ibn Muslim al-Samarqandi (d. 208 AH / 823 CE). Then Imam Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi studied under Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani. As for the fields in which his teachers excelled, they combined principles and branches, tawhid and sects, differentiation and hadith transmission.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed list of al-Maturidi's teachers and their scholarly lineage. It names four direct teachers: Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, and Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi. For each, the passage traces their connection back to Abu Hanifa through intermediate scholars. Similarly, al-Balkhi and al-Razi studied under Abu Muti' al-Balkhi and Abu Muqatil al-Samarqandi, who also have chains to Abu Hanifa. The passage concludes by noting that the fields of expertise of his teachers combined various disciplines: principles (usul) and branches (furu'), tawhid and sects, differentiation and hadith transmission.

Maturidi's Scholarly Domains and Transformation of Creed into Science
Describes Maturidi's scholarly domains and his transformation of Hanafi creed into a demonstrative science.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi transformed the Hanafi creed from a transmitted heritage into a systematic science based on rational and textual proofs.

Core Idea
Maturidi turned creed into a science by verifying principles with conclusive evidence.

Imam al-Maturidi was not merely a transmitter of Hanafi theology; he re-founded it as a demonstrative discipline. This passage overviews his fields of study and explains his pivotal role in elevating creed from received dogma to a rigorous science, using both rational and transmitted proofs. Understanding this transformation clarifies why the Maturidi school became a leading intellectual tradition in Sunni Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the literal English translation. Notice the flow: first his fields, then his mastery, then his transformation.
The passage ends mid-sentence; that's acceptable for this excerpt.
2
Identify the fields of study
The passage lists Maturidi's research areas: tafsir, usul al-fiqh, usul al-'aqidah, and refutation of heretical sects. Consider why each field matters for creed.
3
Understand the transformation
Focus on the key sentence: 'this heritage was transformed from creed to science.' Identify the methods Maturidi used: conclusive proofs, compelling arguments, and certain demonstrations.
This is the core idea of the lesson.
4
Reflect on the outcome
The passage concludes that Maturidi became the head of the Hanafi school and leader of Ahl al-Sunnah. Ask: why did this transformation earn him such status?
Contrast with simply transmitting beliefs.

وأما ميادين بحث الماتريدي فقد دارت حول تفسير القرآن الكريم، وأصول الفقه وأصول العقيدة، ومنازع ذوي البدع على اختلاف مشاربهم. وهكذا يتضح أن أبا منصور الماتريدي درس العلوم العقلية كما درس العلوم النقلية درسا عميقا متقنا، ووقف على أصول هذه وتلك، وتعرف على دقائقها، حتى صار إماما مبرزا في الفقه والتفسير والكلام. ويتضح أنه استقبل ما قدم له من آثار شيوخه استقبال العالم الواعي، فرواها لتلاميذه واستوعبها ثم نماها، فأخذت على يديه شكلا آخر ليؤدى دوره في بيان عقيدة أهل السنة، وينبه إلى ما لا يصح الاعتقاد به من غير دليل ولا برهان. بيد أن هذا التراث حُوِّل على يدي الماتريدي من عقيدة إلى علم، حيث حقق تلك الأصول بالأدلة القاطعة، وناقش الفروع بالحجج الدامغة، وأتقن الحوار والمناظرة بالبراهين اليقينية اللامعة، ليصبح بحق رأس مدرسة أبي حنيفة، ورئيس أهل السنة والجماعة في
As for the fields of al-Maturidi's research, they revolved around the interpretation of the Noble Quran, the principles of jurisprudence and the principles of creed, and the refutations of people of innovations of various persuasions. Thus it becomes clear that Abu Mansur al-Maturidi studied the rational sciences as well as the transmitted sciences in a deep and proficient manner, and grasped the principles of these and those, and became acquainted with their subtleties, until he became a distinguished imam in jurisprudence, tafsir, and kalam. And it becomes clear that he received what was presented to him from the works of his teachers with the reception of a conscious scholar, so he transmitted them to his students, absorbed them, and then developed them, so that they took on another form at his hands to fulfill his role in clarifying the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah and cautioning against what should not be believed without proof or evidence. However, this heritage was transformed at the hands of al-Maturidi from creed to science, as he verified those principles with conclusive proofs, discussed the branches with compelling arguments, and mastered dialogue and debate with dazzling certain demonstrations, so that he became truly the head of the school of Abu Hanifa and the leader of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah in

Commentary
This passage summarizes al-Maturidi's scholarly contributions and methodological transformation. It first lists his fields of research: tafsir (Quranic interpretation), usul al-fiqh (principles of jurisprudence), usul al-'aqidah (principles of creed), and refutation of heretical sects. The passage then emphasizes that he studied both rational and transmitted sciences deeply, mastering their principles and subtleties, becoming an imam in fiqh, tafsir, and kalam. It highlights his role as a conscious receiver of his teachers' heritage: he received it, transmitted it to his students, absorbed it, and developed it, giving it a new form. His purpose was to clarify the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah and warn against beliefs not based on proof. The key statement is that he transformed this heritage from a mere creed (aqidah) into a science ('ilm). He achieved this by verifying principles with conclusive evidence, discussing branches with compelling arguments, and mastering debate with certain demonstrations. The passage concludes that he thus became the head of the Hanafi school and leader of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.

Maturidi's Teachers and His Intellectual Lineage
Describes Maturidi's teachers and their chain of learning from Abu Hanifa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the chain of teachers that connected Imam al-Maturidi to Imam Abu Hanifa and the breadth of their expertise.

Core Idea
Maturidi's knowledge was rooted in a direct chain of scholars reaching back to Abu Hanifa.

Imam al-Maturidi did not develop his theology in isolation. His teachers were part of a scholarly network that traced its authority back to the great founder of the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa. This passage from Maturidi's own Kitab al-Tawhid names his key teachers and shows how they connected him to earlier generations, while also highlighting their mastery of diverse fields.

1
Identify the direct teachers of Maturidi

Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi studied alongside Maturidi under Abu Bakr al-Jawzjani.

Follow the lineage from Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi and Maturidi through Abu Bakr al-Jawzjani, then Abu Sulayman al-Jawzjani, then Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and finally to Imam Abu Hanifa.
Note the death dates provided to appreciate the chronological nearness.

Note the scholarly fields

This breadth explains why Maturidi’s theology is well-grounded in all Islamic sciences.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical account of Maturidi's teachers and their scholarly lineage. It begins by naming his direct teachers: Ishaq ibn Salih al-Jawzjani, Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi, and Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi. Then it explains the connection of Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, who was both teacher and peer to Maturidi, as they both studied under Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Jawzjani. The chain continues: Abu Bakr al-Jawzjani studied under Abu Sulayman Musa ibn Sulayman al-Jawzjani, who in turn studied under the qadi Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, who were students of Imam Abu Hanifa. The passage then provides separate chains for Nasir ibn Yahya al-Balkhi and Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, noting their teachers as well. Finally, it states that Maturidi's teachers excelled in multiple fields: principles (usul) and branches (furu'), tawhid and sects, and critical distinction (tamyiz) and hadith transmission (tahdith). This underscores the breadth of Maturidi's intellectual heritage.

?
The passage mentions that Maturidi's teachers excelled in multiple fields: principles and branches, tawhid and sects, critical distinction and hadith. Maturidi's Scholarly Scope and Transformation of 'Aqida into 'Ilm
Describes Maturidi's research areas and his method of systematizing creed into a science.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi expanded the study of creed from inherited beliefs into a structured science validated by rational and transmitted proofs.

Core Idea
Maturidi transformed 'aqida from inherited belief into a verified science.

Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi was not just a transmitter of his teachers' views; he was a systematic thinker who reshaped the way creed is studied. This passage introduces his broad scholarly scope—covering tafsir, usul al-fiqh, and kalam—and highlights his unique contribution: turning the inherited creed into a rigorous science ('ilm) grounded in definitive proofs. As you read, note how he balanced rational and transmitted sciences and what that meant for the development of Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage slowly, then read the English translation. Try to get the overall feel of Maturidi's scholarly range and his transformative role.
Pay attention to the verbs: 'studied', 'received', 'transmitted', 'developed', 'transformed'.
2
Identify Maturidi's fields of research
The passage lists specific areas: tafsir, usul al-fiqh, usul al-'aqida, and refuting innovators. Notice also the two categories of sciences: rational and transmitted.
This shows his comprehensive approach.
3
Understand the transformation from 'aqida to 'ilm
The key phrase is 'from belief to science'. Reflect on what it means to turn creed into a science—using definitive proofs, conclusive arguments, and luminous proofs.
This is Maturidi's hallmark contribution.
4
Recognize the outcome
The passage concludes that Maturidi became the head of the Hanafi school and leader of Ahl al-Sunna in Transoxiana. This shows the impact of his work.
His systematization made him a central authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ميادين بحث الماتريدي فقد دارت حول تفسير القرآن الكريم، وأصول الفقه وأصول العقيدة، ومنازع ذوي البدع على اختلاف مشاربهم. وهكذا يتضح أن أبا منصور الماتريدي درس العلوم العقلية كما درس العلوم النقلية درسا عميقا متقنا، ووقف على أصول هذه وتلك، وتعرف على دقائقها، حتى صار إماما مبرزا في الفقه والتفسير والكلام. ويتضح أنه استقبل ما قدم له من آثار شيوخه استقبال العالم الواعي، فرواها لتلاميذه واستوعبها ثم نماها، فأخذت على يديه شكلا آخر ليؤدى دوره في بيان عقيدة أهل السنة، وينبه إلى ما لا يصح الاعتقاد به من غير دليل ولا برهان. بيد أن هذا التراث حُوِّل على يدي الماتريدي من عقيدة إلى علم، حيث حقق تلك الأصول بالأدلة القاطعة، وناقش الفروع بالحجج الدامغة، وأتقن الحوار والمناظرة بالبراهين اليقينية اللامعة، ليصبح بحق رأس مدرسة أبي حنيفة، ورئيس أهل السنة والجماعة في بلاد ما وراء النهر.
As for the fields of al-Maturidi's research, they revolved around the interpretation of the Noble Quran, the principles of fiqh and the principles of creed, and the arguments of the people of innovation according to their different inclinations. Thus it is clear that Abu Mansur al-Maturidi studied the rational sciences as well as the transmitted sciences deeply and proficiently, and came to know the principles of both, and became acquainted with their subtleties, until he became a preeminent imam in fiqh, tafsir, and kalam. And it is clear that he received what was presented to him from the works of his teachers with the reception of a knowledgeable scholar, transmitted them to his students, absorbed them, then developed them, so they took on his hands a new form to fulfill his role in clarifying the creed of Ahl al-Sunna, and to alert to what is not correct to believe without proof or evidence. Indeed, this heritage was transformed at the hands of al-Maturidi from creed to science, as he verified those principles with definitive proofs, and discussed the branches with conclusive arguments, and mastered dialogue and debate with luminous certain proofs, to become truly the head of the school of Abu Hanifa and the leader of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a in Transoxiana.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a description of Maturidi's scholarly focus and his methodology. It states that Maturidi's fields of research included tafsir, usul al-fiqh, usul al-'aqida, and refuting the arguments of various sects. He studied both rational ('aqliyya) and transmitted (naqliyya) sciences deeply. He received the heritage from his teachers, preserved it, taught it, and developed it, giving it a new form aimed at clarifying the creed of Ahl al-Sunna and warning against baseless beliefs. Most notably, he transformed this heritage from mere 'aqida into a science ('ilm) by verifying its principles with definitive proofs (adilla qati'a) and discussing branches with conclusive arguments (hujaj damigha), mastering debate with luminous certain proofs (barahin yaqiniyya). As a result, he became the head of the Hanafi school and the leader of Ahl al-Sunna in Transoxiana.

Maturidi's Debates and the Rise of the Maturidiyya
Maturidi's debates in Basra and the naming of his school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi's debates in Basra led to the spread of his theological school and the coining of the term 'Maturidiyya'.

Core Idea
Maturidi's 22 trips to Basra made his school a distinct theological identity.

This lesson traces how Imam Maturidi's active engagement in debates beyond his homeland gave rise to a school named after him. The passage highlights his travels to Basra, the frequency of his debates, and how this resulted in the term 'Maturidiyya' being applied to theologians following Abu Hanifa's method in creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Focus on Maturidi's actions: travel, debates, and their consequences.
Notice the strong linking words like 'بل لقد' and 'مما كان سببًا' to see cause and effect.
2
Note the specific number
The passage states twenty-two trips. Reflect on why the author emphasizes this number and what it tells us about Maturidi's effort.
3
Reflect on naming
Consider why the theological school is named after Maturidi rather than Abu Hanifa. The passage explains that ascription to Abu Hanifa is reserved for fiqh only.
This helps clarify the distinction between the Hanafi fiqh school and the Maturidi kalam school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل لقد تجاوز بمحاوراته ومناظراته موطنه، فكانت له رحلات البصرة - حيث الأشاعرة والمعتزلة وغيرهم - للمناظرة في العقائد بلغت نحو اثنتين وعشرين مرة، مما كان سببًا في ذيوع المذهب ونسبته إليه، بل وفي إطلاق وصف «الماتريدية» على المتكلمين الذين يذهبون مذهب أبي حنيفة في تلك البلاد، واقتصر في النسبة إلى أبي حنيفة أصل المذهب على من يتبعونه في الآراء الفقهية فحسب.
Indeed, he transcended with his conversations and debates his homeland. He had travels to Basra — where the Ash'aris, Mu'tazilis, and others — to debate over creeds, amounting to about twenty-two times. This was a cause for the spread of the school and its attribution to him, nay, even for the application of the description 'al-Maturidiyya' to the theologians who follow the school of Abu Hanifa in those lands. And the ascription to Abu Hanifa, the origin of the school, was confined only to those who follow him in jurisprudential opinions.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage discusses Maturidi's influence beyond his home region. It states that he traveled to Basra about twenty-two times for debates on creed, interacting with Ash'aris, Mu'tazilis, and others. These debates caused his school to spread and become attributed to him, even leading to the term 'Maturidiyya' for theologians following Abu Hanifa's method in those lands. It adds that the ascription to Abu Hanifa himself was reserved only for those who followed him in jurisprudential opinions.

Maturidi's Students and the Continuation of His School
Lists Maturidi's prominent students and describes their role in developing his methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who Maturidi's key students were and how they contributed to the development and preservation of his theological school.

Core Idea
Maturidi's students refined his work, even differing when needed, ensuring the school's vitality.

This passage introduces the generation of scholars who studied under Imam Maturidi and carried forward his legacy. It highlights their commitment to clarifying and expanding his teachings, demonstrating that scholarly tradition is built on honest critique and development, not blind imitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prominent students
Read the names and death dates of Maturidi's immediate students mentioned in the passage. Note their titles and regions.
These scholars were the first link in the chain.
2
Understand the critical refinement process
The passage explains how each generation added to Maturidi's work, even differing with him when necessary. This was not disrespect but scholarly integrity.
They affirmed that human effort can be mistaken.
3
See the examples of Bazdawi and Nasafi
Specific examples illustrate how Bazdawi simplified Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid and how Nasafi promoted the school beyond commentary.
Identify the motivation for Bazdawi's work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقد تخرج على يدي الإمام أبي منصور من أئمة العلماء الكثيرون، وكان من أبرزهم أبو القاسم إسحاق بن محمد بن إسماعيل الشهير بالحكيم السمرقندي (ت ٣٤٠هـ / ٩٥١م)، والإمام أبو الحسن علي بن سعيد الرُّسْتُغَفْي (ت ٣٤٥هـ / ٩٥٦م)، والإمام أبو الليث نصر بن أحمد بن إبراهيم البخاري السمرقندي (ت ٣٧٣هـ / ٩٨٤م)، والإمام أبو محمد محمد بن عبدالكريم بن موسى البزدوي (ت ٣٩٠هـ / ١٠٠٠م). وكما صنع الماتريدي مع شيخ شيوخه الإمام أبي حنيفة، صنع تلاميذ الماتريدي مع آثاره؛ فقد نهض منهم جيل بعد جيل - في حلقة متصلة - بتوضيح مذهب إمامهم، والعمل على تيسيره وتنقيحه وتنميته، مضيفين إليه على طريقه ما قد يكون قصر فيه، من غير تحرج في أن يختلفوا معه فيما يرونه يستحق المخالفة أو يستوجبها، مقررين بذلك مبدأ صدق العلماء، الحقة، وإخلاصهم، ويقينهم بأن الجهد البشري يحتمل الخطأ كما يحتمل الصواب؛ فكانوا بذلك قوى دافعة تدعم المذهب وتحفظه وتذيعه في بلاد ما وراء النهر، وتحقق له الحياة وطول العمر. يقرر ذلك ما نراه في صنيع الإمام أبي اليسر محمد بن عبد الكريم البزدوي (ت ٤٩٣ هـ / ١١٠٠م) الذي تلقى فكر الماتريدي عن أبيه، عن جده، عن الماتريدي، وقدم كتابه أصول الدين في تبسيط المذهب، حيث ذكر في مقدمته أنه لولا أن في كتاب التوحيد الذي صنعه الشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي قليل انغلاق وتطويل وفي تطويله نوع تعسير، لولا ذلك لاكتفى به، ولم يقدم كتابه هذا. وما نراه في صنيع الإمام أبي المعين النسفي (ت ٥٠٨هـ / ١١١٤م)، الذي كان في مقدمة من اهتموا بمذهب الماتريدي ونهضوا لنصرته وإذاعته، وفي سبيله إلى ذلك لم يقتصر على تقديم شرح لتأويلات الماتريدي.
Many of the leading scholars graduated under Imam Abu Mansur, the most prominent of whom were Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il, known as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi (d. 340 AH / 951 CE), Imam Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Sa'id al-Rustughfani (d. 345 AH / 956 CE), Imam Abu al-Layth Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Bukhari al-Samarqandi (d. 373 AH / 984 CE), and Imam Abu Muhammad Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Karim ibn Musa al-Bazdawi (d. 390 AH / 1000 CE). And just as al-Maturidi did with the teacher of his teachers, Imam Abu Hanifa, so did al-Maturidi's students with his works. Generation after generation arose — in a continuous chain — to clarify the school of their imam, working to facilitate, refine, and develop it, adding to it on his path what he might have fallen short in, without hesitation to differ with him in what they saw as deserving or necessitating opposition, thereby affirming the principle of truthfulness, sincerity, and certainty of the scholars that human effort may be mistaken just as it may be correct; thus they became driving forces supporting the school, preserving it, and spreading it in Transoxiana, achieving for it life and longevity. This is confirmed by what we see in the work of Imam Abu al-Yusr Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi (d. 493 AH / 1100 CE), who received al-Maturidi's thought from his father, from his grandfather, from al-Maturidi, and presented his book 'Usul al-Din' in simplification of the school. He mentioned in its introduction that were it not for the slight obscurity and length in the book 'Kitab al-Tawhid' authored by Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, and in its length a type of difficulty, he would have been content with it and not presented this book. And what we see in the work of Imam Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi (d. 508 AH / 1114 CE), who was among the foremost who concerned themselves with the Maturidi school and arose for its support and dissemination, and in his endeavor toward that he did not suffice with providing a commentary on al-Maturidi's interpretations.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage first lists Maturidi's most prominent students: al-Hakim al-Samarqandi, al-Rustughfani, Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi, and Abu Muhammad al-Bazdawi. It then describes the general role of his students: generation after generation worked to clarify, simplify, refine, and expand his school, adding to it where he fell short and even differing with him when they deemed it necessary, embodying the sincerity and honesty of scholars who acknowledge that human effort can err. This continuous chain supported and preserved the school. The passage illustrates this with two examples: Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi wrote 'Usul al-Din' to simplify Maturidi's 'Kitab al-Tawhid', noting its obscurity and length. And Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi was among the foremost in promoting the Maturidi school, not content with merely providing a commentary on Maturidi's interpretations.

This connects to the learning objective.

ولقد تخرج على يدي الإمام أبي منصور من أئمة العلماء الكثيرون، وكان من أبرزهم أبو القاسم إسحاق بن محمد بن إسماعيل الشهير بالحكيم السمرقندي (ت ٣٤٠هـ / ٩٥١م)، والإمام أبو الحسن علي بن سعيد الرُّسْتُغَفْي (ت ٣٤٥هـ / ٩٥٦م، والإمام أبو الليث نصر بن أحمد بن إبراهيم البخاري السمرقندي (ت ٣٧٣هـ / ٩٨٤م)، والإمام أبو محمد محمد بن عبدالكريم بن موسى البزدوي (ت ٣٩٠هـ / ١٠٠٠م).
Many leading scholars studied under Imam Abu Mansur, and among the most prominent were: Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad ibn Ismail known as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi (d. 340 AH / 951 CE), Imam Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Sa'id al-Rustughfani (d. 345 AH / 956 CE), Imam Abu al-Layth Nasr ibn Ahmad ibn Ibrahim al-Bukhari al-Samarqandi (d. 373 AH / 984 CE), and Imam Abu Muhammad Muhammad ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Musa al-Bazdawi (d. 390 AH / 1000 CE).

Commentary
This passage enumerates the most prominent students of Imam Maturidi. It provides their names, titles, and death dates, establishing the chain of transmission of his school. These scholars were key in preserving and spreading Maturidi's teachings.

Why Bazdawi Wrote Usul al-Din
Bazdawi's motivation for writing Usul al-Din.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the motivation behind Imam Bazdawi's authorship of Usul al-Din as a simplification of Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid.

Core Idea
Bazdawi wrote to simplify, not to contradict.

This passage gives us a window into the transmission of Maturidi's thought through his students. Imam Bazdawi, a direct intellectual descendant of Maturidi, found the original text too complex and lengthy for easy study. He therefore composed Usul al-Din to make the school more accessible, while remaining fully faithful to Maturidi's teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its English translation. Notice how Bazdawi justifies his authorship.
2
Trace the chain of transmission
The passage tells us Bazdawi received Maturidi's thought from his father, from his grandfather, from Maturidi himself. This establishes his authority and continuity.
Consider why this chain matters for credibility.
3
Identify the dual critique
Bazdawi mentions two issues with Kitab al-Tawhid: complexity (انغلاق) and length (تطويل). Understand each.
Tawil means lengthening, but here it implies difficulty.
4
Reflect on the implication
Bazdawi says he would have been satisfied with Maturidi's book if not for these issues. This shows he did not disagree with the content, only sought to make it easier.
This refutes the misconception of disagreement.
5
Answer the checkpoint
Take the quiz to confirm your understanding of the reason for Bazdawi's book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقرر ذلك ما نراه في صنيع الإمام أبي اليسر محمد بن عبد الكريم البزدوي ت ٤٩٣ هـ / (۱۱۱٠م) الذي تلقى فكر الماتريدي عن أبيه، عن جده، عن الماتريدي، وقدم كتابه أصول الدين في تبسيط المذهب، حيث ذكر في مقدمته أنه لولا أن في كتاب التوحيد الذي صنعه الشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي قليل انغلاق وتطويل وفي تطويله نوع تعسير، لولا ذلك لاكتفى به، ولم يقدم كتابه هذا.
This is confirmed by what we see in the work of Imam Abu al-Yusr Muhammad ibn Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi (d. 493 AH / 1110 CE), who received the thought of Maturidi from his father, from his grandfather, from Maturidi, and he presented his book Usul al-Din to simplify the school, as he mentioned in its introduction that were it not that in the Book of Tawhid composed by Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi there is a little complexity and length, and in its length a kind of difficulty, were it not for that, he would have been satisfied with it and not presented his book.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage provides an example of how a later scholar, Bazdawi, viewed Maturidi's work. He received Maturidi's thought through his father and grandfather, directly from Maturidi. He wrote Usul al-Din to simplify the school because he found Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid somewhat complex and lengthy, with difficulty. Had it not been for that, he would have been content with Maturidi's original work.

Key Terms
أبو اليسر البزدوي
أصول الدين
كتاب التوحيد
تبسيط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Bazdawi disagreed with Maturidi and wrote Usul al-Din to contradict him.
Correction: Bazdawi wrote to simplify Maturidi's work, not to contradict it. He explicitly states he would have been satisfied with Kitab al-Tawhid if not for its complexity and length.

Checkpoint

A) Because he disagreed with Maturidi
B) Because Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid was too complex and lengthy
C) To contradict Maturidi
D) Because he was asked to by the caliph

Key Takeaway
Imam Bazdawi wrote Usul al-Din to simplify Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid, which he found complex and lengthy, while remaining faithful to his teacher.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a complex Islamic text, do you tend to avoid it, or do you seek to understand it and even simplify it for others? Bazdawi did not avoid Maturidi's complexity; he engaged with it and made it accessible. What one complex topic in your faith have you been avoiding, and what is one concrete step you will take this week to begin understanding it deeply?
?
Bazdawi acknowledged his teacher's work and only added his own because of the need for clarity. Do you sometimes feel that you have to innovate or be original to make a contribution, rather than faithfully transmit and clarify what you have learned? How can you cultivate humility in your learning journey, prioritizing service to the truth over personal recognition?
?
If you were to write a book to simplify a difficult aspect of Aqeedah for someone you love, what would it be and why? Consider: what is preventing you from doing that now—lack of knowledge, fear of error, or simply procrastination? Write down one commitment to overcome that barrier this month.

Later Maturidi Scholars: Nasafi and Sabuni
Describes contributions of Nasafi, Abu Hafs, and al-Sabuni.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the contributions of three key later Maturidi scholars: Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, Abu Hafs al-Nasafi, and Nur al-Din al-Sabuni.

Core Idea
Later Maturidi scholars preserved and expanded the school through key texts and debates.

The Maturidi school did not stop with its founder. In the centuries after Imam al-Maturidi, several scholars emerged who systematized, defended, and spread his teachings. This lesson introduces three of those scholars—Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, Abu Hafs al-Nasafi, and Nur al-Din al-Sabuni—whose works became foundational in the tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about three scholars
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: each scholar is introduced with 'وما نراه في صنيع'.
This passage is a continuous description, not a list.
2
Identify each scholar and their main contribution
For each scholar, note their full name, death date, and the work(s) they are known for. Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi wrote Tabshirat al-Adilla; Abu Hafs al-Nasafi wrote al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya; Nur al-Din al-Sabuni wrote two books debating philosophers and theologians.
3
Notice the incident of the student's attribution
The passage mentions that Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi's student, Ala al-Din al-Samarqandi, took his commentary on Maturidi's Ta'wilat and attributed it to himself. This shows the importance of proper attribution.
This is an interesting historical detail.
4
Consider the significance of al-Sabuni's approach
Al-Sabuni's works engaged with philosophers' views, showing the Maturidi school's engagement with other traditions. Reflect on how this might have strengthened Maturidi kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما نراه في صنيع الإمام أبي المعين النسفي ت ٥٠٨هـ / ١١١٤م) ، الذي كان في مقدمة من اهتموا بمذهب الماتريدي ونهضوا لنصرته وإذاعته، وفي سبيله إلى ذلك لم يقتصر على تقديم شرح لتأويلات الماتريدي، تلقفه منه تلميذه الإمام علاء الدين أبو بكر بن محمد بن أحمد السمرقندي، ونسبه إلى نفسه، بل ألف كتابه المشهور بـ تبصرة الأدلة. وما نراه في صنيع أبي حفص نجم الدين عمر بن محمد بن أحمد النسفي ( ت ٥٣٧هـ / ١١٤٢م) ، حين قدم كتابه العقائد النسفية ، ثم ما نراه في صنيع نورالدين بن محمود بن أبي بكر الصابوني (ت ٥٨٠ هـ / ١١٨٤م) ، حيث قدم كتابين له، وهما: أحمد الكفاية في الهداية والبداية في أصول الدين مناظرًا فيهما بين آراء الفلاسفة والمتكلمين.
And what we see in the work of Imam Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi (d. 508 AH / 1114 CE), who was among the foremost who cared for the Maturidi school and rose to support and propagate it, and in his way to that he did not limit himself to presenting a commentary on Maturidi's Ta'wilat, which his student Imam Ala al-Din Abu Bakr ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi took from him and attributed to himself, but he rather authored his famous book called Tabirrat al-Adilla. And what we see in the work of Abu Hafs Najm al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Nasafi (d. 537 AH / 1142 CE), when he presented his book al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya, and then what we see in the work of Nur al-Din Mahmud ibn Abi Bakr al-Sabuni (d. 580 AH / 1184 CE), when he presented two books: Ahmad al-Kifaya fi al-Hidaya and al-Bidaya fi Usul al-Din, in which he debated between the views of the philosophers and the theologians.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage highlights the contributions of three important Maturidi scholars. Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi authored Tabirrat al-Adilla, an important Maturidi kalam work. His student then took his commentary and claimed it. Abu Hafs al-Nasafi authored the famous Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya. Al-Sabuni wrote two works comparing philosophers and theologians. These works were crucial for the development and dissemination of Maturidi kalam.

Key Terms

تبصرة الأدلة
أبو حفص النسفي
العقائد النسفية
نور الدين الصابوني
الكفاية في الهداية
البداية في أصول الدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ala al-Din al-Samarqandi authored the commentary on Maturidi's Ta'wilat.
Correction: The commentary was actually written by Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi; his student al-Samarqandi attributed it to himself.

Key Takeaway
The later Maturidi scholars Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, Abu Hafs al-Nasafi, and Nur al-Din al-Sabuni each contributed key texts that systematized and defended Maturidi theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What one step can you take today to actively engage with theological knowledge rather than just read about it?

Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi went beyond commentary to write an original work. Have you ever taken something you learned and made it your own by applying it or teaching it to someone else? If not, what is stopping you?

Are you willing to confront it with the same courage as al-Sabuni, even if it requires hard intellectual work?

Kitab al-Maqalat: Correcting a Misattribution
Corrects a misattribution of a manuscript to al-Maturidi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence for al-Maturidi's authorship of Kitab al-Maqalat and why a previously misidentified manuscript is actually by Ibn Furak.

Core Idea
Not every manuscript attributed to al-Maturidi is actually his.

This passage examines the evidence for one of al-Maturidi's works, Kitab al-Maqalat. It clarifies that a manuscript thought to be his is actually by Ibn Furak, and explains why the attribution to al-Maturidi remains plausible despite the lack of a known manuscript.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the initial claim about Kitab al-Maqalat.
2
Identify the misattribution
Find where Brockelmann's error is corrected. What was the mistaken manuscript?
3
Understand the correction
Al-Tanji explains why the manuscript is not al-Maturidi's. What is the evidence?
The manuscript turned out to be by Ibn Furak.
4
Consider the conclusion
Despite the lack of a known manuscript, the passage argues that Kitab al-Maqalat is still correctly attributed to al-Maturidi. Why?
Because al-Nasafi explicitly states it, and other contemporary works had similar titles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام . وعبارة أبي المعين النسفي في تبصرة الأدلة واضحة في أن لأبي منصور كتابا آخر باسم كتاب المقالات غير كتاب التوحيد . غير أن الأستاذ محمد بن تاويت الطنجي علق على ما ذكره بروكلمان بالآتي: يقول بروكلمان 46 ,.GAL, 1, 195; Suppl) إن هناك نسخة منه في مكتبة كويريلي تحت رقم ٨٥٦ ، وهو خطأ ؛ فالكتاب - ومنه نسخة أخرى في مكتبة الفاتح تحت رقم ٢٨٩٤ ـ لا صلة له بالماتريدي. وهو لمؤلف لم أوفق لمعرفته، قصد فيه إلى بيان مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعري من كتبه " . ولدى الاطلاع على هذه النسخة بالمكتبة رأينا أنها نسخة خطية لكتاب مجرد مقالات الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري لأبي بكر محمد بن الحسن بن فورك (ت ٤٠٦ هـ / ١٠١٥م). فالواضح أن من مؤلفات الماتريدي كتاب المقالات؛ وإذا كنا نحن حتى اليوم لم نستطع الحصول على نسخة خطية منه في المكتبات، فهذا لا يدل على عدم صحة نسبته إلى الماتريدي. ومن المحتمل أن الماتريدي في هذا الكتاب يرد على جملة مقالات المخالفين لأهل السنة، إذ ظهر في عصره مجموعة من الكتب تحمل هذا العنوان (المقالات)؛ فقد ألف أبو القاسم الكعبي كتابه المقالات، وألف أبو الحسن الأشعري مقالات الإسلاميين.
٣ - كتاب الأصول أو أصول الدين ذکره کكارل بروكلمان باسم كتاب الأصول، ولم يذكر في وصفه سوى اسم المكتبة أو البلد الموجود فيها، كما ذكر أنه لمؤلف مجهول ؛ ولعل الكتاب الذي ورد ذكره في هدية العارفين باسم الدرر في أصول الدين هو هذا الكتاب الذي نحن بصدده وذكره أبو زهرة باسم كتاب الأصول في أصول الدين
- الرد على القرامطة
ذكر أبو المعين النسفي له كتابين في الرد على القرامطة، يرد في أحدهما على أصول مذاهبهم، وفي الآخر يرد على فروعها، ولم يذكر اسم الكتابين . وذكره من المعاصرين أيوب علي بدون وصف له، وكذلك ذكره محمد أبو زهرة وعلى عبد الفتاح المغربي، ولم يذكره كارل بروكلمان ولا فؤاد سزكين؛ وذكره فتح الله خليف أثناء الحديث عن مؤلفاته باسم الرد على أصول القرامطة .
ه - رد الأصول الخمسة لأبي محمد الباهلي
هذا الكتاب ذكره أبو المعين النسفي هكذا ، ولم نقف على وصف له، ولا على ترجمة الباهلي. وذكره من المعاصرين أيوب علي بدون وصف، وكذلك ذكره فتح الله خليف وعلى عبد الفتاح المغربي ، ولم يذكره بروكلمان ولا سزكين.
٦ - رد أوائل الأدلة للكعبي ذكره النسفي بهذا الاسم، كما ورد الكتاب أيضاً بالاسم نفسه عند كارل بروكلمان وعند الباحثين المعاصرين؛ غير أن أبا الوفاء القرشي قد أشار إلى الكتاب باسم كتاب رد أهل الأدلة . وأما عن كتاب أوائل الأدلة فالكعبي ،مؤلفه وهو : أبو القاسم عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود البلخي الكعبي الخراساني (ت ٣١٩ هـ / ٩٣١م) ، رئيس فرقة الكعبية من معتزلة بغداد". - رد تهذيب الجدل للكعبي
ذكره النسفي بهذا الاسم، وكذلك الباحثون المعاصرون"، ولم يذكره بروكلمان ولا سزكين. وقد ورد ذكره في هدية العارفين باسم الرد على تهذيب الكعبي في الجدل".
Speech. And the expression of Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi in Tabṣirat al-Adilla is clear that Abu Mansur has another book called Kitāb al-Maqālāt besides Kitāb al-Tawḥīd. However, Professor Muhammad b. Tāwit al-Ṭanjī commented on what Brockelmann mentioned as follows: Brockelmann says (GAL, 1, 195; Suppl 46) that there is a copy of it in the Kuyrīlī library under number 856, but this is an error; for the book – and there is another copy in the Fatih library under number 2894 – has no connection to al-Māturīdī. It is by an author whose identity I have not been able to determine; its purpose is to explain the doctrine of Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī from his books. And upon examining this copy in the library, we saw that it is a manuscript of the book Mujarrad Maqālāt al-Shaykh Abī al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī by Abū Bakr Muḥammad b. al-Ḥasan b. Fūrak (d. 406 AH / 1015 CE). So it is clear that among al-Māturīdī’s writings is Kitāb al-Maqālāt; and even if we have not until today been able to obtain a manuscript of it in libraries, this does not indicate the incorrectness of its attribution to al-Māturīdī. It is probable that al-Māturīdī in this book refutes a number of the doctrines of those who oppose Ahl al-Sunna, for in his era a group of books bearing this title (al-Maqālāt) appeared; Abū al-Qāsim al-Kaʿbī authored his book al-Maqālāt, and Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī authored Maqālāt al-Islāmiyyīn. 3 – Kitāb al-Uṣūl or Uṣūl al-Dīn: Carl Brockelmann mentioned it as Kitāb al-Uṣūl, and in his description he only mentioned the name of the library or country where it is found, and he said it is by an unknown author; and perhaps the book mentioned in Hadiyyat al-ʿĀrifīn as al-Durar fī Uṣūl al-Dīn is this book we are dealing with, and Abū Zahra mentioned it as Kitāb al-Uṣūl fī Uṣūl al-Dīn. – al-Radd ʿalā al-Qarāmiṭa: Abū al-Muʿīn al-Nasafī mentioned that he has two books on refutation of the Qarāmiṭa, in one of which he refutes the principles of their schools, and in the other he refutes their branches, but he did not name the two books. Among contemporaries, Ayyūb ʿAlī mentioned them without description, as did Muḥammad Abū Zahra and ʿAlī ʿAbd al-Fattāḥ al-Maghribī; Carl Brockelmann and Fuʿād Sezgin did not mention them; Fatḥ Allāh Khalīf mentioned them in his discussion of his works as al-Radd ʿalā Uṣūl al-Qarāmiṭa. 5 – Radd al-Uṣūl al-Khamsa li-Abī Muḥammad al-Bāhilī: This book was mentioned by Abū al-Muʿīn al-Nasafī in this way, and we have not found a description of it, nor a biography of al-Bāhilī. Among contemporaries, Ayyūb ʿAlī mentioned it without description, as did Fatḥ Allāh Khalīf and ʿAlī ʿAbd al-Fattāḥ al-Maghribī; Brockelmann and Sezgin did not mention it. 6 – Radd Awāʾil al-Adilla li-l-Kaʿbī: al-Nasafī mentioned it by this name, and the book also appears by the same name in Carl Brockelmann and among contemporary researchers; however, Abū al-Wafāʾ al-Qurashī referred to the book as Kitāb Radd Ahl al-Adilla. As for the book Awāʾil al-Adilla, its author is al-Kaʿbī, who is: Abū al-Qāsim ʿAbd Allāh b. Aḥmad b. Maḥmūd al-Balkhī al-Kaʿbī al-Khurāsānī (d. 319 AH / 931 CE), head of the Kaʿbiyya sect of the Muʿtazila of Baghdad. – Radd Tahdhīb al-Jadal li-l-Kaʿbī: al-Nasafī mentioned it by this name, as did contemporary researchers; Brockelmann and Sezgin did not mention it. It is mentioned in Hadiyyat al-ʿĀrifīn as al-Radd ʿalā Tahdhīb al-Kaʿbī fī al-Jadal.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic listing of the known works of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, as compiled by a modern editor. It begins by discussing Kitab al-Maqalat, clarifying that al-Maturidi indeed wrote a book by this title separate from Kitab al-Tawhid. The editor corrects a misattribution by Brockelmann, showing that a manuscript thought to be al-Maturidi's is actually a work by Ibn Furak. The passage then proceeds to list other works: Kitab al-Usul (or Usul al-Din), which Brockelmann considered anonymous but may be the same as al-Durar fi Usul al-Din; two refutations of the Qaramita, whose names are not given; Radd al-Usul al-Khamsa by Abu Muhammad al-Bahili, about which little is known; Radd Awa'il al-Adilla by al-Ka'bi, with a note that al-Qurashi called it Radd Ahl al-Adilla; and Radd Tahdhib al-Jadal by al-Ka'bi. Each entry includes references to later scholars who mentioned the work, highlighting which have been lost or survive only in citations. The passage serves to establish the corpus of al-Maturidi's writings and to clarify scholarly controversies over attribution.

Correction: It is actually Ibn Furak's Mujarrad Maqalat al-Ash'ari.

Al-Maturidi's Kitab al-Maqalat is known from textual citations, but no manuscript has been found—a misidentified manuscript turned out to be by Ibn Furak.

?

Maturidi's Other Known Works
Enumerates al-Maturidi's other works with notes on their manuscript evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the other known works of al-Maturidi besides Kitab al-Tawhid and identify which ones have uncertain manuscript evidence.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi authored several polemical works, many of which are lost or only known from citations.

This passage continues listing al-Maturidi's works: Kitab al-Usul, two refutations of the Qaramita, a refutation of al-Bahili's work, and refutations of works by al-Ka'bi. Each entry provides what little is known about manuscript copies and mentions by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of works
Read through the Arabic and English to see the works enumerated.
2
Note the evidence for each
For each work, notice whether it is known from a manuscript, from citations, or from both.
Only Kitab al-Usul has a possible manuscript; others are only mentioned by later authors.

Identify the refutations
Al-Maturidi wrote several refutations. Against whom? The Qaramita, al-Bahili, and al-Ka'bi.
Al-Ka'bi is the target of two refutations.

الكلام . وعبارة أبي المعين النسفي في تبصرة الأدلة واضحة في أن لأبي منصور كتابا آخر باسم كتاب المقالات غير كتاب التوحيد . غير أن الأستاذ محمد بن تاويت الطنجي علق على ما ذكره بروكلمان بالآتي: يقول بروكلمان 46 ,.GAL, 1, 195; Suppl) إن هناك نسخة منه في مكتبة كويريلي تحت رقم ٨٥٦ ، وهو خطأ ؛ فالكتاب - ومنه نسخة أخرى في مكتبة الفاتح تحت رقم ٢٨٩٤ ـ لا صلة له بالماتريدي. وهو لمؤلف لم أوفق لمعرفته، قصد فيه إلى بيان مذهب أبي الحسن الأشعري من كتبه " . ولدى الاطلاع على هذه النسخة بالمكتبة رأينا أنها نسخة خطية لكتاب مجرد مقالات الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري لأبي بكر محمد بن الحسن بن فورك (ت ٤٠٦ هـ / ١٠١٥م). فالواضح أن من مؤلفات الماتريدي كتاب المقالات؛ وإذا كنا نحن حتى اليوم لم نستطع الحصول على نسخة خطية منه في المكتبات، فهذا لا يدل على عدم صحة نسبته إلى الماتريدي. ومن المحتمل أن الماتريدي في هذا الكتاب يرد على جملة مقالات المخالفين لأهل السنة، إذ ظهر في عصره مجموعة من الكتب تحمل هذا العنوان (المقالات)؛ فقد ألف أبو القاسم الكعبي كتابه المقالات، وألف أبو الحسن الأشعري مقالات الإسلاميين.
٣ - كتاب الأصول أو أصول الدين ذکره کكارل بروكلمان باسم كتاب الأصول، ولم يذكر في وصفه سوى اسم المكتبة أو البلد الموجود فيها، كما ذكر أنه لمؤلف مجهول ؛ ولعل الكتاب الذي ورد ذكره في هدية العارفين باسم الدرر في أصول الدين هو هذا الكتاب الذي نحن بصدده وذكره أبو زهرة باسم كتاب الأصول في أصول الدين
- الرد على القرامطة
ذكر أبو المعين النسفي له كتابين في الرد على القرامطة، يرد في أحدهما على أصول مذاهبهم، وفي الآخر يرد على فروعها، ولم يذكر اسم الكتابين . وذكره من المعاصرين أيوب علي بدون وصف له، وكذلك ذكره محمد أبو زهرة وعلى عبد الفتاح المغربي، ولم يذكره كارل بروكلمان ولا فؤاد سزكين؛ وذكره فتح الله خليف أثناء الحديث عن مؤلفاته باسم الرد على أصول القرامطة .
ه - رد الأصول الخمسة لأبي محمد الباهلي
هذا الكتاب ذكره أبو المعين النسفي هكذا ، ولم نقف على وصف له، ولا على ترجمة الباهلي. وذكره من المعاصرين أيوب علي بدون وصف، وكذلك ذكره فتح الله خليف وعلى عبد الفتاح المغربي ، ولم يذكره بروكلمان ولا سزكين.
٦ - رد أوائل الأدلة للكعبي ذكره النسفي بهذا الاسم، كما ورد الكتاب أيضاً بالاسم نفسه عند كارل بروكلمان وعند الباحثين المعاصرين؛ غير أن أبا الوفاء القرشي قد أشار إلى الكتاب باسم كتاب رد أهل الأدلة . وأما عن كتاب أوائل الأدلة فالكعبي ،مؤلفه وهو : أبو القاسم عبد الله بن أحمد بن محمود البلخي الكعبي الخراساني (ت ٣١٩ هـ / ٩٣١م) ، رئيس فرقة الكعبية من معتزلة بغداد". - رد تهذيب الجدل للكعبي
ذكره النسفي بهذا الاسم، وكذلك الباحثون المعاصرون"، ولم يذكره بروكلمان ولا سزكين. وقد ورد ذكره في هدية العارفين باسم الرد على تهذيب الكعبي في الجدل".
Speech. And the expression of Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi in Tabṣirat al-Adilla is clear that Abu Mansur has another book called Kitāb al-Maqālāt besides Kitāb al-Tawḥīd. However, Professor Muhammad b. Tāwit al-Ṭanjī commented on what Brockelmann mentioned as follows: Brockelmann says (GAL, 1, 195; Suppl 46) that there is a copy of it in the Kuyrīlī library under number 856, but this is an error; for the book – and there is another copy in the Fatih library under number 2894 – has no connection to al-Māturīdī. It is by an author whose identity I have not been able to determine; its purpose is to explain the doctrine of Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī from his books. And upon examining this copy in the library, we saw that it is a manuscript of the book Mujarrad Maqālāt al-Shaykh Abī al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī by Abū Bakr Muḥammad b. al-Ḥasan b. Fūrak (d. 406 AH / 1015 CE). So it is clear that among al-Māturīdī’s writings is Kitāb al-Maqālāt; and even if we have not until today been able to obtain a manuscript of it in libraries, this does not indicate the incorrectness of its attribution to al-Māturīdī. It is probable that al-Māturīdī in this book refutes a number of the doctrines of those who oppose Ahl al-Sunna, for in his era a group of books bearing this title (al-Maqālāt) appeared; Abū al-Qāsim al-Kaʿbī authored his book al-Maqālāt, and Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī authored Maqālāt al-Islāmiyyīn. 3 – Kitāb al-Uṣūl or Uṣūl al-Dīn: Carl Brockelmann mentioned it as Kitāb al-Uṣūl, and in his description he only mentioned the name of the library or country where it is found, and he said it is by an unknown author; and perhaps the book mentioned in Hadiyyat al-ʿĀrifīn as al-Durar fī Uṣūl al-Dīn is this book we are dealing with, and Abū Zahra mentioned it as Kitāb al-Uṣūl fī Uṣūl al-Dīn. – al-Radd ʿalā al-Qarāmiṭa: Abū al-Muʿīn al-Nasafī mentioned that he has two books on refutation of the Qarāmiṭa, in one of which he refutes the principles of their schools, and in the other he refutes their branches, but he did not name the two books. Among contemporaries, Ayyūb ʿAlī mentioned them without description, as did Muḥammad Abū Zahra and ʿAlī ʿAbd al-Fattāḥ al-Maghribī; Carl Brockelmann and Fuʿād Sezgin did not mention them; Fatḥ Allāh Khalīf mentioned them in his discussion of his works as al-Radd ʿalā Uṣūl al-Qarāmiṭa. 5 – Radd al-Uṣūl al-Khamsa li-Abī Muḥammad al-Bāhilī: This book was mentioned by Abū al-Muʿīn al-Nasafī in this way, and we have not found a description of it, nor a biography of al-Bāhilī. Among contemporaries, Ayyūb ʿAlī mentioned it without description, as did Fatḥ Allāh Khalīf and ʿAlī ʿAbd al-Fattāḥ al-Maghribī; Brockelmann and Sezgin did not mention it. 6 – Radd Awāʾil al-Adilla li-l-Kaʿbī: al-Nasafī mentioned it by this name, and the book also appears by the same name in Carl Brockelmann and among contemporary researchers; however, Abū al-Wafāʾ al-Qurashī referred to the book as Kitāb Radd Ahl al-Adilla. As for the book Awāʾil al-Adilla, its author is al-Kaʿbī, who is: Abū al-Qāsim ʿAbd Allāh b. Aḥmad b. Maḥmūd al-Balkhī al-Kaʿbī al-Khurāsānī (d. 319 AH / 931 CE), head of the Kaʿbiyya sect of the Muʿtazila of Baghdad. – Radd Tahdhīb al-Jadal li-l-Kaʿbī: al-Nasafī mentioned it by this name, as did contemporary researchers; Brockelmann and Sezgin did not mention it. It is mentioned in Hadiyyat al-ʿĀrifīn as al-Radd ʿalā Tahdhīb al-Kaʿbī fī al-Jadal.

Maturidi's Independence: Hanafi Fiqh and Silence on Ash'ari
Maturidi's Hanafi allegiance and theological independence from Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Māturīdī was a Ḥanafī in fiqh but not merely a representative of the Ḥanafī school, and that he never mentioned al-Ashʿarī, indicating the independence of his theological school.

Core Idea
Maturidi followed Hanafi fiqh but stood independent—silent on Ash'ari.

In this passage, we see al-Māturīdī’s relationship to two key figures: Abū Ḥanīfa in fiqh and al-Ashʿarī in theology. While he defends Ḥanafī positions and expresses gratitude to Abū Ḥanīfa, the author warns against seeing him as a mere mouthpiece. Strikingly, despite living in the same era, al-Māturīdī never mentions al-Ashʿarī or his school. This silence speaks volumes about the distinct development of the Māturīdī tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without over-analyzing, then read the translation. Notice the dual emphasis: Hanafi affiliation and the absence of Ash'ari.
2
Examine the Hanafi connection
Identify how the author describes Maturidi's Hanafism: he defends Hanafi opinions in his tafsir and shows gratitude to Abu Hanifa, but is not merely a 'representative'.
The author corrects a possible misconception.
3
Reflect on the silence regarding Ash'ari
Consider the significance of Maturidi never mentioning al-Ash'ari in his extant works. What does this suggest about the relationship between the two schools?
This silence indicates theological independence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والماتريدي الذي يعتبر حنفي المذهب في الفقه نراه يدافع عن آراء هذا المذهب الفقهية في تأويلات القرآن، وفى مؤلفاته يقدم امتنانه وتقديره لأبي حنيفة . غير أن ذلك لا يعني - كما كان يظن البعض - أن الماتريدي كان ممثلاً للحنفية في بلاد ما وراء النهر " . وقد رأينا كذلك بأن الماتريدي وإن كان قد وجّه في تأويلات القرآن انتقاداته إلى الشافعي، إلا أنه لم يثبت في كتابيه الموجودين بين أيدينا أنه أشار إلى أبي الحسن الأشعري أو مذهبه.
And al-Māturīdī, who is considered Ḥanafī in fiqh, we see him defending the opinions of this school of fiqh in Taʾwīlāt al-Qurʾān, and in his works he expresses his gratitude and appreciation for Abū Ḥanīfa. However, this does not mean—as some used to think—that al-Māturīdī was a representative of the Ḥanafiyya in Transoxiana. And we have also seen that al-Māturīdī, although he directed his criticisms in Taʾwīlāt al-Qurʾān towards al-Shāfiʿī, it has not been established in the two books available to us that he referred to Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī or his school.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage discusses al-Māturīdī's relationship with other scholars and schools. It begins by noting his affiliation with the Ḥanafī school in fiqh; indeed, he defends Ḥanafī opinions in his Quran commentary and shows appreciation for Abū Ḥanīfa. However, the passage warns against overstating this connection: it is not accurate to think that al-Māturīdī was merely a representative of the Ḥanafī school in Transoxiana. The passage then turns to his relationship with al-Shāfiʿī and al-Ashʿarī. It notes that al-Māturīdī did criticize al-Shāfiʿī in his tafsīr, but interestingly, in his extant works, he never mentions Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī or his theological school. This silence is significant for understanding the independence of the Māturīdī school and its distinct development apart from Ashʿarism, even though both are considered Sunnī.

Key Terms

تأويلات القرآن (Taʾwīlāt al-Qurʾān)
أبو الحسن الأشعري (Abū al-Ḥasan al-Ashʿarī)
ما وراء النهر (Mā warāʾ al-nahr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that because Maturidi was Hanafi in fiqh, he simply followed Hanafi theology blindly or was just a representative of the Hanafi school in Transoxiana.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Maturidi defended Hanafi opinions but was not merely a representative; he had his own theological school independent from Ash'ari as well.

Key Takeaway
Al-Māturīdī was a Ḥanafī in fiqh but his theological school developed independently, as evidenced by his silence on al-Ashʿarī.
