Maturidi's Neglect: A Refuted Explanation
Refutation of a false explanation for Maturidi's neglect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical neglect of al-Māturīdī and why the claim that it was due to a lack of philosophical foundation is incorrect.

Core Idea
Maturidism was neglected due to history, not a lack of philosophical depth.

Al-Māturīdī was a pioneering figure in Sunni theology and Quranic interpretation, yet he and his school remained obscure to researchers until the mid-20th century. Scholars offered various reasons for this neglect, including the claim that Māturīdism had no philosophical or intellectual foundation. The passage refutes this claim, setting the stage for a more accurate understanding of the school's significance.

Guided Path
1
Learn about Maturidi's contributions
The passage begins by affirming that al-Māturīdī was a true founder of Sunni kalām and tafsīr bi al-dirāya. Reflect on how this directly contradicts the idea that his school lacks intellectual depth.
2
Identify the false explanation
The passage mentions that some researchers proposed various reasons for Maturidi's neglect, including the idea that his school has no philosophical foundation. This is the specific claim being refuted.
3
Understand the refutation
The passage quotes Professor Muḥammad Saʿīd Yāzījī, who states that those who made that claim have erred. This refutation clears the way for exploring the real historical reasons.
The real reasons might include limited manuscript access or political factors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن الجدير بالذكر أن أبا منصور الماتريدي كان مؤسسا حقيقيا للكلام السني وكذلك التفسير بالدراية؛ فكونه مُهملاً ومجهولاً لدى الباحثين منذ البداية إلى منتصف القرن الماضي أدى بهم إلى تقديم بيانات مختلفة حول أسباب ذلك. غير أن ما أشار إليه الأستاذ محمد سعيد يازيجى أو على قد أصاب حينما قال بأنه قد أخطأ كل من ذهب إلى القول بأن الماتريدية ليس لها أي أساس فلسفى وفكرى وأنها لذلك أُهملت.
And it is worth mentioning that Abū Manṣūr al-Māturīdī was a true founder of Sunnī kalām and also of tafsīr bi al-dirāya (interpretation based on reasoning). So his being neglected and unknown to researchers from the beginning until the middle of the last century led them to present various statements about the reasons for that. However, what Professor Muḥammad Saʿīd Yāzījī (or ʿAlī) pointed out is correct when he said that those who claimed that Māturīdism has no philosophical and intellectual foundation and that it was therefore neglected have all erred.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage addresses the historical neglect of al-Māturīdī and his school. It first asserts that al-Māturīdī was a true founder of both Sunnī kalām and tafsīr bi al-dirāya (interpretation based on reason). Despite this, he was neglected and unknown to researchers from early times until the mid-20th century, leading scholars to propose various reasons for this neglect. The passage then cites the modern scholar Muḥammad Saʿīd Yāzījī (possibly Mustafa Sait Yazıcıoğlu) who refutes a common explanation: that Māturīdism was neglected because it lacked a philosophical or intellectual basis. Yāzījī says that this claim is mistaken. The implication is that the real reasons for neglect are different, perhaps historical or due to lack of access to texts.

Key Terms
التفسير بالدراية (tafsīr bi al-dirāya)
الماتريدية (al-Māturīdiyya)
الأساس الفلسفي (al-asās al-falsafī)
الأساس الفكري (al-asās al-fikrī)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidism was neglected because it lacks a philosophical or intellectual foundation.
Correction: The passage refutes this, asserting that al-Māturīdī was a true founder of Sunni kalām and tafsīr bi al-dirāya, implying a deep intellectual basis.

Checkpoint
What does the passage refute regarding the neglect of al-Māturīdī?
A) That his works were lost.
B) That Maturidism has no philosophical or intellectual foundation.
C) That he was not a true Sunni.
D) That he was only a Hanafi jurist.

Key Takeaway
The claim that Maturidism was neglected due to a lack of philosophical foundation is refuted; the school is intellectually robust.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How often do you judge the depth of a person or idea based on how well-known they are? This lesson refutes the idea that Maturidi's neglect was due to lack of philosophical foundation. When in your own life have you dismissed something as unimportant simply because it was obscure? What would it take for you to truly investigate its worth?
?
The passage states that researchers offered various explanations for the neglect. Are you quick to form explanations for things you don't understand, or do you wait for the truth to emerge? What would it look like for you to hold your assumptions loosely and remain open to correction?
?
If you had accepted the false explanation about Maturidism, would you have missed the opportunity to learn from a profound intellectual tradition? What assumptions about Islamic scholarship do you hold that might need re-evaluation?

His Name and Genealogy
He is
Imam Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi. Al-Maturidi is a nisba to the village in which he was born, called Matrit or Maturit. Commentary
This passage introduces the biography of Imam al-Maturidi. It begins with the heading 'Introduction' and the title of the section: 'The Life and Works of al-Maturidi.' Imam al-Maturidi: Name, Lineage, and Context
Biographical introduction of Imam al-Maturidi's name, lineage, and context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the full name, lineage, birthplace, and historical context of Imam al-Maturidi, including the meaning of his titles and the estimate of his birth year.

Core Idea
Imam al-Maturidi's name, lineage, and titles reveal his Central Asian roots and his high status as a defender of Sunni orthodoxy.

Before diving into the theological contributions of Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, it is essential to know who he was. This lesson introduces his name, his birthplace in the village of Maturid near Samarkand, the titles his followers gave him, and his prophetic lineage back to Abu Ayyub al-Ansari. Understanding his background helps us appreciate the context of his work.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse every detail. Let the author's rhythm come through. Then read the translation to get the full picture.
2
Identify the full name and its components
Notice that the name includes his kunya, ism, nasab, and nisba. Understand that 'al-Maturidi' links him to a village near Samarkand.
The nisba is derived from the village name Maturid (or Maturit).
3
Note the titles and their significance
Look for the titles 'Alam al-Jundi' (Banner of the Army) and 'Imam al-Mutakallimin' (Imam of the Theologians). Consider what these titles say about his role.
These titles were given by his followers and indicate his leadership.
4
Examine his lineage and birth estimates
The passage mentions that his lineage traces to Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, and that his birth year is estimated around 238 AH. Reflect on why these details matter for his authority.
The estimate is based on his teacher's death date.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ - حياة الماتريدي وأعماله اسمه ونسبه هو الإمام أبو منصور محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي . والماتريدي نسبة إلى القرية التى ولد بها وتسمى ماتريد أو ماتريت . وماتريد أو ماتريت قرية من قرى سمرقند في بلاد ما وراء النهر، ویراد به ما وراء نهر جيحون . وأحيانا تضاف سمرقند إلى النسبة فيقال : الشيخ الإمام علم الهدى أبو منصور محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي السمرقندي، كما تقرأ على طرة هذا الكتاب الذي نقدم له. أما علم الجندى، فهو اللقب الذي يخلعه عليه أصحابه ، كما يلقبونه أحياناً إمام المتكلمين، وكلها تدل على مكانته عند أصحابه ومنزلته : إمام الهدى و عندهم في العلم وجهاده في نصرة السنة والدفاع عن العقيدة وإحياء الشريعة. لا تعرف شيئاً عن والديه ولا عن أحد من أسرته ، وإن كان المؤرخون يذكرون أن نسبه يرجع إلى أبي أيوب خالد بن زيد بن كليب الأنصاري ، وهو الذي نزل عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حين هاجر للمدينة؛ ولذلك نجد الإمام البياضي يذكر الأنصاري، صراحة عند ذكر اسم الإمام الماتريدي حيث يقول : الإمام أبو منصور محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي الأنصاري. ولا يذكر أحد من المؤرخين تاريخ مولده ، وإن كان الدكتور أيوب علي أنه ولد حوالى عام ۲۳۸ / ۸۵۲ م؛ لأن أحد أساتذة الماتريدي هو محمد بن مقاتل الرازي الذي توفي عام ٥٢٤٨ / ٨٦٢م . فإن صح ذلك يكون الماتريدي قد عاش ما يقرب من المائة تمام؛ لأن المؤرخين متفقون على أنه توفي عام ٣٣٣ هـ / ٩٤٤ م.
1 - The life of al-Maturidi and his works: his name and lineage. He is the Imam Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi. And al-Maturidi is a relative attribution to the village in which he was born, called Maturid or Maturit. And Maturid or Maturit is a village among the villages of Samarkand in Transoxiana (ma wara' al-nahr), and what is meant is beyond the Oxus River (Jayhun). And sometimes Samarkand is added to the relative attribution, so it is said: the Shaykh, the Imam, the Banner of Guidance, Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi al-Samarqandi, as you read on the title-page of this book which we are introducing. As for 'Alam al-Jundi, it is the title bestowed upon him by his followers, and they also sometimes call him Imam al-Mutakallimin (Imam of the Theologians), all of which indicate his status among his followers and his rank: Imam of Guidance and their position in knowledge and his struggle in supporting the Sunna and defending the creed and reviving the Shari'a. Nothing is known about his parents or anyone from his family, although historians mention that his lineage goes back to Abu Ayyub Khalid ibn Zayd ibn Kulayb al-Ansari, with whom the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) stayed when he migrated to Medina. Therefore we find Imam al-Bayadi explicitly mentioning al-Ansari when mentioning the name of Imam al-Maturidi, saying: Imam Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi al-Ansari. And none of the historians mention his date of birth, although Dr. Ayyub Ali suggests that he was born around 238 AH / 852 CE, because one of al-Maturidi's teachers is Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi who died in 248 AH / 862 CE. If that is correct, then al-Maturidi lived nearly one hundred years, because historians agree that he died in 333 AH / 944 CE.
Source pages p. 542

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Maturidi. It begins by stating his full name: al-Imam Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi. The name 'al-Maturidi' is a nisba (relative attribution) to the village of Maturid or Maturit, which is a village in the region of Samarkand in Transoxiana (what lies beyond the Oxus River). Sometimes Samarkand is added to his name, so he is called al-Maturidi al-Samarqandi, as seen on the title page of the book. The passage then mentions that his followers gave him the title 'Alam al-Jundi (the Banner of the Army) and also called him Imam al-Mutakallimin (Imam of the Theologians), indicating his high status and his efforts in defending the Sunna, the creed, and reviving the Shari'a. Next, it notes that little is known about his parents or family, but historians trace his lineage to Abu Ayyub al-Ansari, the companion who hosted the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Medina. Therefore, some sources add 'al-Ansari' to his name. The passage then addresses his birth date, stating that none of the historians mention it, but Dr. Ayyub Ali estimates it around 238 AH / 852 CE based on the fact that his teacher Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi died in 248 AH / 862 CE, implying that he must have been born earlier. Since historians agree that he died in 333 AH / 944 CE, he would have lived nearly a hundred years.

أبو منصور
ماتريد
سمرقند

علم الجندى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that 'al-Maturidi' refers to a place in Turkey or the Arab world, rather than a village near Samarkand in Central Asia.
Correction: Al-Maturidi is named after the village of Maturid (or Maturit) in the Samarkand region of Transoxiana (modern-day Uzbekistan).

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Maturidi’s full name, titles, and lineage to an Ansar companion ground his authority and place him in the scholarly tradition of Central Asia.

Al-Maturidi's Birth Date and Lifespan
Estimates birth year and questions implied lifespan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars estimate al-Maturidi's birth date and the resulting approximate lifespan of nearly 100 years.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's birth is estimated from his teacher's death, suggesting a long life.

This passage reveals that no historian records al-Maturidi's exact birth date. However, Dr. Ayyub Ali provides an estimate based on the death of one of his teachers, Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi. This estimate leads to a calculation that al-Maturidi lived nearly a century, which we will examine along with the consensus on his death year.

Guided Path
1
Read the birth date estimate
Start by reading the Arabic passage about the birth date. Notice that no historian gives a precise date.
2
Understand the reasoning
See how Dr. Ayyub Ali uses the teacher's death year (248 AH) to estimate the birth year (238 AH). This assumes the teacher was active before his death.
The teacher died 10 years after the estimated birth.
3
Calculate the lifespan
Recognize that if born in 238 AH and died in 333 AH, that is 95 years, nearly 100. The author puts a question mark, implying uncertainty.
The exact calculation is 95 lunar years.
4
Note the death consensus
The passage states that historians agree on the death year 333 AH, except Tashkoprizadeh. This consensus is key to the lifespan estimate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سمياة الماتريدي وأعماله ولا يذكر أحد من المؤرخين تاريخ مولده ، وإن كان الدكتور أيوب علي أنه ولد حوالى عام ۲۳۸ / ۸۵۲ م ؛ لأن أحد أساتذة الماتريدي هو محمد بن مقاتل الرازي الذي توفي عام ٥٢٤٨ / ٨٦٢م . فإن صح ذلك يكون الماتريدي قد عاش ما يقرب من المائة تمام ؟ ؛ لأن المؤرخين متفقون على أنه توفي عام ٣٣٣ هـ / ٩٤٤ م ، ولا يخرج على هذا الإجماع إلا طاش کوپری زاده . فى المتحف البريطاني مخطوطة تحمل رقم 12781 Or. بعنوان : کتاب نقض المبتدعة من السواد الأعظم على طريقة الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة ، كتبه أبو القاء اسحاق بن محمد الماتريدي المتوفى عام ٥٣٤٢ / ٩٥٣ م . ويقول الاستاذ تريتون A. The naming of al-Maturidi and his works. None of the historians mention his date of birth, although Dr. Ayyub Ali estimated that he was born around the year 238 / 852 CE, because one of al-Maturidi's teachers was Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi who died in 248 / 862 CE. If that is correct, then al-Maturidi would have lived nearly a hundred years? Because historians agree that he died in 333 AH / 944 CE, and none contradicts this consensus except Tashkoprizadeh. In the British Museum there is a manuscript numbered Or. 12781 entitled 'Kitab Naqd al-Mubtadi'ah min al-Sawad al-A'zam 'ala Tariqat al-Imam al-A'zam Abi Hanifah', written by Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad al-Maturidi who died in 342 / 953 CE. Professor A. S. Triton says that he may have been the brother of the famous Imam al-Maturidi founder of the Maturidi school, and he holds that he studied under Imam al-Maturidi in fiqh and kalam. We do not rule out that he studied under Imam al-Maturidi and that he is the judge Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il known as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi who died in 340/951 CE... But we rule out that he was the brother of the Imam because the difference between the two names is clear, and also historians do not mention anything of that sort.
Source pages p. 543

Commentary
This passage addresses the uncertainty of al-Maturidi's birth date. It reports that no historian gives a precise date, but Dr. Ayyub Ali estimated 238 AH based on the death date of a teacher. It then calculates that he would have lived about 100 years given his death date in 333 AH. The author notes that this consensus on death date is only contested by Tashkoprizadeh. Then the passage discusses a manuscript by someone similarly named, possibly a brother, but the author argues against that possibility due to name differences and lack of historical evidence.

Correction: The passage shows it is only an estimate, and no historian records it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Maturidi's birth is unknown, but his death is certain. You know your birth date, but your death is hidden. If you were to die today, what would your life have amounted to for the sake of Allah? What changes must you make now, knowing that the hour is unknown?
?
The passage deduces al-Maturidi's existence from his teacher. Think of the teachers who have shaped your iman. Are you actively learning from them, or do you take them for granted? What if their death came tomorrow—would you have learned enough?
?
Historians agreed on al-Maturidi's death year. After you die, what will be your legacy? Will there be a chain of students or deeds that testify to your life? What are you building today that will outlive you?

Refuting a Possible Brother Relation
Analyzes a manuscript and refutes a proposed familial relation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why scholars reject the claim that a manuscript author might be al-Maturidi's brother.

Core Idea
A similar name in a manuscript does not prove brotherhood without evidence.

The passage introduces a manuscript by someone named Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad al-Maturidi and a suggestion by Professor Triton that he might be the brother of the famous Imam. The author carefully evaluates this but ultimately rejects it based on name differences and lack of historical record. Let's explore the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the manuscript passage
Read the Arabic about the manuscript in the British Museum. Note the title and author's name.
2
Understand Triton's claim
Professor Triton suggests this author might be the brother of Imam al-Maturidi and studied under him.
Triton bases this on the name similarity.
3
See the author's acceptance
The author does not rule out that he studied under al-Maturidi, possibly identifying him as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi.
This is a separate point.
4
Analyze the rejection of brotherhood
The author rejects brotherhood because the names differ and historians never mention a brother.
The difference is clear in the names.

سمياة الماتريدي وأعماله ولا يذكر أحد من المؤرخين تاريخ مولده ، وإن كان الدكتور أيوب علي أنه ولد حوالى عام ۲۳۸ / ۸۵۲ م ؛ لأن أحد أساتذة الماتريدي هو محمد بن مقاتل الرازي الذي توفي عام ٥٢٤٨ / ٨٦٢م . فإن صح ذلك يكون الماتريدي قد عاش ما يقرب من المائة تمام ؟ ؛ لأن المؤرخين متفقون على أنه توفي عام ٣٣٣ هـ / ٩٤٤ م ، ولا يخرج على هذا الإجماع إلا طاش کوپری زاده . فى المتحف البريطاني مخطوطة تحمل رقم 12781 Or. بعنوان : کتاب نقض المبتدعة من السواد الأعظم على طريقة الإمام الأعظم أبي حنيفة ، كتبه أبو القاء اسحاق بن محمد الماتريدي المتوفى عام ٥٣٤٢ / ٩٥٣ م . ويقول الاستاذ تريتون A. S. Triton إنه ربما كان شقيق الإمام الماتريدي المشهور مؤسس المدرسة الماتريدية ، كما يذهب إلى أنه تتلمذ على الإمام الماتريدى فى الفقه والكلام . ونحن لا نستبعد أن يكون قد تتلمذ على الإمام الماتريدي وأن يكون هو القاضي أبو القاسم اسحق بن محمد بن اسماعيل الشهير بالحكيم السمرقندي المتوفى عام ٩٥١/٥٣٤٠م ... ولكننا نستبعد أن يكون شقيق الإمام لأن الاختلاف بين الاسمين بين كما أن المؤرخين لا يذكرون شيئاً من ذلك .
The naming of al-Maturidi and his works. None of the historians mention his date of birth, although Dr. Ayyub Ali estimated that he was born around the year 238 / 852 CE, because one of al-Maturidi's teachers was Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi who died in 248 / 862 CE. If that is correct, then al-Maturidi would have lived nearly a hundred years? Because historians agree that he died in 333 AH / 944 CE, and none contradicts this consensus except Tashkoprizadeh. In the British Museum there is a manuscript numbered Or. 12781 entitled 'Kitab Naqd al-Mubtadi'ah min al-Sawad al-A'zam 'ala Tariqat al-Imam al-A'zam Abi Hanifah', written by Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad al-Maturidi who died in 342 / 953 CE. Professor A. S. Triton says that he may have been the brother of the famous Imam al-Maturidi founder of the Maturidi school, and he holds that he studied under Imam al-Maturidi in fiqh and kalam. We do not rule out that he studied under Imam al-Maturidi and that he is the judge Abu al-Qasim Ishaq ibn Muhammad ibn Isma'il known as al-Hakim al-Samarqandi who died in 340/951 CE... But we rule out that he was the brother of the Imam because the difference between the two names is clear, and also historians do not mention anything of that sort.

Commentary
This passage addresses the uncertainty of al-Maturidi's birth date. It reports that no historian gives a precise date, but Dr. Ayyub Ali estimated 238 AH based on the death date of a teacher. It then calculates that he would have lived about 100 years given his death date in 333 AH. The author notes that this consensus on death date is only contested by Tashkoprizadeh. Then the passage discusses a manuscript by someone similarly named, possibly a brother, but the author argues against that possibility due to name differences and lack of historical evidence.

Al-Maturidi's Chain of Teachers to Abu Hanifa
Lists al-Maturidi's teachers and their chains to Abu Hanifa, with a focus on Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Maturidi's education connects through a chain of Hanafi scholars back to Abu Hanifa, and the significance of this scholarly lineage.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's knowledge is authenticated by a direct chain of teachers to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson explores the teachers of Imam al-Maturidi and how they link back to the founder of the Hanafi school, Abu Hanifa. Understanding this chain is crucial for appreciating the authority of al-Maturidi's theological works. The passage from al-Kafawi and al-Zabidi provides a clear genealogy of his teachers.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the teachers
Read the Arabic passage and translation, and list all the teachers mentioned. Notice the pattern of 'teacher-of' links.
The passage names several teachers, each with a chain.
2
Trace the chain back to Abu Hanifa
Follow the chain from al-Maturidi through his teachers to Abu Hanifa. Identify the intermediate scholars.
The chain goes through Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, then to students of Abu Hanifa.
3
Focus on Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi
Pay attention to the details about Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi, his lineage, his martyrdom, and his scholarly status. Why is he highlighted?
He is al-Maturidi's primary teacher and a renowned scholar.
4
Assess the significance of the chain
Reflect on why historical sources emphasize this chain. How does it strengthen al-Maturidi's authority?
It establishes a verified transmission of knowledge.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نقرأ في المصادر التي بين أيدينا أن الماتريدي تفقه في العلم على أئمة العلماء تنتهي إلى الإمام أبي حنيفة . يذكر الكفوي أن الإمام الماتريدي تخرج بأبي نصر العياضي ، وتفقها على أبي بكر أحمد الجوزجاني ، عن أبي سليمان الجوزجاني ، عن محمد ، عن أبي حنيفة . ويقول الزبيدي : تخرج بالإمام أبي نصر العياضي الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن اسحاق بن صالح الجوزجاني صاحب الفرق والتمييز ومن مشايخ الماتريدي محمد بن مقاتل الرازي قاضي الري ... فأما أبو بكر الجوزجاني وأبو نصر العياضي ونصير بن يحيى فكلهم تفقهوا على الإمام أبي سليمان بن موسى بن سليمان الجوزجاني ، وهو على الإمامين أبي يوسف ومحمد بن الحسن ، وتفقه محمد بن مقاتل ونصير بن يحيى أيضاً على الإمامين أبي مطيع الحكم بن عبد الله البلخي وأبي مقاتل حفص بن مسلم السمرقندي ، وأخذ محمد بن مقاتل أيضاً عن محمد بن الحسن ، أربعتهم عن الإمام أبي حنيفة . أما أبو نصر العياضي أول شيوخه فهو أنصاري مثله ، يرجع نسبه إلى يحيى بن قيس بن سعد بن عبادة الأنصاري الخزرجي . كان من أهل العلم والجهاد فقد استشهد خلف أربعين رجلاً كلهم من أقران الماتريدي وهو يحارب الكفرة في بلاد الترك . ويذكر المؤرخون أنه لم يكن أحد يضاهيه في البلاد في علمه
We read in the sources available to us that al-Maturidi studied jurisprudence under imams of scholars whose chain ends with Imam Abu Hanifah. Al-Kafawi mentions that Imam al-Maturidi graduated under Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi, and studied fiqh under Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, from Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, from Muhammad, from Abu Hanifah. Al-Zabidi says: 'He graduated under Imam Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi', Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ishaq ibn Salih al-Juzjani, author of 'al-Firaq wa al-Tamyiz', and among al-Maturidi's teachers is Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, judge of Rayy... As for Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi, and Nasir ibn Yahya, they all studied fiqh under Imam Abu Sulayman ibn Musa ibn Sulayman al-Juzjani, who studied under the two Imams Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. And Muhammad ibn Muqatil and Nasir ibn Yahya also studied under the two Imams Abu Muti' al-Hakam ibn 'Abd Allah al-Balkhi and Abu Muqatil Hafs ibn Muslim al-Samarqandi. And Muhammad ibn Muqatil also took from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. All four of them from Imam Abu Hanifah. As for Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi, his first teacher, he was an Ansari like him, his lineage goes back to Yahya ibn Qays ibn Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah al-Ansari al-Khazraji. He was a man of knowledge and jihad; he was martyred leaving behind forty men, all of whom were peers of al-Maturidi, while he was fighting the disbelievers in the land of the Turks. Historians mention that no one in the land equaled him in knowledge.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage describes al-Maturidi's education and his teachers. It begins by stating that he studied fiqh under scholars whose chain goes back to Abu Hanifa. It then lists specific teachers: al-Kafawi says he graduated under Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi and studied under Abu Bakr al-Juzjani and others. Al-Zabidi adds details about the chain. The passage then traces the teachers of each of these scholars, showing how they all connect to Abu Hanifa. Finally, it focuses on Abu Nasr al-Ayyadi, noting his Ansari lineage, his knowledge, and his martyrdom in battle against the Turks. This establishes the scholarly pedigree of al-Maturidi.

Life of Imam al-Maturidi

Maturidi's Scholarly Lineage and Teachers
Chain of teachers and transmission of Hanafi creedal works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi's scholarly lineage connects him directly to Imam Abu Hanifa and the key creedal works that form the foundation of his theology.

Core Idea
Maturidi's creed is not his invention; it is the transmitted Hanafi orthodoxy.

This passage from the biographical sources establishes the scholarly credentials of Imam al-Maturidi. It traces his teachers and their teachers back to Abu Hanifa, showing that his theological method is rooted in a living chain of transmission. The passage also highlights the specific creedal works of Abu Hanifa that were studied and transmitted by this chain, which Maturidi later systematized.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the chain of narration
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how the author begins with Maturidi's death date and then immediately moves to his education.
The chain of teachers is central to establishing authority.
2
Identify the key teachers and their links to Abu Hanifa
Look for the names: Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, Muhammad ibn Muqatil, etc. Trace how each connects back to Abu Hanifa through intermediate figures like Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani.
The passage presents multiple parallel chains, all converging on Abu Hanifa.
3
Examine the mention of al-Fiqh al-Akbar and other works
Find the list of creedal works attributed to Abu Hanifa: al-Fiqh al-Akbar, al-Risala, al-Fiqh al-Absat, Kitab al-‘Alim wa al-Muta‘allim, and al-Wasiyya. These are the texts Maturidi studied and transmitted.
These works form the textual basis of Maturidi's theology.
4
Reflect on how this lineage establishes Maturidi's authority
Consider why the biographer includes details about the piety and martyrdom of teachers. This reinforces the reliability of the transmission and the orthodoxy of the creed.
The chain is not just academic; it is a chain of righteous scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سمياة الماتريدي وأعماله
الذي يذكر أنه توفي عام 333 هـ ثم يضيف، وقيل: سنة ست وثلاثين. ودفن بسمرقند.
ثقافته
نقرأ في المصادر التي بين أيدينا أن الماتريدي تفقه في العلم على أئمة العلماء تنتهي إلى الإمام أبي حنيفة. ومن شيوخه في عصره الذين أخذوا العلم بدورهم عن أبي حنيفة. يذكر الكفوي أن الإمام الماتريدي تخرج بأبي نصر العياضي، وتفقها على أبي بكر أحمد الجوزجاني، عن أبي سليمان الجوزجاني، عن محمد، عن أبي حنيفة. ويقول الزبيدي: تخرج بالإمام أبي نصر العياضي الإمام أبو بكر أحمد بن اسحاق بن صالح الجوزجاني صاحب الفرق والتمييز ومن مشايخ الماتريدي محمد بن مقاتل الرازي قاضي الري... فأما أبو بكر الجوزجاني وأبو نصر العياضي ونصير بن يحيى فكلهم تفقهوا على الإمام أبي سليمان بن موسى بن سليمان الجوزجاني، وهو على الإمامين أبي يوسف ومحمد بن الحسن، وتفقه محمد بن مقاتل ونصير بن يحيى أيضاً على الإمامين أبي مطيع الحكم بن عبد الله البلخي وأبي مقاتل حفص بن مسلم السمرقندي، وأخذ محمد بن مقاتل أيضاً عن محمد بن الحسن، أربعتهم عن الإمام أبي حنيفة. أما أبو نصر العياضي أول شيوخه فهو أنصاري مثله، بن قيس بن سعد بن عبادة الأنصاري الخزرجي. كان من أهل العلم والجهاد فقد استشهد خلف أربعين رجلاً كلهم من أقران الماتريدي وهو يحارب الكفرة في بلاد الترك. ويذكر المؤرخون أنه لم يكن أحد يضاهيه في البلاد في علمه. يرجع نسبه إلى يحيى.
وورعه. وقد ورث ولداه الإمامان الكبيران أبو أحمد العياضي وأبو بكر العياضي عن أبيهما العلم والورع حتى قيل في حق ابنه أحمد: الدليل على صحة مذهب أبي حنيفة أن أبا بكر أحمد العياضي على مذهبه، ولو لم يكن ذلك مذهباً مختاراً لم يعتقده أبو أحمد العياضي رحمه الله.
ورغم أن أبا نصر العياضي كان شيخاً للماتريدي فإنه كان يجلس معه في حلقة أبي بكر أحمد الجوزجاني، فقد تخرجا معاً في حلقته. ويذكر الكفوي أن أبا بكر أحمد الجوزجاني كان عالماً جامعاً بين العلوم من الأصول والفروع وكان في أنواع العلوم في الذروة العالية. وكذلك كان يجلس الإمام أبو بكر تلميذه الإمام أبي نصر العياضي في حلقة شيخها الإمام أبي أحمد الجوزجاني سليمان الجوزجاني تلميذ محمد بن الحسن صاحب الإمام أبي حنيفة. ويذكر ابن النديم أن أبا سليمان الجوزجاني كان ورعاً ديناً فقيهاً محدثاً.
تلك هي مشيخة الصلاح والتقوى التي تخرج فيها الماتريدي. وقد عكفت هذه المشيخة على رواية الكتب المنسوبة للإمام أبي حنيفة ورسائله ووصاياه في أصول العقائد ودراستها. فكان الفقه الأكبر المنسوب لأبي حنيفة والرسالة والفقه الأبسط وكتاب العالم والمتعلم والوصية هي التعليقة التي يحملها فقهاء مذهب النعمان في أصول العقائد. وقد حملها الماتريدي ورواها عن شيوخه، ولكنها أخذت شكلاً آخر على يديه. كانت هذه المؤلفات بمثابة بيان لعقيدة أهل السنة.
His name is al-Maturidi and his works. He who mentions that he died in the year 333 AH then adds, and it was said: the year six and thirty. And he was buried in Samarkand. His education. We read in the sources that are in our hands that al-Maturidi studied jurisprudence (tafaqqaha) in knowledge under the imams of scholars ending with Imam Abu Hanifa. And among his teachers in his time who took knowledge in turn from Abu Hanifa. Al-Kafawi mentions that Imam al-Maturidi graduated under Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, and studied jurisprudence under Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, from Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, from Muhammad, from Abu Hanifa. And al-Zabidi says: Imam Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ishaq ibn Salih al-Juzjani, author of al-Furq wa al-Tamyiz, graduated under Imam Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, and among the teachers of al-Maturidi is Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, judge of Rayy... As for Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, and Nasir ibn Yahya, all of them studied jurisprudence under Imam Abu Sulayman ibn Musa ibn Sulayman al-Juzjani, and he (studied) under the two imams Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan; and Muhammad ibn Muqatil and Nasir ibn Yahya also studied jurisprudence under the two imams Abu Muti‘ al-Hakam ibn ‘Abd Allah al-Balkhi and Abu Muqatil Hafs ibn Muslim al-Samarqandi; and Muhammad ibn Muqatil also took from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan; all four of them (traced back) to Imam Abu Hanifa. As for Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, his first teacher, he was an Ansari like him, the son of Qays ibn Sa‘d ibn ‘Ubada al-Ansari al-Khazraji. He was a man of knowledge and jihad; he was martyred leaving behind forty men, all of them peers of al-Maturidi, while he was fighting the disbelievers in the land of the Turks. And the historians mention that there was no one who matched him in the land in his knowledge. His lineage goes back to Yahya. And his piety. And his two sons, the two great imams Abu Ahmad al-‘Iyadi and Abu Bakr al-‘Iyadi, inherited from their father knowledge and piety, until it was said concerning his son Ahmad: The proof of the correctness of the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is that Abu Bakr Ahmad al-‘Iyadi followed his madhhab; if it were not a chosen madhhab, Abu Ahmad al-‘Iyadi would not have believed it, may Allah have mercy on him. And despite the fact that Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi was a teacher of al-Maturidi, he used to sit with him in the study circle of Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani; indeed they both graduated together in his circle. And al-Kafawi mentions that Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani was a scholar comprehensive in the sciences of principles and branches, and he was at the highest peak in the types of sciences. And likewise, Imam Abu Bakr, the student of Imam Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, used to sit in the study circle of its teacher Imam Abu Ahmad al-Juzjani Sulayman al-Juzjani, the student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, the companion of Imam Abu Hanifa. And Ibn al-Nadim mentions that Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani was pious, religious, a jurist, a hadith scholar. Those are the teachers of righteousness and piety under whom al-Maturidi graduated. And this group of teachers devoted themselves to narrating the books attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, his letters, and his wills in the principles of creed and studying them. So al-Fiqh al-Akbar attributed to Abu Hanifa, and al-Risala, and al-Fiqh al-Absat, and Kitab al-‘Alim wa al-Muta‘allim, and al-Wasiyya are the commentary that the jurists of the madhhab of al-Nu‘man carry in the principles of creed. And al-Maturidi carried them and narrated them from his teachers, but they took another form at his hands. These works were like an exposition of the creed of Ahl al-Sunna.
Source pages p. 544

Commentary
This passage is a biographical narrative describing Imam al-Maturidi's teachers and the scholarly chain through which he received the Hanafi tradition. The author begins by stating that sources report al-Maturidi died in 333 AH, with an alternative date of 336 AH, and was buried in Samarkand. It then discusses his education, stating he studied under scholars whose chain goes back to Imam Abu Hanifa. The author names specific teachers: Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, and Muhammad ibn Muqatil al-Razi, among others. He traces the chains: Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi, and Nasir ibn Yahya all studied under Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, who studied under Abu Yusuf and Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, who were direct students of Abu Hanifa. Additionally, Muhammad ibn Muqatil and Nasir ibn Yahya studied under Abu Muti‘ and Abu Muqatil, and Muhammad ibn Muqatil also studied under Muhammad ibn al-Hasan. Thus the entire chain is connected to Abu Hanifa. The passage then highlights Abu Nasr al-‘Iyadi's noble lineage (Ansari) and his martyrdom in battle against the Turks. It notes his sons inherited his knowledge and piety, with a saying cited that Abu Bakr Ahmad al-‘Iyadi's adherence to Abu Hanifa's madhhab is proof of its correctness. Despite being a teacher, Abu Nasr sat in the same study circle as al-Maturidi under Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, indicating scholarly humility and shared learning. The passage praises Abu Bakr al-Juzjani as a comprehensive scholar. It then describes the chain of teachers as upright and pious, and states that this group devoted themselves to narrating and studying Abu Hanifa's creedal works: al-Fiqh al-Akbar, al-Risala, al-Fiqh al-Absat, Kitab al-‘Alim wa al-Muta‘allim, and al-Wasiyya. These texts became the foundation for Hanafi creed. Al-Maturidi transmitted these works from his teachers, but he gave them a new formulation which served as an exposition of Sunni creed. The passage thus establishes al-Maturidi's scholarly credentials and the doctrinal sources of his school.

Key Terms

سلسلة
شيخ
الفقه الأكبر
الوصية
عقيدة أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Maturidi independently invented his creed without prior tradition.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that al-Maturidi was part of an established chain of transmission from Abu Hanifa, and his theology is a systematization of the creedal works he received from his teachers.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Maturidi's theology is transmitted directly from Abu Hanifa through a chain of pious scholars, and he systematized the creedal works of the Hanafi school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to follow the truth, but have you ever traced your own beliefs back to their sources? This lesson shows that al-Maturidi's creed came through a chain of teachers. What is your chain? Who are the scholars you rely on for your faith, and how certain are you that they faithfully transmitted the teachings of the Salaf?
?
The teachers of al-Maturidi were not only knowledgeable but also righteous; some even died in battle. Do you see your own teachers – living or deceased – as people of piety whose lives demand that you take their teaching seriously? Or do you treat learning aqeedah as a mere academic exercise, without letting it transform your character? This lesson confronts you: the creed is not a set of statements; it is a living tradition passed through lives of sacrifice. Will you let it change you?
?
Al-Maturidi did not invent anything new; he systematized what was already given. In your own life, do you tend to seek novel spiritual experiences or innovative opinions, rather than humbly adhering to the established transmitted teachings? This lesson calls you to check your heart: are you content to be a follower of the way of the Prophet (as transmitted through the scholars) or do you secretly desire to be original, to stand out? Repent of any pride and embrace the tradition that was defended with blood.

Maturidi's Scholarly Lineage and Transmission of Hanafi Creed
Traces Maturidi's teachers and the transmission of Hanafi creedal works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the chain of teachers through which Imam al-Maturidi inherited the Hanafi creedal tradition and the key works that formed the basis of his theological formulation.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's creed is rooted in a chain of pious scholars transmitting Abu Hanifa's works.

This passage situates Imam al-Maturidi within a specific scholarly lineage, tracing his teachers and their teachers back to the companions of Abu Hanifa. It highlights how the transmission of key creedal texts like al-Fiqh al-Akbar shaped the Hanafi-Maturidi tradition. Let us explore this chain and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its historical narrative. Then read the English translation to understand the details.
Pay attention to the names and relationships.
2
Identify the scholarly chain
Trace the teacher-student connections: Abu Hanifa → Muhammad ibn al-Hasan → Abu Ahmad al-Juzjani → Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani → Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi → al-Maturidi.
Notice that Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi was both a teacher and a fellow student of al-Maturidi.
3
Note the key creedal works
The passage lists five foundational works: al-Fiqh al-Akbar, al-Risala, al-Fiqh al-Absat, Kitab al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim, and al-Wasiyya.
These texts were the core of Hanafi creed before Maturidi's systematization.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider why the author includes this lineage: it establishes the authenticity and authority of Maturidi's theological project as a continuation of Abu Hanifa's legacy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة: وقد ورث ولداه الإمامان الكبيران أبو أحمد العياضي وأبو بكر العياضي عن أبيها العلم والورع حتى قيل في حق ابنه أحمد: الدليل على صحة مذهب أبي حنيفة أن أبا بكر أحمد العياضي على مذهبه، ولو لم يكن ذلك مذهبا مختارا لم يعتقده أبو أحمد العياضي رحمه الله. ورغم أن أبا نصر العياضي كان شيخا للماتريدي فإنه كان يجلس معه في حلقة أبي بكر أحمد الجوزجاني، فقد تخرجا معا في حلقته. ويذكر الكفوي أن أبا بكر أحمد الجوزجاني كان عالما جامعا بين العلوم من الأصول والفروع وكان في أنواع العلوم في الذروة العالية. وكذلك كان يجلس الإمام أبو بكر تلميذه الإمام أبي نصر العياضي في حلقة شيخها الإمام أبي أحمد الجوزجاني سليمان الجوزجاني تلميذ محمد بن الحسن صاحب الإمام أبي حنيفة. ويذكر ابن النديم أن أبا سليمان الجوزجاني كان ورعا دينا فقيها محدثا. تلك هي مشيخة الصلاح والتقوى التي تخرج فيها الماتريدي. وقد عكفت هذه المشيخة على رواية الكتب المنسوبة للإمام أبي حنيفة ورسائله ووصاياه في أصول العقائد ودراستها. فكان الفقه الأكبر المنسوب لأبي حنيفة والرسالة والفقه الأبسط وكتاب العالم والمتعلم والوصية هي التعليقة التي يحملها فقهاء مذهب النعمان في أصول العقائد. وقد حملها الماتريدي ورواها عن شيوخه، ولكنها أخذت شكلا آخر على يديه كانت هذه المؤلفات بمثابة بيان لعقيدة أهل السنة.
Introduction: And his two sons, the two great imams Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi and Abu Bakr al-'Iyadi, inherited from their father knowledge and piety, such that it was said regarding his son Ahmad: 'The proof of the correctness of the madhhab of Abu Hanifa is that Abu Bakr Ahmad al-'Iyadi followed his madhhab; if it were not a chosen madhhab, Abu Ahmad al-'Iyadi would not have believed in it, may Allah have mercy on him.' And although Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi was a teacher of al-Maturidi, he used to sit with him in the study circle of Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, as they both graduated from his circle. Al-Kafawi mentions that Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani was a scholar encompassing both the principles and the branches and was at the highest peak in all types of sciences. Likewise, Imam Abu Bakr (al-Maturidi), the student of Imam Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, used to sit in the study circle of its shaykh, Imam Abu Ahmad al-Juzjani Sulayman al-Juzjani, the student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, the companion of Imam Abu Hanifa. Ibn al-Nadim mentions that Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani was pious, religious, a jurist, and a hadith scholar. That is the shaykhly group of righteousness and piety in which al-Maturidi was educated. This shaykhly group devoted itself to narrating the books attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, his epistles, and his wills regarding the principles of beliefs, and to studying them. So 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar' attributed to Abu Hanifa, 'al-Risala', 'al-Fiqh al-Absat', 'Kitab al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim', and 'al-Wasiyya' are the collection that the jurists of the madhhab of al-Nu'man (Abu Hanifa) carry regarding the principles of beliefs. Al-Maturidi carried them and narrated them from his teachers, but they took another form at his hands, and these works became like an exposition of the creed of Ahl al-Sunna.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage provides a historical account of the scholarly environment in which Imam al-Maturidi was raised. It begins by highlighting the piety and knowledge of the two sons of a certain scholar (likely al-'Iyadi), using their adherence to Abu Hanifa's madhhab as evidence for the soundness of that madhhab. It then notes that even though Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi was a teacher of al-Maturidi, both attended the same study circle of Abu Bakr Ahmad al-Juzjani, indicating a shared scholarly lineage. The passage quotes al-Kafawi praising al-Juzjani as a comprehensive scholar of both usul and furu'. It further describes the chain: Imam Abu Bakr (al-Maturidi) sat in the circle of his teacher Abu Nasr al-'Iyadi, who sat in the circle of Abu Ahmad al-Juzjani, who was a student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan (al-Shaybani), a companion of Abu Hanifa. Ibn al-Nadim attests to the piety and expertise of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani as a faqih and muhaddith. The passage then summarizes that this shaykhly group was characterized by righteousness and piety, and they focused on narrating and studying Abu Hanifa's works on creed, specifically listing 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar', 'al-Risala', 'al-Fiqh al-Absat', 'Kitab al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim', and 'al-Wasiyya'. These texts constituted the core creedal corpus for Hanafi jurists. Al-Maturidi transmitted these works from his teachers, but later reshaped them into a more systematic exposition of Ahl al-Sunna creed. The passage thus establishes the authenticity and chain of transmission of the Hanafi creedal tradition that al-Maturidi inherited.

أصول العقائد
الفقه الأكبر

Misconception: Imam al-Maturidi developed his theology independently without relying on Abu Hanifa.
Correction: This passage shows that al-Maturidi was part of a chain transmitting Abu Hanifa's creedal works, and his work is a systematization of that tradition.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Maturidi's theological work is a continuation and systematization of the creed of Abu Hanifa, transmitted through a chain of pious scholars.

Maturidi's Scholarly Defense of the Creed
Overview of Maturidi's scholarly output and refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi's writings demonstrate his lifelong commitment to defending the Sunni creed and his mastery of multiple Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Maturidi's books reveal a lifetime dedicated to defending the creed.

The titles of Maturidi's books are not random; they reflect a clear mission. This passage shows that he devoted his life to refuting deviant groups and also possessed deep knowledge across theology, jurisprudence, and exegesis. Let's explore his scholarly legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the central claim
The passage opens by stating that the book titles prove Maturidi's life mission. Notice the key phrase 'كرس حياته للدفاع عن العقيدة'.
This sets the theme for all his works.
2
Identify the groups he refutes
The passage lists refutations against the Mu'tazila, specifically al-Ka'bi, then the Qaramita and Rawafid. Count the works mentioned for each.
Al-Ka'bi was a prominent Mu'tazili scholar.
3
Recognize his breadth of scholarship
Beyond refutations, Maturidi wrote in usul al-fiqh, tafsir, and fiqh. Notice the titles of his tafsir work.
This shows he was not just a theologian.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تدل عناوين الكتب التي يذكرها المؤرخون للماتريدي على أنه كرس حياته للدفاع عن العقيدة والرد على المنحرفين عن السنة، كما تدل أيضاً على سعة معارفه وإلمامه بعلوم الدين من فقه وأصول وكلام وتفسير. فقد رد على المعتزلة ونقض أصولهم الخمسة وتعقب الكعبي بالذات، إمام أهل الأرض عند المعتزلة ومعاصر الماتريدي فنقض آراءه ومؤلفاته. ففي الرد على المعتزلة صنف بيان وهم المعتزلة، رد الأصول الخمسة لأبي محمد الباهلي. وفي نقض آراء الكعبي ومؤلفاته صنف رد أوائل الأدلة للكعبي، رد تهذيب الجدل للكعبي، رد وعيد الفساق للكعبي. وكذلك رد على القرامطة والروافض وصنف في ذلك الرد على أصول القرامطة، رد كتاب الإمامة لبعض الروافض. أما مؤلفاته في أصول الفقه: الشرائع، وكتاب الجدل. وهو فوق ذلك يكتب في التفسير والكلام على طريقة أهل السنة، كما يصنف في الفقه. فيسمى كتابه في التفسير تأويلات أهل السنة أو التأويلات الماتريدية في بيان أصول أهل السنة وأصول التوحيد.
The titles of the books that historians mention for al-Maturidi indicate that he devoted his life to defending the creed and refuting those who deviate from the Sunnah, and they also indicate the breadth of his knowledge and his mastery of the religious sciences: jurisprudence, principles, theology, and exegesis. He refuted the Mu'tazila and invalidated their five principles, and specifically pursued al-Ka'bi, the imam of the people of the earth according to the Mu'tazila and a contemporary of al-Maturidi, thus refuting his views and works. In refuting the Mu'tazila he composed 'Bayan Wahm al-Mu'tazila' and 'Rad al-Usul al-Khamsa' by Abu Muhammad al-Bahili. And in refuting the views and works of al-Ka'bi he composed 'Rad Awa'il al-Adilla' for al-Ka'bi, 'Rad Tahdhib al-Jadal' for al-Ka'bi, and 'Rad Wa'id al-Fussaq' for al-Ka'bi. He also refuted the Qaramita and the Rawafid, composing 'Rad ala Usul al-Qaramita' and 'Rad Kitab al-Imama' for some of the Rawafid. As for his works in the principles of jurisprudence: 'al-Shara'i' and 'Kitab al-Jadal'. And beyond that he wrote in exegesis and theology according the method of Ahl al-Sunna, just as he composed in jurisprudence. He called his book on exegesis 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunna' or 'al-Ta'wilat al-Maturidiyya fi Bayan Usul Ahl al-Sunna wa Usul al-Tawhid'.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a biographical description of Imam Maturidi's scholarly activity, specifically his refutations and works. It begins by stating that the titles of his books show he dedicated his life to defending the creed and refuting deviation. It then details his refutations: against the Mu'tazila, he invalidated their five principles and specifically targeted al-Ka'bi; he wrote three works against al-Ka'bi. He also refuted the Qaramita and Rawafid. The passage then lists his works in usul al-fiqh and mentions his tafsir, which he named to reflect its focus on the principles of Ahl al-Sunna and tawhid.

Praise for Maturidi's Tafsir and Its Characteristics
Haji Khalifa's praise and description of Maturidi's tafsir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Haji Khalifa praised Maturidi's tafsir and what makes it distinctive in clarity and preservation.

Core Idea
Maturidi's tafsir is praised for its unparalleled clarity and ease among his works.

Haji Khalifa, the famous Ottoman bibliographer, offers remarkable praise for Maturidi's Quranic commentary. His description highlights the tafsir's accessibility and depth, and notes that it remains one of the few Maturidi works to survive. Let's examine his words and understand why this tafsir holds such a special place.

Guided Path
1
Read Haji Khalifa's praise
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the emphatic language: 'no other book equals it'.
Haji Khalifa was a well-known bibliographer.
2
Identify key characteristics
Look for reasons the tafsir is praised: uniqueness, ease of use, clarity. Find where these are mentioned.
3
Contrast with al-Razi's method
The passage compares Maturidi's style to that of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. Understand why the author prefers Maturidi's approach.
Al-Razi's tafsir is known for extensive digressions.
4
Note surviving and misattributed works
The passage lists which of Maturidi's works survive and which are falsely attributed to him. This is important for historical accuracy.
Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar is often misattributed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصف حاجي خليفة هذا الكتاب فيقول: وهو كتاب لا يوازيه فيه كتاب، بل لا يدانيه شيء من تصانيف من سبقه في ذلك الفن. ويذكر حاجي خليفة أيضاً أنه أسهل تناولا من كتبه الأخرى ولذلك أخذ منه أصحاب الماتريدي وعولوا عليه. والحق أن التأويلات أسهل تناولا من التوحيد، وأوضح وأيسر. فهو يسوق تفسير الآية في وضوح ويسر، ويستخرج منها كل ما يستفاد بدون أن يغرقنا في متاهات من التفاريع كما يفعل فخر الدين الرازي مثلاً في تفسيره. وهذا التفسير يشهد بسعة علم الماتريدي وغزارة معارفه في علوم الدين واللغة. ومن حسن الحظ قد حفظ لنا الزمن هذا التفسير كما حفظ لنا كتاب التوحيد وكتاب المقالات أما كتبه الأخرى فقد ضاعت كلها. وينسب إليه خطأ شرح الفقه الأكبر وشرح الإبانة والعقيدة الماتريدية.
Haji Khalifa describes this book, saying: 'It is a book that no other book equals, indeed nothing from the works of those before him in that art approaches it.' Haji Khalifa also mentions that it is easier to handle than his other books, and therefore the companions of al-Maturidi took from it and relied on it. The truth is that 'al-Ta'wilat' is easier to handle than 'al-Tawhid', clearer and simpler. He presents the interpretation of the verse with clarity and ease, and extracts from it everything that can be benefited without drowning us in labyrinths of branches as Fakhr al-Din al-Razi does for example in his tafsir. This tafsir bears witness to the breadth of al-Maturidi's knowledge and the abundance of his expertise in the religious and linguistic sciences. Fortunately, time has preserved for us this tafsir as it preserved for us the books 'al-Tawhid' and 'al-Maqalat'; as for his other books, all of them have been lost. And it is falsely attributed to him: Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar, Sharh al-Ibana, and al-Aqida al-Maturidiyya.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a description and praise of Maturidi's tafsir, 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunna', by the bibliographer Haji Khalifa. It begins with Haji Khalifa's statement that the book is unparalleled and easier than Maturidi's other works. The author then adds that the tafsir is indeed easier than 'Kitab al-Tawhid' and clearer. He describes Maturidi's method: he explains verses with clarity without excessive branching, unlike al-Razi. The passage concludes by noting that this tafsir, along with 'Kitab al-Tawhid' and 'al-Maqalat', have survived, while other works are lost, and lists three works incorrectly attributed to Maturidi.

التأويلات

شرح الفقه الأكبر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar, Sharh al-Ibana, and al-Aqida al-Maturidiyya are authentic works of Imam Maturidi.
Correction: The passage states these three books are falsely attributed to him.

Key Takeaway

The Two Heads of Sunni Kalam
Tashkopru Zadeh introduces the two heads of Ahl al-Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical Sunni scholars identified the two main theological schools (Ash'ari and Maturidi) and their association with legal schools and regions.

Core Idea
Sunni theology has two founding masters: one Hanafi, one Shafi'i.

This passage from Tashkopru Zadeh's biographical work presents the two great figures of Sunni kalam. It explains their legal school affiliations and notes that al-Ash'ari became more widespread in key regions. Understanding this sets the stage for appreciating the historical and legal contexts of Maturidi and Ash'ari theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read Tashkopru Zadeh's statement and the subsequent gloss by al-Kastali. Notice how he introduces the two figures and their affiliations.
The passage is short but packed with information about legal school ties and geographical spread.
2
Identify the two heads and their legal schools
Identify that al-Maturidi is Hanafi and al-Ash'ari is Shafi'i. Consider why legal school affiliation might matter for theological tradition.
This shows that theological schools were often linked to legal schools in early Islam.
3
Note the regional prevalence
From al-Kastali's gloss, observe that al-Ash'ari is more famous in Khurasan, Iraq, and Syria. Think about what this tells us about the spread of Ash'arism.
This geographical note helps explain why Ash'arism became more dominant in many regions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقول طاش كوبري زاده: ثم اعلم أن رئيس أهل السنة والجماعة في علم الكلام رجلان: أحدهما حنفي والآخر شافعي، أما الحنفي فهو أبو منصور محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي إمام الهدى ورئيس السنة، وأما الآخر الشافعي فهو شيخ إمام المتكلمين وناصر سنة سيد المرسلين والذاب عن الدين والساعي في حفظ عقائد المسلمين أبو الحسن الأشعري البصري. وجاء في حاشية المولى مصلح الدين مصطفى الكستلي على شرح العقائد النسفية للتفتازاني: المشهور من أهل السنة في ديار خراسان والعراق والشام وأكثر.
Tashkopru Zadeh says: 'Then know that the head of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a in the science of kalam are two men: one Hanafi and the other Shafi'i. As for the Hanafi, he is Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi, the imam of guidance and the head of the Sunnah. As for the other, the Shafi'i, he is the shaykh, the imam of the theologians, the supporter of the Sunnah of the Master of Messengers, the defender of the religion, the one striving in preserving the beliefs of Muslims, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari al-Basri.' And it came in the gloss of al-Mawla Muslih al-Din Mustafa al-Kastali on Sharh al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya of al-Taftazani: 'The well-known of Ahl al-Sunna in the lands of Khurasan, Iraq, Syria, and most of...'
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from Tashkopru Zadeh's biographical work comparing the two founders of the Sunni theological schools. It presents both Maturidi and Ash'ari as heads of Ahl al-Sunna, but distinguishes them by regional affiliation: Maturidi is Hanafi, Ash'ari is Shafi'i. Then it cites the gloss of al-Kastali, which notes that Ash'ari is more famous in Khurasan, Iraq, Syria, and most regions. This highlights the historical spread of Ash'arism versus Maturidism. The passage thus provides a summary of the respective prominence of the two schools.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni theological tradition is led by two figures: al-Maturidi (Hanafi) and al-Ash'ari (Shafi'i), with Ash'ari more widespread.

Maturidi's Tafsir and Surviving Works
Praise of Maturidi's Tafsir and listing of his works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the significance of Imam al-Maturidi's Tafsir (al-Ta'wilat) and know which of his works have survived and which are falsely attributed to him.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi's Tafsir is unmatched, and three major works survive, but not all attributions are genuine.

This passage highlights the exceptional quality of al-Maturidi's Quranic commentary (al-Ta'wilat) as praised by scholars like Haji Khalifa. It also clarifies which works are authentically his and which are falsely attributed, helping us appreciate his legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it, then read the English translation. Let the author's praise and listing come through.
Notice the comparison with al-Razi's tafsir.
2
Identify the key works mentioned
List the works that are said to have survived (al-Ta'wilat, Kitab al-Tawhid, Kitab al-Maqalat) and those falsely attributed (Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar, Sharh al-Ibana, al-Aqida al-Maturidiyya).
Remember that some works are lost.
3
Reflect on why the Tafsir is praised
The passage says it is easier and clearer than his other works, and it extracts benefits without unnecessary complexities. Compare this to the style of al-Razi mentioned.
This shows Maturidi's depth and clarity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الماتريدي والأشعري
بل لا يدانيه شيء من تصانيف من سبقه في ذلك الفن المؤرخون الذين كتبوا في طبقات ومع ذلك يهمله. ويذكر حاجي خليفة أيضاً أنه أسهل تناولا من كتبه الأخرى ولذلك أخذ منه أصحاب الماتريدي وعولوا عليه. والحق أن التأويلات، أسهل تناولا من التوحيد، وأوضح وأيسر. فهو يسوق تفسير الآية في وضوح ويسر، ويستخرج منها كل ما يستفاد بدون أن يغرقنا في متاهات من التفاريع كما يفعل فخر الدين الرازي مثلاً في تفسيره. وهذا التفسير يشهد بسعة علم الحظ الماتريدي وغزارة معارفه في علوم الدين واللغة. ومن حسن قد حفظ لنا الزمن هذا التفسير كما حفظ لنا كتاب التوحيد وكتاب المقالات أما كتبه الأخرى فقد ضاعت كلها. ويُنسب إليه خطأ شرح الفقه الأكبر وشرح الإبانة والعقيدة الماتريدية.
Al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari. Rather, nothing from the compositions of those who preceded him in that art [of tafsir] among the historians who wrote in layers equals it, yet he is neglected. Haji Khalifa also mentions that it is easier in handling than his other books, and therefore the followers of al-Maturidi took from it and relied upon it. The truth is that al-Ta'wilat (The Interpretations) is easier in handling than al-Tawhid (The Book of Monotheism), and clearer and simpler. He presents the interpretation of the verse with clarity and ease, and extracts from it everything that can be benefited without drowning us in labyrinths of divisions as Fakhr al-Din al-Razi does, for example, in his tafsir. This tafsir attests to the vastness of al-Maturidi's learning and the abundance of his knowledge in the religious sciences and language. Fortunately, time has preserved for us this tafsir, just as it preserved for us Kitab al-Tawhid and Kitab al-Maqalat (The Book of Doctrines); as for his other books, they have all been lost. And mistakenly attributed to him are Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar (Commentary on the Greater Jurisprudence), Sharh al-Ibana (Commentary on the Clarification), and al-Aqida al-Maturidiyya (The Maturidite Creed).
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a description and evaluation of Imam al-Maturidi's works. It begins by stating that his tafsir (Qur'an commentary) is unmatched by any earlier work in that field, yet he is neglected by historians. Haji Khalifa notes that this tafsir is easier to handle than al-Maturidi's other books, so his followers relied on it. The passage then clarifies that his book 'al-Ta'wilat' (The Interpretations) is actually easier and clearer than his 'Kitab al-Tawhid'. The author praises the tafsir for presenting verses with clarity and extracting all benefits without getting lost in unnecessary elaborations, unlike al-Razi's tafsir. It testifies to al-Maturidi's vast knowledge. Fortunately, this tafsir along with 'Kitab al-Tawhid' and 'Kitab al-Maqalat' have survived, while all his other works are lost. The passage ends by noting that some works are falsely attributed to him, namely a commentary on 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar', a commentary on 'al-Ibana', and 'al-Aqida al-Maturidiyya'.

Key Terms
التأويلات
التوحيد
المقالات
شرح الفقه الأكبر
شرح الإبانة
العقيدة الماتريدية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All of al-Maturidi's works are lost.
Correction: Three major works survive: al-Ta'wilat, Kitab al-Tawhid, and Kitab al-Maqalat. However, some works are falsely attributed to him.

Checkpoint
Which work of al-Maturidi does the passage describe as easier and clearer than his Kitab al-Tawhid?

B) al-Ta'wilat
C) Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar
D) Sharh al-Ibana

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Maturidi's Tafsir (al-Ta'wilat) is a masterpiece of clarity, and three of his works survive, but some attributed works are not genuine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage says al-Maturidi's tafsir is 'unmatched' yet he is 'neglected'. Are you also neglecting great works of Islamic scholarship simply because they are not widely promoted? What one step will you take this week to explore al-Maturidi's tafsir?
?
You are told that some works are 'mistakenly attributed' to al-Maturidi. How diligently do you verify the sources of your own Islamic knowledge? Commit to checking the chain of attribution for one Islamic text you currently rely on.
?
Al-Maturidi's tafsir extracts 'everything that can be benefited' from each verse. When you read the Quran, do you settle for shallow understanding, or do you strive to extract all possible benefits? What change will you make in your Quran study habits starting today?

The Two Leaders of Ahl al-Sunna
Quotes establishing Maturidi and Ash'ari as leaders with regional distribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ahl al-Sunna has two recognized chiefs in kalam: Abu Mansur al-Maturidi and Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, and their schools are geographically distributed.

Core Idea
Sunni kalam has two founding imams: al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari.

This passage introduces the two great figures who define Sunni theological methodology. Using quotes from later scholars, it establishes their leadership and the regions where their schools predominated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to identify the two imams and their titles as given by Tashkopruzade.
Notice the elaborate praise for al-Maturidi.
2
Note the geographical distribution
The Kastali quote assigns Ash'aris to Khurasan, Iraq, Syria, and most regions, while Maturidis are in Transoxiana.
This shows the historical spread of each school.
3
Understand the inclusive definition
Al-Zabidi states that 'Ahl al-Sunna' absolutely refers to both Ash'aris and Maturidis.
This affirms both schools as orthodox.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- الماتريدي والاشعري
تقديم الأشعري على الماتريدي
يقول طاش کوپری زاده : ثم اعلم أن رئيس أهل السنة والجماعة في علم الكلام رجلان : أحدهما حنفي والآخر شافعي، أما الحنفي فهو أبو منصور محمد بن محمد بن محمود الماتريدي إمام الهدى ورئيس الجماعة إمام المتكلمين وناصر سنة سيد المرسلين والذاب عن الدين والساعي في حفظ عقائد المسلمين، وأما الآخر الشافعي فهو شيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري البصري ....
وجاء في حاشية المولى مصلح الدين مصطفى الكستلي على شرح العقائد النسفية للتفتازاني : المشهور من أهل السنة في ديار خراسان والعراق والشام وأكثر الأمصار هم الأشاعرة أصحاب أبي الحسن علي بن اسماعيل بن سالم بن سالم بن اسماعيل بن عبد الله بن بلال أبي برده بن أبي موسى الأشعري صاحب رسول الله، وفي ديار ما وراء النهر الماتريدية أصحاب أبي منصور الماتريدي عليه السلام. نصر العياضي تلميذ أبي بكر الجوزجاني صاحب أبي سليمان الجوزجاني تلميذ أبي تلميذ محمد بن الحسن الشيباني من أصحاب الإمام أبي حنيفة ١٤ ويقول الزبيدي : إذا أطلق أهل السنة والجماعة فالمراد بهم الأشاعرة والماتريدية ٢٠ أن هذه النصوص التي قدمناها توضح أن الأشعري والماتريدي هما علما أهل السنة والجماعة فإنه وجد دائماً ميل للتقليل من شأن الماتريدي وتقديم الأشعري على أنه علم الإسلام المدافع عن العقيدة ضد المبتدعة المنحرفين عن أن الماتريدي كان أسبق من الأشعري إلى السنة ومذاهب السلف. هذا مع نصرة مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة، كما نشأ على السنة ومات عليها، بينما نشأ الأشعري على الاعتزال وظل معتزلياً إلى سن الأربعين.
Al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari. Preference of al-Ash'ari over al-Maturidi. Tashkopruzade said: Then know that the chief of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a in the science of kalam are two men: one Hanafi and the other Shafi'i. As for the Hanafi, he is Abu Mansur Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Maturidi, the Imam of Guidance, the Chief of the Community, the Imam of Theologians, the Supporter of the Sunnah of the Master of Messengers, the Defender of the Religion, the Striver in Preserving the Creeds of the Muslims. As for the other, the Shafi'i, he is Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari al-Basri... It came in the marginalia of al-Mawla Muslih al-Din Mustafa al-Kastali on the commentary on al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya by al-Taftazani: The well-known among Ahl al-Sunna in the lands of Khurasan, Iraq, Syria, and most of the regions are the Ash'aris, the followers of Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Salim ibn Salim ibn Isma'il ibn Abdullah ibn Bilal Abi Burda ibn Abi Musa al-Ash'ari, the Companion of the Messenger of God. And in the lands of Transoxiana are the Maturidis, the followers of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, peace be upon him. Nasr al-Ayadi, student of Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, the companion of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, student of Abu student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, one of the companions of Imam Abu Hanifa. And al-Zabidi says: If Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a are mentioned absolutely, what is meant by them are the Ash'aris and the Maturidis. That these texts which we have presented clarify that al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are the two scholars of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, for there has always been a tendency to belittle the status of al-Maturidi and to give precedence to al-Ash'ari as the scholar of Islam who defended the creed against the innovators, deviating from the fact that al-Maturidi was earlier than al-Ash'ari in [adhering to] the Sunnah and the ways of the Salaf. This is alongside his supporting the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, as he grew up on the Sunnah and died upon it, while al-Ash'ari grew up on Mu'tazilism and remained a Mu'tazili until the age of forty.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of scholarly quotations and commentary establishing al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari as the two great imams of Ahl al-Sunna in kalam, but with an argument that al-Maturidi actually holds precedence and was always on the Sunnah. It begins with a quote from Tashkopruzade naming the two leaders: the Hanafi al-Maturidi and the Shafi'i al-Ash'ari, with eloquent titles for each. Then a quote from al-Kastali's marginalia on al-Taftazani's commentary describes the geographical distribution of the two schools: Ash'aris in Khurasan, Iraq, Syria, etc., and Maturidis in Transoxiana. The chain of transmission is traced back to Imam Abu Hanifa through several links, though the text has a broken phrase 'talmidh Abi talmidh'. Then al-Zabidi is quoted stating that the term Ahl al-Sunna refers to both Ash'aris and Maturidis. The author then comments that despite these texts making it clear that both are scholars of Ahl al-Sunna, there is a tendency to belittle al-Maturidi and give undue preference to al-Ash'ari. The author argues that al-Maturidi was earlier in adhering to the Sunnah and the ways of the Salaf, and he supported the Sunni madhhab throughout his life, growing up on the Sunnah and dying upon it. In contrast, al-Ash'ari grew up as a Mu'tazili and remained so until age forty. Thus al-Maturidi's adherence to orthodoxy was continuous and preceded al-Ash'ari's conversion.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
الماتريدي
الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Zabidi, what is meant by 'Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a'?
A) Only Ash'aris
B) Only Maturidis
C) Both Ash'aris and Maturidis
D) Only Salafis

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a includes two recognized theological schools: the Ash'ari and the Maturidi, each with its own founding imam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Maturidi's Precedence over Ash'ari
Argument for Maturidi's precedence in adherence to Sunnah over Ash'ari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that Abu Mansur al-Maturidi adhered to the Sunnah continuously and preceded al-Ash'ari, who was a Mu'tazili until age forty.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi was always on the Sunnah, while al-Ash'ari converted later.

After establishing both as leaders, the author makes a critical comparative point: al-Maturidi grew up on the Sunnah and died upon it, whereas al-Ash'ari was a Mu'tazili for the first forty years of his life. This challenges any tendency to diminish al-Maturidi's role.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the Arabic and translation to see the author's claim about the two imams' backgrounds.
Pay attention to the contrast introduced by 'بينما' (while).
2
Compare their beginnings
Al-Maturidi grew up on the Sunnah and died upon it, while al-Ash'ari grew up as a Mu'tazili and remained so until forty.
This highlights al-Maturidi's consistent orthodoxy.
3
Reflect on the implication
The author argues that al-Maturidi was earlier in adhering to the Sunnah, countering the tendency to prefer al-Ash'ari.

This passage is a compilation of scholarly quotations and commentary establishing al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari as the two great imams of Ahl al-Sunna in kalam, but with an argument that al-Maturidi actually holds precedence and was always on the Sunnah. It begins with a quote from Tashkopruzade naming the two leaders: the Hanafi al-Maturidi and the Shafi'i al-Ash'ari, with eloquent titles for each. Then a quote from al-Kastali's marginalia on al-Taftazani's commentary describes the geographical distribution of the two schools: Ash'aris in Khurasan, Iraq, Syria, etc., and Maturidis in Transoxiana. The chain of transmission is traced back to Imam Abu Hanifa through several links, though the text has a broken phrase 'talmidh Abi talmidh'. Then al-Zabidi is quoted stating that the term Ahl al-Sunna refers to both Ash'aris and Maturidis. The author then comments that despite these texts making it clear that both are scholars of Ahl al-Sunna, there is a tendency to belittle al-Maturidi and give undue preference to al-Ash'ari. The author argues that al-Maturidi was earlier in adhering to the Sunnah and the ways of the Salaf, and he supported the Sunni madhhab throughout his life, growing up on the Sunnah and dying upon it. In contrast, al-Ash'ari grew up as a Mu'tazili and remained so until age forty. Thus al-Maturidi's adherence to orthodoxy was continuous and preceded al-Ash'ari's conversion.

السلف
الماتريدي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari is the sole founder of Sunni kalam.
Correction: Al-Maturidi was equally a leader and was actually earlier in consistently following the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi's lifelong adherence to the Sunnah gives him precedence over al-Ash'ari, who converted from Mu'tazilism at age forty.

The Neglect of al-Maturidi by Historians
Describes the neglect of Maturidi by medieval historians compared to Ash'ari

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Maturidi was neglected by medieval historians compared to al-Ash'ari, and the significance of this omission.

Core Idea
Al-Maturidi was ignored by major biographers despite his contemporary Tahawi acknowledging him.

This passage highlights a curious historical phenomenon: despite his immense influence, Imam al-Maturidi was overlooked by many medieval historians. By examining specific examples, we see a pattern of neglect that contrasts with the recognition given to his counterpart, al-Ash'ari. Let's explore these textual clues.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Get a feel for the author's argument.
Notice the key names and the contrast between Ibn al-Nadim and al-Tahawi.
2
Analyze the contrast
Focus on the example: Ibn al-Nadim (died <50 years after Maturidi) did not mention him, while al-Tahawi (a near contemporary) did. Why might this be significant?
Al-Tahawi was a Hanafi scholar like Maturidi, Ibn al-Nadim was a bibliographer.
3
List the omitted historians
Identify the four historians listed as omitting Maturidi: Ibn Khallikan, Ibn al-Imad, al-Safadi, and the author of Fawat al-Wafayat. Consider what this pattern suggests.
These are major biographical dictionary authors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالرغم من ويبدو هذا الميل نحو التقليل من شأن الماتريدي في إهمال كثير من المؤرخين له، محاضر لم يذكره ابن النديم (م ٣٧٩ هـ / ٩٨٧ م) الذي توفي بعده بأقل من خمسين عاماً، بينما يذكر الإمام الطحاوي (م ٣٢١ هـ / ٩٣٣ م) الماتريدي وشيخ الأحناف وإمام أهل السنة في مصر كما يذكر الأشعري. ولم يترجم له ابن خلكان ولا ابن العماد ولا الصفدي ولا صاحب فوات الوفيات.
Despite and it appears this tendency toward belittling the status of al-Maturidi in the neglect of many historians for him, an instance: Ibn al-Nadim (d. 379 AH / 987 CE), who died less than fifty years after him, did not mention him, while Imam al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH / 933 CE) mentions al-Maturidi and the Shaykh of the Hanafis and the Imam of Ahl al-Sunna in Egypt just as he mentions al-Ash'ari. And Ibn Khallikan, Ibn al-Imad, al-Safadi, and the author of Fawat al-Wafayat did not write a biography for him.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a demonstration of the neglect that al-Maturidi suffered at the hands of major historians. The author states that there is a tendency to belittle al-Maturidi's status, as seen in the fact that many historians ignored him. As an example, Ibn al-Nadim (who died less than fifty years after al-Maturidi) did not mention him in his famous work al-Fihrist, whereas Imam al-Tahawi, who lived earlier, did mention both al-Maturidi and al-Ash'ari, referring to al-Maturidi as the Shaykh of the Hanafis and the Imam of Ahl al-Sunna in Egypt. The passage then lists other historians who omitted al-Maturidi from their biographical dictionaries: Ibn Khallikan (author of Wafayat al-A'yan), Ibn al-Imad (author of Shadharat al-Dhahab), al-Safadi (author of al-Wafi bi al-Wafayat), and the author of Fawat al-Wafayat (Ibn Shakir al-Kutubi). This selective omission shows a bias against al-Maturidi, despite his importance.

Key Terms
ابن النديم
الطحاوي
ابن خلكان
ابن العماد
الصفدي
فوات الوفيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Maturidi was historically obscure and unknown in his own time.
Correction: The passage shows that his contemporary al-Tahawi knew and respected him, calling him 'Shaykh of the Hanafis' and 'Imam of Ahl al-Sunna'. His omission by later historians does not reflect his contemporary standing but rather a later bias.

Checkpoint

B) Ibn al-Nadim
C) Ibn Khallikan
D) al-Safadi

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi's neglect by major biographers was not due to obscurity in his own time, but a later scholarly bias.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Maturidi was omitted by many historians despite being recognized by his contemporaries. Is there anyone in your life—a teacher, a friend, or a truth—that you have neglected because it was unpopular or unnoticed by others? How will you correct that neglect?
?
If later historians could omit a great imam due to bias, what does that say about your own sources of knowledge? Are you willing to seek truth beyond the famous names and books? Commit to one concrete step to broaden your sources this week.

The Historical Neglect of Imam al-Maturidi
Discusses the historical bias and neglect of Imam al-Maturidi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence of historical bias against Imam al-Maturidi and the neglect shown by historians and even his own followers.

Core Idea
Despite his foundational role, Imam al-Maturidi was unjustly overshadowed by al-Ash'ari.

This passage explores a puzzling phenomenon: while Imam al-Maturidi was a pioneer of Sunni orthodoxy, historians and even his own Hanafi school have given him far less attention than his Ash'ari counterpart. We will examine the evidence presented by the author to understand this neglect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the passage once and identify the author's main argument about the treatment of Imam al-Maturidi compared to al-Ash'ari.
Notice the author states there is a tendency to belittle al-Maturidi.
2
List the historians who neglected Maturidi
Go through the passage and note down the historians and biographers mentioned who failed to mention or write about al-Maturidi.
Ibn al-Nadim, Ibn Khallikan, Ibn al-'Imad, al-Safadi, Ibn Khaldun, al-Suyuti are mentioned.
3
Examine the role of his own followers
Consider the surprising fact that even Hanafi biographers and Imam al-Nasafi himself did not give due attention to al-Maturidi. Reflect on what this suggests about the bias.
The passage compares this with the Shafi'is' extensive coverage of al-Ash'ari.
