الأمصار هم الأشاعرة أصحاب أبي الحسن علي بن اسماعيل بن سالم بن سالم بن اسماعيل بن عبد الله بن بلال أبي برده بن أبي موسى الأشعري صاحب رسول الله وفي ديار ما وراء النهر الماتريدية أصحاب أبي منصور الماتريدي عليه السلام . نصر العياضي تلميذ أبي بكر الجوزجاني صاحب أبي سليمان الجوزجاني تلميذ أبي تلميذ محمد بن الحسن الشيباني من أصحاب الإمام أبي حنيفة ١٤ ويقول الزبيدي : إذا أطلق أهل السنة والجماعة فالمراد بهم الأشاعرة والماتريدية ٢٠ أن هذه النصوص التي قدمناها توضح أن الأشعري والماتريدي هما علما أهل السنة والجماعة فإنه وجد دائماً ميل للتقليل من شأن الماتريدي وتقديم الأشعري على أنه علم الإسلام المدافع عن العقيدة ضد المبتدعة المنحرفين عن أن الماتريدي كان أسبق من الأشعري إلى السنة ومذاهب السلف". هذا مع نصرة مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة ، كما نشأ على السنة ومات عليها ، بينما نشأ الأشعري على الاعتزال وظل معتزلياً إلى سن الأربعين . بالرغم من ويبدو هذا الميل نحو التقليل من شأن الماتريدي في إهمال كثير من المؤرخين له، محاضر يذكره ابن النديم (م) ۱۳۷۹ هـ / ۹۸۷ م) الذي توفي بعده وأصحاب التراجم فلم بأقل من خمسين عاماً ، بينما يذكر الإمام الطحاوي (م) الطحاوي (م ۳۲۱ هـ / ۹۳۳ م) الماتريدي وشيخ الأحناف وإمام أهل السنة في مصر كما يذكر الأشعري" . ولم يترجم له ابن خلكان ولا ابن العماد ولا الصفدي ولا صاحب فوات الوفيات . بل إن ابن خلدون لم يذكره في مقدمته في الفصل الذي كتبه عن علم الكلام كما أهمله جلال الدين السيوطي فلم يذكره في طبقات المفسرين بالرغم من الماتريدي علم من أعلام التفسير ، يشهد بذلك تفسيره الكبير المسمى تأويلات القرآن أو تأويلات أهل السنة ومن الغريب أن يشارك أصحابه أنفسهم - بدون قصد منهم – في إزكاء هذا الميل . فالأحناف في طبقاتهم وتراجمهم مروا على صاحبهم سريعاً حتى لا يكاد يظفر الباحث في هذه المصادر إلا بشذرات قصيرة عن حياة الماتريدي . ولو قارنا ما كتبه الشافعية في طبقاتهم عن الأشعري" بهذه الشذرات القصيرة لأدركنا الفور مدى عناية الشافعية بإمامهم ومقدار تقصير الأحناف في حق شيخهم . بل إن الأمر لم يقتصر على أصحاب الطبقات وأنما تعداه إلى من نصروا مذهب الماتريدي وعقيدته ، فالإمام النسفي لا يذكر الماتريدي في كتابه على العقائد النسفية .
The regions are the Ash'aris, the followers of Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Isma'il ibn Salim ibn Salim ibn Isma'il ibn Abdullah ibn Bilal Abi Burda ibn Abi Musa al-Ash'ari, the Companion of the Messenger of God, and in the lands beyond the river (Transoxiana) the Maturidis, the followers of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, peace be upon him. Nasr al-Ayyadhi, the student of Abu Bakr al-Juzjani, the master of Abu Sulayman al-Juzjani, the student of Abu... the student of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani from the companions of Imam Abu Hanifa. And al-Zabidi says: 'When Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is mentioned, what is meant by them are the Ash'aris and the Maturidis.' That these texts which we have presented clarify that al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi are the two scholars of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, for there has always been a tendency to belittle the status of al-Maturidi and to elevate al-Ash'ari as the scholar of Islam, the defender of creed against heretical innovators, despite the fact that al-Maturidi was earlier to the Sunna and the methods of the predecessors. This is along with his support of the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, as he was raised upon the Sunna and died upon it, while al-Ash'ari was raised upon Mu'tazilism and remained a Mu'tazili until the age of forty. Despite this, this tendency to belittle the status of al-Maturidi appears in the neglect of many historians for him. Ibn al-Nadim (d. 379 AH / 987 AD), who died less than fifty years after him, and the authors of biographical works do not mention him, while they mention Imam al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH / 933 AD) and al-Maturidi, the shaykh of the Hanafis and the imam of Ahl al-Sunna in Egypt, as they mention al-Ash'ari. And Ibn Khallikan did not write a biography for him, nor did Ibn al-'Imad, nor al-Safadi, nor the author of Fawat al-Wafayat. Rather, Ibn Khaldun did not mention him in his Muqaddima in the chapter he wrote on the science of kalam, and Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti neglected him, not mentioning him in his Tabaqat al-Mufassirin, despite al-Maturidi being a prominent figure in tafsir, as testified by his great tafsir called Ta'wilat al-Qur'an or Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunna. And it is strange that his own followers themselves—without intending to—contributed to fostering this tendency. For the Hanafis in their tabaqat and biographical works passed over their companion quickly, so that the researcher can scarcely find in these sources anything but short fragments about the life of al-Maturidi. And if we compare what the Shafi'is wrote in their tabaqat about al-Ash'ari with these short fragments, we would immediately realize the extent of the Shafi'is' care for their imam and the extent of the Hanafis' negligence regarding their shaykh. Rather, the matter was not limited to the authors of tabaqat, but extended to those who supported the school and creed of al-Maturidi, for Imam al-Nasafi does not mention al-Maturidi in his book al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a historical and critical discussion of the relative neglect of Imam al-Maturidi compared to Imam al-Ash'ari. It begins by identifying the two main theological schools of Ahl al-Sunna: the Ash'aris in the western regions and the Maturidis in Transoxiana. The author then quotes al-Zabidi to affirm that when 'Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a' is used, it refers to both Ash'aris and Maturidis. The core argument is that despite al-Maturidi being earlier in adherence to the Sunna and dying upon it—whereas al-Ash'ari was a Mu'tazili until age forty—there has been a persistent tendency to downplay al-Maturidi and elevate al-Ash'ari. The author provides evidence of this neglect: many historians such as Ibn al-Nadim, Ibn Khallikan, Ibn al-'Imad, al-Safadi, and the author of Fawat al-Wafayat failed to write biographies of al-Maturidi. Even Ibn Khaldun and al-Suyuti omitted him, despite his major tafsir. Astonishingly, even his own followers, the Hanafis, gave him scant attention in their biographical works, while the Shafi'is extensively covered al-Ash'ari. The passage culminates with the criticism that Imam al-Nasafi, a major Maturidi theologian, does not even mention al-Maturidi in his famous creedal work al-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya. The author uses these examples to highlight what he sees as an unjust historical bias.

Describes the neglect of Maturidi by scholars and his own followers.

Maturidi's own followers neglected him more than outsiders did.

This passage highlights a curious historical phenomenon: despite being a foundational figure in Islamic theology and exegesis, Imam Maturidi received surprisingly little attention from later scholars, including his own Hanafi school. The author compares this with the extensive coverage given to Ash'ari by Shafi'is, revealing a disparity that shaped the reception of Maturidi's thought.

Why Was Maturidi Neglected?
Author asks and answers why Maturidi was neglected.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the primary reason for the historical neglect of Imam al-Maturidi compared to Imam al-Ash'ari.

Core Idea
Geography, not theology, explains Maturidi's lesser fame.

This short passage addresses a natural question: if both Maturidi and Ash'ari are Sunni imams, why is Ash'ari more widely studied? The author gives a straightforward answer based on location. As you read, notice how the author frames the question and then offers a single, clear explanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Let the author's reasoning unfold without interruption.
The passage is short but contains a complete argument: question → answer.
2
Identify the reason given
Locate the exact reason the author provides for the neglect. Pay attention to the phrase 'ليس هناك من سبب لذلك إلا أن...'.
3
Contrast the two regions
Notice the contrast between 'ما وراء النهر' (Transoxiana) and 'العراق' (Iraq). Reflect on why Iraq was considered the center of the Islamic world at that time.
This geographical contrast is the heart of the explanation.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider what this explanation implies about the spread of theological schools. Does it suggest that the content of the school determined its reach? Or were external factors more decisive?
The passage challenges any assumption that neglect implies inferiority.

بقي علينا الآن أن نسأل عن سبب مثل هذا الميل نحو التقليل من الماتريدي وتقديم الأشعري عليه . يبدو لنا أنه ليس هناك من سبب لذلك إلا أن الماتريدي عاش في بلاد ما وراء النهر بعيدا عن العراق مركز العالم الإسلامي في ذلك الوقت حيث نشأ الأشعري وذاع مذهبه
It remains for us now to ask about the reason for such a tendency to belittle Maturidi and prefer Ash'ari over him. It seems to us that there is no reason for that except that Maturidi lived in Transoxiana, far from Iraq, the center of the Islamic world at that time, where Ash'ari arose and his school spread.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This short passage is the author's explanation for the neglect of Maturidi. After noting the tendency to elevate Ash'ari over Maturidi, the author states that the sole reason is geographical: Maturidi lived in the remote region of Transoxiana, while Ash'ari was in Iraq, the intellectual and political heart of the Islamic world. This distance meant that Maturidi's school did not receive the same attention.

Key Terms
ما وراء النهر
العراق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The neglect of Maturidi is due to his theology being inferior or less orthodox than Ash'ari's.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the sole reason is geographical remoteness, not theological shortcomings.

Checkpoint
What reason does the author give for the neglect of Maturidi?
A) His school was heretical.
B) He lived far from Iraq, the center of the Islamic world.
C) He wrote fewer works than Ash'ari.
D) He died before his teachings could spread.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's historical neglect is explained by geography, not by any deficiency in his theological school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'transoxianas' — distant truths, neglected scholars, or overlooked teachings — have you allowed to remain on the periphery of your faith journey because they are not familiar or convenient? Will you commit to seeking one such truth this week, regardless of distance?
?
If the spread of truth can be hindered by mere geography, what does the ease with which you access only mainstream Islamic teachings say about your willingness to pursue knowledge where it is less popular? When was the last time you deliberately learned from a source outside your comfort zone?

Why Al-Maturidi is Less Famous than Al-Ash'ari
Asks why Maturidi is less valued than Ash'ari and gives a geographical reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the geographical reason why Imam al-Maturidi is often less emphasized than Imam al-Ash'ari in Sunni theology.

Core Idea
Geography, not theology, explains Maturidi's lesser fame.

This lesson examines a historical puzzle: why is al-Maturidi, the great Imam of the Maturidi school, often less valued than al-Ash'ari? The passage suggests a simple but powerful reason rooted in geography. As we read, consider how location and historical context can shape the spread of ideas.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic text and its English translation. Notice how the author frames the question as something that 'remains for us to ask'.
2
Identify the cause
The passage gives one clear reason for the disparity. What is it? Look at the phrase 'except that...'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does the author think this reason is sufficient? Consider how far Transoxiana was from Iraq and what that meant for the spread of a school.
4
Connect to a possible misconception
Some might think Maturidi's theology is inferior. How does this passage counter that assumption?
The passage implies the theology itself is not the cause.

بقي علينا الآن أن نسأل عن سبب مثل هذا الميل نحو التقليل من الماتريدي وتقديم الأشعري عليه . يبدو لنا أنه ليس هناك من سبب لذلك إلا أن الماتريدي عاش في بلاد ما وراء النهر بعيدا عن العراق مركز العالم الإسلامي في ذلك الوقت حيث نشأ الأشعري وذاع مذهبه.

It seems to us that there is no reason for that except that al-Maturidi lived in the land of Transoxiana, far from Iraq, the center of the Islamic world at that time, where al-Ash'ari arose and his school spread.

Commentary
This passage asks a historical question about why Maturidi is often underestimated compared to Ash'ari. The author provides a single cause: geography. Maturidi lived in Transoxiana (Ma wara al-nahr), far from the Iraqi heartland where Ash'ari worked and his school spread. The implication is that the disparity is due to historical and geographical circumstances, not doctrinal deficiency.

Key Terms

الأشعري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Maturidi's theology is inferior to Ash'ari's.
Correction: The passage attributes the difference in fame to geographical reasons, not theological merit.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason for the tendency to underestimate al-Maturidi and prefer al-Ash'ari?
A) al-Maturidi's theology is weaker
B) al-Ash'ari had more students
C) al-Maturidi lived far from Iraq, the center of the Islamic world
D) al-Ash'ari wrote more books

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi's lesser fame compared to al-Ash'ari is due to his geographical remoteness from the Islamic center, not the quality of his theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever assume that scholars or teachers who are less famous are less knowledgeable? How does this lesson challenge that hidden bias in your own heart? What concrete step can you take to value scholars from less prominent regions or backgrounds?
?
Have you ever felt overlooked because of where you come from or your circumstances? How does al-Maturidi's story (being overshadowed due to geography) speak to your experience of not receiving the recognition you deserve? What does this teach you about seeking Allah's pleasure over human acclaim?
?
In your pursuit of Islamic knowledge, do you gravitate toward well-known figures and popular institutions? What might you be missing by ignoring scholars on the periphery? Will you commit to seeking out a lesser-known teacher or text this week, trusting that truth is not limited by geography?

Maturidi's Originality in Epistemology
The author notes Maturidi's pioneering role in epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Maturidi pioneered the inclusion of a formal theory of knowledge as an introduction in theological works.

Core Idea
Maturidi set the sunna of starting kalam books with epistemology.

In this passage, the author highlights a unique contribution of Imam al-Maturidi to the field of theology: he was the first to systematically present a theory of knowledge at the beginning of his works. This practice became a standard for later theologians, shaping the structure of kalam literature. Let's explore the significance of this innovation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the contrast between 'before' and 'after' al-Maturidi.
The passage is a single sentence; pay attention to the flow.
2
Identify the claim
What does the author claim about the state of theological works before and after al-Maturidi?
The claim is that no earlier theologian presented a theory of knowledge, while later ones almost always did.
3
Understand 'sunna' in this context
The word 'sunna' here means an established practice or precedent. How does the author use it to describe Maturidi's influence?
It refers to the normative practice of beginning works with epistemology.
4
Reflect on significance
Why was this innovation important for the development of kalam? Consider how it changed the structure of theological writing.
This made epistemology a foundational topic in systematic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن لا نجد قبل الماتريدي متكلماً يعرض نظرية في المعرفة، كما أننا لا نكاد نجد بعده متكلماً تخلو مؤلفاته من مقدمة في المعرفة، فكأنه قد استن العلماء الكلام سنة ساروا عليها من بعده في تقديم مؤلفاتهم بالكلام في المعرفة ومناقشة قيمة معارفنا.
And we do not find before al-Maturidi any theologian (mutakallim) who presents a theory of knowledge, just as we hardly find after him any theologian whose works lack an introduction on knowledge, as if he established for the theologians a sunna that they followed after him in prefacing their works with discourse on knowledge and discussing the value of our cognitions.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage is an observation on Maturidi's originality. The author claims that before Maturidi, no theologian presented a theory of knowledge (nazariyya fi al-ma'rifa) as a distinct topic, and after him, almost every theologian's work includes an introduction on knowledge. Maturidi effectively established a sunna (normative practice) that later theologians followed: beginning their works with a discussion of knowledge and the value of cognitions. This highlights Maturidi's influence on the structure of later kalam works.

Key Terms
نظرية في المعرفة
السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Maturidi invented the entire field of epistemology.
Correction: The passage does not claim he invented epistemology, only that he was the first to formally introduce it as a standard opening topic in theological works.

Checkpoint
What did Maturidi establish according to this passage?
A) A new school of thought
B) A sunna for theologians to begin works with a discussion of knowledge
C) The first theory of sense perception
D) The necessity of reflection

Key Takeaway
Maturidi established the precedent of beginning theological works with a theory of knowledge, influencing later generations of kalam scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely studied theology starting with epistemological foundations—did you ever pause to think that this structure was pioneered by one person? How does that affect your gratitude towards scholars who shaped the path before you?
?
Maturidi's 'sunna' of introducing knowledge discussions was taken up by later scholars. What 'sunna' (positive practice) are you leaving behind in your own learning or teaching? Are you consciously building a legacy of benefit?
?
Before Maturidi, no theologian had formally presented a theory of knowledge. Are there areas in your own understanding that you take for granted without knowing their origin? Will you commit to investigating the roots of your own knowledge structure?

Life of Imam al-Maturidi
beginner
4 min
Maturidi's Pioneering Theory of Knowledge
Commentator notes Maturidi's unique contribution to kalam epistemology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Maturidi's pioneering role in introducing a systematic theory of knowledge into kalam theology and how this became a standard tradition.

Core Idea
Maturidi made epistemology the foundation of kalam.

This passage from a classical commentary highlights a turning point in kalam literature. The commentator notes that before Imam al-Maturidi, no theologian had explicitly presented a theory of knowledge. After him, it became standard to begin theological works with an epistemological introduction. Let's explore the significance of this shift.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the contrast between 'before' and 'after' Maturidi.
2
Identify the key claim
The commentator claims that Maturidi was the first to present a theory of knowledge. Find the exact phrase that expresses this.
3
Reflect on the tradition
The passage says Maturidi established a 'sunnah' (tradition) for later scholars. Think about what this means for the development of kalam.
This tradition involved prefacing works with a discussion on knowledge.
4
Consider the impact
Why was it important to start with a theory of knowledge? How does it affect the way theology is done?
It shows that epistemology became foundational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونحن لا نجد قبل الماتريدي متكلماً يعرض نظرية في المعرفة ، كما أننا لا نكاد نجد بعده متكلماً تخلو مؤلفاته من مقدمة في المعرفة ، فكأنه قد استن العلماء الكلام سنة ساروا عليها من بعده في تقديم مؤلفاتهم بالكلام في المعرفة ومناقشة قيمة معارفنا .
We do not find before al-Maturidi a mutakallim who presents a theory of knowledge, just as we hardly find after him a mutakallim whose works are devoid of an introduction on knowledge. It is as if he established for the scholars of kalam a tradition that they followed after him in prefacing their works with discussion on knowledge and examining the value of our cognitions.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage highlights al-Maturidi's unique contribution: he was the first to include a systematic theory of knowledge (nazariyyat al-ma'rifa) in his work. The commentator asserts that before Maturidi, no mutakallim had done this, and after him it became standard practice for kalam scholars to begin their works with an epistemological introduction. Maturidi effectively established a normative tradition for the field.

Key Terms
الماتريدي
نظرية المعرفة
المتكلم
مقدمة في المعرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what did al-Maturidi establish that became a tradition?
A) A proof for the existence of God
B) A theory of knowledge as an introduction to kalam
C) A refutation of the Mu'tazila
D) A classification of divine attributes

Key Takeaway
Al-Maturidi pioneered the inclusion of theory of knowledge as a standard introduction in kalam works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn new things about your faith, do you ever pause to examine the foundation on which that knowledge rests, or do you simply accept it? What would it take for you to build your beliefs on a solid epistemological basis like al-Maturidi did?
?
Al-Maturidi established a tradition that benefited generations after him. What small but intentional practice in your study of Islam could become a legacy that helps others after you? Are you willing to commit to it starting today?
?
If someone asked you to explain the basis of your knowledge about Allah—not just what you know, but how you know it—what would you say? Does your confidence in that knowledge lead you to action, or is it just mental assent?
